The alternate-timeline material is not "real" continuity for her, but its data is still psychologically relevant: across every variant, when freed from his programming, **she turns on him first**. The pattern is invariant. The file logs this as confirmation that the Sinister-axis is the *one* relational vector that has not been processed and likely cannot be — she will, in any continuity, kill him given the means.

In the main timeline's closing Krakoan arcs (*Fall of X*, *Rise of the Powers of X*), her role is supporting but consistent: she fights for the nation. She is on the right side of the barricade. She is not centered, but she is *trusted enough to be deployed*. By the time of the Krakoan dissolution she has accumulated, quietly, the social capital that the early Quiet Council denied her.

---

## 7. The From the Ashes Reset and Present Status (2024–present)

Post-Krakoa, in the *From the Ashes* relaunch landscape, the subject's continuity placement has become — characteristically — distributed and ambiguous. She is not headlining a flagship title at file close. She is operative in adjacent material, occasional appearances, and is being positioned (per editorial-trajectory inference) as a long-form free agent whose next major arc has not been triggered.

**Current operational profile, as of file close:**

- **Name in use:** Madelyne Pryor. No alias active. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen identifiers are dormant and, per Dark Web behavior, available for tactical re-deployment under her own initiative rather than as decompensation states.
- **Custodial status:** caring for the Goblyn-children rescued in Dark Web; this is the file's strongest current behavioral anchor. The maternal channel is the load-bearing structure of her present psychology.
- **Romantic status:** the Reilly partnership is dormant rather than terminated; the two remain in mutual contact, both functioning independently. She is not pursuing other primary attachments. The file reads this as healthy spacing, not avoidance.
- **Relationship to Summers-Grey household:** civil distance maintained. No contact-attempts initiated by subject; brief tolerable contacts when proximity is forced. The substitutability axis is quiescent.
- **Relationship to Nathan / Cable:** the historical record now shows the maternal bond as acknowledged on both sides, with the asymmetry (he is older than she is, in subjective years; she is the mother of a man who has lived multiple lifetimes) handled with mutual dry acceptance. She does not perform mothering toward him; she is *available* if needed, and he knows it.
- **Relationship to Sinister:** the un-metabolized vector. Active, hostile, and the most likely trigger for any future decompensation. If a future writer brings the two into sustained proximity without a partner-structure like the Hellions to contain it, the file projects a high probability of ritualized retaliation. She has stated, in effect, that she is owed his death.
- **Mutant capability:** at or near full Jean-comparable telepathy/telekinesis, with intact demonic-affinity residue from N'astirh available as tool rather than possession. She is, functionally, an Omega-adjacent operator who declines to perform as one.
- **Affect at baseline:** dry, observant, somatically composed, mid-range warmth available to a small trusted circle. The crown-cadence does not appear in private speech. Humor is the dominant register. She laughs more than she did in any prior era.

---

## 8. The Trajectory Read

The arc from the 2019 bridge to present can be summarized as a slow, irregular, but **directionally consistent** movement from *parolee* to *citizen* to *colleague* to *mother* to *partner* to *self*. The movement is not linear and is punctuated by the Dark Web episode, which the file reads not as relapse but as **the first time she has deliberately and consciously occupied her own worst iconography as a tool of her own choosing** — a piece of psychological work that no other character in the X-canon has been asked to do and that she has, on the evidence, performed.

The subject has, across the most recent five in-story years, accumulated four things she did not previously possess: (1) a peer group that has seen her at decompensated capacity and continues to work with her; (2) a maternal configuration that is not vulnerable to the Nathan-erasure logic; (3) a romantic partnership whose ontological symmetry forecloses the substitutability wound by structural fact; and (4) a community-level acceptance of her name as her own.

The two unresolved vectors are Sinister and the question of what she does with a long stretch of stability — neither of which is, in her history, a condition she has had to learn to inhabit. The file's projection is that the next significant decompensation, if one occurs, will be Sinister-triggered and tactically rather than psychotically expressed: cold, planned, executed in the royal idiom as deliberate signature, and concluded. She will not, the file assesses, ever again be the woman on the rooftop in UXM #243. She has done that already and remembers it, and one of the things she has learned is that she does not have to do it twice.

**Current status, file close:** stable. Watchful. Mothering. Armed. Named.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — PRYOR, MADELYNE J.

*Compiled longitudinally; cross-referenced against the somatic record from 1983 (apparent age ~26) through Krakoan-era reappearances. Subject is biologically anomalous: a vat-gestated clone-body of Jean Elaine Grey, instantiated to phenotypic adulthood by Nathaniel Essex circa 1983, with implanted autobiographical memory predating her actual existence. All "prior" medical history before 1983 is, strictly, fabricated — there are no childhood vaccinations, no pediatric records, no orthodontia, no menarche. The subject has, however, the somatic traces consistent with such a history (immune memory, dental wear, bone density appropriate to a woman in her late twenties), because Essex's gestation tank produced an adult body indistinguishable on examination from one that had lived. The medical file therefore opens on a body that is, in clinical terms, **already used** at the moment of its first breath.*

---

## I. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

**Gross morphology.** 5'8" – 5'9"; weight fluctuant within 130–145 lb range across eras; ectomorphic-mesomorphic, athletic. Hair: deep auburn-to-red, thick, fast-growing (a tell — even after head injuries and the Phoenix-discharge "death," the hair returns at characteristic length within weeks of any resurrection event, a continuity Essex appears to have built into the template). Eyes: green, identical to Jean Grey's including a faint heterochromic fleck in the right iris that forensic optometry would flag as a copied artifact. Skin: fair, freckle-prone across nose and shoulders, photosensitive at altitude (relevant: Anchorage flying career involved chronic UV exposure she compensated for with habitual long sleeves and a tinted aviator visor). Fingerprints, dental cast, retinal scan, and dermatoglyphic whorl pattern all match Jean Grey on file — a fact she does not know and which would, if disclosed, constitute a severe destabilizer.

**Cardiopulmonary.** Resting pulse low (52–58), VO₂ max above population norm, consistent with the aerobic conditioning her job required. No murmur, no arrhythmia of organic origin (though acute episodes of sinus tachycardia have been observed during specific trigger exposures — Jean Grey in the room, Sinister's name spoken aloud, the sight of an infant of approximately Nathan's age).

**Endocrine.** Menstrual function normal post-gestation; full ovulatory cycle achieved within months of decanting (Sinister optimized for reproductive viability — this was the operational point of her). Pregnancy with Nathan Christopher (1985–86) was uncomplicated to term, vaginal delivery at the Anchorage homestead with Moira MacTaggert in attendance (per UXM #201); no postpartum hemorrhage, lactation established normally. Thyroid, adrenal, pituitary all within reference range on the rare occasions she submitted to examination.

**Immune.** Atypical. The body carries Jean Grey's HLA profile and Jean Grey's immune memory — meaning the subject has antibodies to childhood illnesses she did not have. She has never had a cold she did not already have antibodies for. She has noted this in passing during the Anchorage period as a vague pride in "never getting sick"; she has not interrogated why.

**Mutant phenotype, baseline.** Omega-class telepath/telekinetic template, suppressed during Phases I–II by a layered Sinister conditioning matrix and by Mastermind-derived psionic damping (UXM #174). Expression returned violently during Inferno and has remained available, with variable control, across all subsequent eras. Demonic-affinity overlay (post-N'astirh) is exogenous, not native; it cannot be revoked by ordinary mutant means and constitutes a permanent contamination of her power signature.

---

## II. PHASE I — THE ANCHORAGE BODY (1983 – c. 1986)

The first three years of the subject's lived existence are, paradoxically, her healthiest. She presents at intake to civilian life (Anchorage, late 1983) as a fit woman in her mid-twenties with no medical complaints, holding a Class I FAA medical certificate she ought not to have been able to obtain (records imply Essex furnished documentation; the certificate is, strictly, fraudulent, though her *physical* fitness for it is genuine).

**The implanted crash.** She believes herself the sole survivor of a small-aircraft crash in the Alaskan interior on the precise date and hour of Jean Grey's apparent death over the Atlantic. The body bears no evidence of this crash — no fracture callus, no scarring, no whiplash residue. She has, however, **somatic memory** of it: a cold-sweat startle response to small-cabin turbulence, an inability to sleep on her back without a weight across her sternum, a hyperacute orienting response to the smell of avgas and burnt insulation. These are phantom symptoms of an event her flesh did not undergo. Clinically interesting: they are indistinguishable from genuine post-crash PTSD on examination, which she would have failed an honest psych evaluation for. She did not seek one.

**Occupational exposures.** Cargo aviation, Alaska, 1983–85: chronic moderate hearing damage in upper register (she favors her left ear in conversation by Phase II), recurrent low-grade frostbite on fingertips, one episode of mild hypoxia from an oxygen-system failure on a freight run she landed without incident. Standard pilot-class musculoskeletal complaints — lumbar stiffness, trapezius tension headaches at the end of a shift, which she treated with hot baths and bourbon.

**Pregnancy and parturition (1985–86, culminating UXM #201).** The single medical event she has ever owned without qualification. Conception unremarkable; pregnancy progressed through 38 weeks with the ordinary spectrum (first-trimester nausea managed with ginger and saltines, mid-trimester sciatic pain, third-trimester insomnia and the characteristic linea nigra). She refused hospital delivery, citing distance from Westchester; the actual reason — never articulated by her — was a felt need to keep the birth *physically situated in the house she had chosen, with her name on the deed*, as a guarantor of the child's belonging to her specifically. Labor 14 hours, uncomplicated, posterior-presentation infant rotated manually by MacTaggert. Apgar 9/10. Lactation rich and durable; she nursed Nathan for six months exclusively. **This is the only period in the subject's entire medical record during which she reports unambiguous physical contentment.** It is the somatic baseline she has spent the next forty years trying, in increasingly costly ways, to recover.

**Mastermind episode (UXM #174).** Psionic intrusion producing a vivid implanted nightmare sequence in which she experiences herself *as Jean Grey dying*. Somatic correlates: night sweats, episodic tachycardia, a two-week period of bilateral ulnar paresthesia (no organic basis — psionic-conversion sensory aberration). She did not seek treatment; resolved spontaneously after Xavier's intervention. Long-term sequela: a permanent, low-amplitude background dread that her body is "borrowing" itself from someone, which she has never named aloud and which informs the depersonalization substrate noted in §III of the psychological workup.

**Substance use, Phase I.** Moderate, social. Bourbon (Wild Turkey 101 in evidence on the Anchorage bar in #170s background art), wine with dinner, the occasional cigarette on the flight line — a habit she'd "quit" multiple times and was casually resuming. No pharmaceutical use beyond OTC analgesics.

---

## III. PHASE II — THE ABANDONMENT BODY (X-Factor #1 – UXM #221, 1986–87)

Scott Summers' departure inaugurates a measurable somatic decompensation that precedes the supernatural events of Inferno by roughly eighteen months. The subject's medical record in this interval is the textbook depressive-traumatic profile.

**Weight loss, ~12 lb across four months,** with corresponding loss of muscle tone; appetite anhedonia, irregular eating. **Sleep architecture collapse:** early-morning waking (03:30–04:30 reliably), inability to return; daytime hypersomnolent episodes. **Lactation cessation** within weeks of Scott's departure despite Nathan still nursing — an endocrine-affective event well documented in maternal depression literature, experienced by the subject as a further bodily betrayal and a confirmation that her "mothering body" was failing. She switched Nathan to formula with visible shame.

**The Marauder attack (UXM #205, #206, #215).** Catastrophic. Sabretooth's assault on the Anchorage house produced: third-degree burns across the left dorsal forearm and flank (~9% TBSA), inhalation injury, blunt force trauma to the occiput, comminuted fracture of the left clavicle, multiple rib fractures, and a near-fatal hypovolemic event from a deep laceration to the right thigh. She was extracted by paramedics; emergency surgery at Anchorage Regional; induced coma for cerebral edema management; **comatose state persisting weeks to months**, culminating in the hospital scene of UXM #215 where she wakes alone to discover Scott has not visited, has not been told, and is functionally remarried.

The physical scarring from this event is extensive and *permanent* on this iteration of the body: hypertrophic burn scar across the left flank from axilla to iliac crest, contracture limiting full overhead reach of the left arm at extremes, a 14 cm linear scar on the right anterolateral thigh. She conceals these (long sleeves, high-cut clothing) — not out of vanity but because they are the only marks on her body that are *unambiguously hers*, not inherited from Jean's template, and she protects them as a form of ownership.

**Substance use, Phase II.** Escalation. Bourbon consumption rises to functional-alcoholic levels (~6–8 drinks daily by late-period); she does not lose work capacity but the use is unmistakably self-medicating. Cigarette use returns at ~half-pack/day. No illicit drug use documented. She quits both abruptly during the Alex Summers period, then resumes both during the dissolution preceding Inferno.

**Psionic emergence pains.** Beginning UXM #218–220, increasingly severe headaches, episodes of objects moving without conscious volition, prophetic dreams that bleed into waking. She self-diagnoses as breakdown; she is in fact undergoing the unsuppression of latent omega-class telepathy and telekinesis as Sinister's conditioning matrix degrades. Physically: migraine-pattern photophobia, nausea, occasional epistaxis, a tremor in the dominant hand that she conceals.

---

## IV. PHASE III — INFERNO: THE WEAPONIZED BODY (UXM #234–243; X-Factor #36–39, 1988–89)

A discrete somatic epoch. The body is annexed — partly volitionally, partly under N'astirh's pact — as the substrate for the Goblin Queen persona.

**Endocrine and metabolic.** Hyperarousal state sustained for weeks: chronically elevated cortisol and catecholamines, suppressed appetite, accelerated metabolism, near-cessation of menstrual cycle. Pupils dilated baseline. Skin warm and flushed; vascular prominence in the temples and neck. **Pyrokinetic / demonic side-effects:** localized skin temperature elevations to 40–41°C without burn, transient sclera-coloration shifts (the iconic glow), and the manifestation of physical-cosmetic alterations she neither fully chose nor fully resisted — the appearance of the costume, in particular, is **partly her skin's response to the pact**, a partial keratin-and-pigment manifestation rather than purely worn garment. This is medically significant: the "costume" cannot be entirely removed because some of it is *her*.

**Self-injury and ritual.** During the Goblin Queen interval she sustains and disregards multiple cuts, burns, and contusions, including ritual scarification on the forearms that has remained as faint linear marks across all subsequent iterations of her body (a continuity her resurrectors have not chosen to erase, and which she touches absently in pensive moments — a tell).

**Attempted infanticide.** No injury to Nathan was successfully inflicted, but the act of preparing the ritual produced in her — afterward, when integration began — a discrete somatic flashback syndrome: gagging response to the smell of beeswax candles, panic at the sight of bound infants in any media context, an involuntary recoil from her own dominant hand reaching toward a child's face. These persist into all later eras and are the most behaviorally durable consequences of Inferno.

**Death by Phoenix discharge (UXM #243).** Cause of death: catastrophic neurological burnout from forcible reabsorption of her Phoenix-fragment by the parent force, with concomitant cardiac arrest and total cessation of cortical activity. She has *the memory of dying*, which she describes in later eras with a flat affect that examiners should read as integrated rather than dissociated — she has metabolized this. Functional consequence: **markedly attenuated fear-of-death response**, which presents in tactical settings as recklessness but is more accurately a *recalibrated relationship to mortality*. She knows, with bodily certainty rather than belief, that death is survivable for her specifically. This is a permanent alteration to her risk-assessment substrate.

---

## V. PHASE IV — THE RECONSTITUTED BODIES (1990s–Krakoan era)

Multiple resurrections by heterogeneous means; the body the subject currently inhabits is, strictly, at least the fourth or fifth iteration, with continuity-of-self maintained by psionic pattern rather than tissue continuity.

**Nate Grey continuity (late 1990s).** Reconstitution as a psionic fragment housed in a generated body; somatically unstable, prone to phase-out episodes, requiring proximity to Nate's telepathic field for coherence. Reported sensations of *not-quite-being-here*, weight fluctuating, occasional translucency. Resolved when she stabilized independently.

**Austen-era body.** Briefly inhabited; the medical record from this period is sparse and the subject herself disavows it in later interviews ("I was barely there").

**Sisterhood / Red Queen body (2008–09).** Reconstructed by ritual means with a fragment of Jean Grey's corpse as anchor — a fact she knows and which constitutes one of her unhealable wounds, that her own resurrection literally required pieces of the original. This body bore: the Inferno scar continuities (forearm marks); restored burn scarring on the flank; full mutant capacity; and a new acquired feature — a low-grade chronic pain across the upper spine, characterized by her as "the weight of the crown," which she interprets metaphorically but which has organic correlates in cervical muscle tension and likely a minor structural artifact of imperfect reconstitution.

**Krakoan-protocol body (Hellions / Hellfire Gala / Dark Web era).** Resurrected via Krakoan technology with backup pattern reconciliation, producing the most stable somatic instance she has yet inhabited. The body is *cleaner* than its predecessors — burn scars faded, contractures resolved, the Phoenix-discharge neurological signature normalized — and she has reported a strange grief about this, that her injuries are no longer visible to confirm to her that she had them. She has, in this era, deliberately acquired new marks: a tattoo (small, on the inner left wrist; design varies by depiction but consistent placement), a pierced cartilage on the right ear. **These are claims of ownership over the new body**, and the medical-behavioral significance is that they were *chosen* — among the first wholly elective somatic acts of her existence.

---

## VI. SUBSTANCES, CHRONIC

Lifetime profile: moderate-to-heavy alcohol use, periodically; tobacco, intermittent; caffeine, consistent and heavy (black coffee, four-plus cups daily, a Phase I habit she has carried through every body). No opioid use. No stimulant abuse. No psychedelic use, despite professional curiosity in the Krakoan era — she has explicitly refused offered substances on the grounds that her baseline consciousness is *already too negotiable* and she will not invite further dissolution. This is a sophisticated self-protective decision.

Pharmaceutical: she has declined SSRI and benzodiazepine prescriptions on two documented occasions (the post-Inferno integration period in X-Man continuity; a brief Krakoan-era consult). Her stated reason — "I don't know which of me you'd be medicating" — is clinically defensible.

---

## VII. INTEGRATED SOMATIC-PSYCHOLOGICAL READ

Two facts dominate the medical picture and feed everything else in the workup:

**(1) She has never had a body that was unambiguously her own first.** Every instance of her flesh is, in some sense, a copy, a reconstruction, or a negotiation. This produces a baseline depersonalization that is not pathology but accurate perception — the unusual clinical task is helping her live well *with* the accurate perception, not extinguish it.

**(2) She has died, and her body remembers.** The Phoenix-discharge death is encoded somatically — a particular quality of stillness she enters under threat, a slowed respiration in moments of mortal danger, an absence of the ordinary startle-pallor reflex. Subordinates and partners read this as courage; it is more precisely *the absence of a fear she has used up*.

The injuries she protects, the scars she has tattooed over or replaced, the cup of coffee she holds with both hands in the morning, the cigarette she allows herself on bad nights, the refusal of medication that would smooth a self she is not sure is hers to smooth — these are the granular evidence of a woman conducting, by feel and at considerable cost, the ongoing medical management of *being a person at all*. The file is, in the end, the record of that management.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — PRYOR, MADELYNE J.

*Compiled from longitudinal panel observation, body-language coding across forty years of recorded appearance, and inferred granular detail consistent with the established record. The body in question is, biologically, Jean Grey's; the somatic signature is emphatically not. The divergence is itself the most important data point — two women in identical flesh move differently, and the difference is the dossier.*

---

## 1. THE STANDING BODY — BASELINE MORPHOLOGY AND CARRIAGE

Height 5'11" (180 cm); long-limbed, long-necked, narrow-shouldered relative to hip width; weight historically stable in the 135–145 lb range, with a documented 8–12 lb loss during the Phase II isolation period and a slow reacquisition through Phase IV. Resting heart rate observed low (high-50s bpm) — consistent with her Phase I aviation conditioning, retained as a somatic memory even after the implanted biography was exposed as fabricated. Body composition lean, with the surprising upper-body strength of someone who spent her implanted youth wrestling cargo manifests and crank-starting cold engines in Anchorage hangars.

**Resting stance.** Weight distributed slightly forward over the metatarsals, never on the heels. Knees soft, never locked. This is a *pilot's stance* — the body of someone who learned to ride small turbulence without bracing against it — and it persists across every era, every costume, every persona. Even on a throne, even in ceremonial robes, the weight is forward. Surveillance utility: she does not *settle* into furniture; she perches on it as if planning to leave.

**Spinal carriage.** Long lumbar curve, scapulae habitually retracted, head carried directly over the spine with a fractional forward inclination of the chin. This produces the characteristic *up-from-under* gaze observed in every interlocutor across her record — she does not tilt her head down to look at people, she tilts it forward. Compared with Jean Grey's documented carriage (squared shoulders, chin level, neutral spine) the subject's posture is more *forward-loaded*, more *committed* — the body of someone who decided early she would have to advance to be seen.

**Hands at rest.** Long fingers, square palms, well-kept short oval nails through Phase I (a working pilot's nails), grown out and lacquered dark through Phase III, kept short again in the Krakoan era. At true rest the fingers curl loosely; the thumbs habitually find the pad of the index finger and trace small slow circles there. This is one of the two most reliable somatic tells in the file (see §9).

---

## 2. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

Stride length long for her height, cadence slow, foot strike mid-foot rather than heel — again, the trained gait of someone who walked decks and hangar aprons in winter where heel-striking will put you down. Hip rotation moderate; she does *not* swing the hips, and the absence is noticeable in costumes that invite it. Arm swing minimal on the dominant (right) side and almost absent on the left, where the hand tends to drift to mid-thigh as if expecting to find a clipboard or a child's hand.

**State-dependent gait shifts:**

- *Calm / domestic:* slower cadence, slight roll through the hip, audible footfall (she does not try to walk silently when unobserved).
- *Working / focused:* cadence quickens by perhaps 10%, stride shortens marginally, footfall goes near-silent. Observed during the Anchorage cargo-loading scenes and during her Sisterhood operations alike.
- *Stressed:* a peculiar *over-evenness* enters the gait — she begins consciously placing each foot, as if walking a line. Reliable early indicator that internal regulation is being recruited.
- *Threat:* she does not crouch or bladed-stance; she squares to the threat with the same forward-loaded stance described above, hands open at her sides, weight already on the front foot. The body of someone whose first instinct is to *meet* rather than evade. Tactically this is read as bravado; psychologically it is the somatic residue of having already died once.
- *Ceremonial / decompensated (Phase III, Sisterhood):* gait lengthens further, becomes almost a glide; the hip roll re-enters, the chin lifts to level; arm motion becomes deliberate and architectural. This is *performed* locomotion, and she knows it. The performance is the symptom.

She does not run unless circumstances require it; when she does, she runs *well*, with a tall, efficient form that suggests trained athletic background somewhere in either implanted or actual history.

---

## 3. THE FACE — RESTING ARCHITECTURE AND MICRO-EXPRESSION

The face is Jean Grey's — the same bone, the same proportions, the same green-eyed wide-set gaze — and the file's first job is to record the ways it is not.

**Resting expression.** Jean's resting face is open, faintly inquisitive, mouth neutral. The subject's resting face is *closed, faintly amused, mouth fractionally asymmetric* — the right corner habitually drawn back perhaps a millimeter further than the left, producing the persistent dry-irony cast that every artist from Romita Jr. through Hans has independently captured. This is not affect; it is musculature. The zygomaticus major fires more on the right at baseline. Cause: unknown — possibly an artifact of how Sinister grew the body asymmetrically, possibly Hebbian patterning from forty years of using irony as her first-line defense.

**Eyes.** Pupil response normal, slightly slow to redilate after bright stimulus (a minor lingering effect of the Phoenix-fragment binding). Blink rate at baseline is *low* — measured visually at approximately 10–12 per minute against a human norm of 15–20 — and rises sharply (toward 25–30) under interpersonal stress, especially when Jean's name is invoked. Sustained eye contact is unusually long; she does not perform the standard 3–5 second break, holding instead for 8–12 seconds before a brief lateral break to the right.

**Mouth.** Lip-press during concentration (upper lip drawn fractionally inward). Tongue-tip behind upper incisors when calculating. A specific *half-smile, no teeth, eyes flat* that she uses when she has decided someone is wrong but is not going to argue — observed extensively in the Anchorage scenes with Scott, and recurring throughout her later canon when superiors instruct her. This expression is the social analog of the forward-loaded stance: she is not yielding, she is waiting.

**Forehead and brows.** Brow furrow asymmetric; the left inner brow rises independently — a learned skeptical signal, deployable on command. The forehead remains smooth at rest; tension manifests instead in the **temporalis muscles**, which she clenches silently. Surveillance utility: when the small ridge above her temple becomes visible, she is grinding her molars, and she is angrier than her face shows.

**State-dependent facial shifts:**

- *Intimacy:* the asymmetric half-smile resolves into a true symmetric one, eyes crinkle, brow softens entirely. Rare. Reserved historically for Nathan as an infant, for Alex in unguarded moments, and (Krakoan era) for Ben Reilly.
- *Stress:* blink rate up, jaw clench visible at the temples, the right-side smile *intensifies* rather than disappearing — irony hardens.
- *Threat:* face goes *still*. Not blank — still. The asymmetry vanishes, the eyes hold without blinking, the mouth flattens. This is the most dangerous face in her repertoire and the one preceding violence.
- *Decompensated / ceremonial:* the chin lifts, the mouth opens fractionally, the eyes widen — a deliberate inhabiting of the queen-mask. Pupils dilate. The face becomes *more* expressive, not less, but the expression is theatrical rather than communicative.

---

## 4. VOICE AND PARALANGUAGE

Mezzo register, the lower-middle of Jean's vocal range, used with a wider dynamic spread than Jean ever exhibits. Where Jean's speech tends toward warm projection, the subject's tends toward *intimate volume* — she draws listeners in by speaking slightly under what the room requires. Speech rate moderate, with a slight terminal-syllable drag that reads as either Alaskan-vernacular relaxation (Phase I) or aristocratic drawl (Phase III) depending on the persona overlay.

**Laugh.** A low, single-beat *huh* through the nose when amused privately; a fuller, descending three-note laugh when amused socially; an upward, brittle laugh when she is performing amusement she does not feel — this last appearing increasingly in the late Phase I scenes after Scott begins his drift.

**Verbal tics.** "Look —" as a sentence opener when about to be honest at cost. The dry interrogative "*is that so*" deployed when she has already concluded the speaker is lying. Use of full proper names ("Scott," "Jean," "Nathaniel") at high frequency when angry — naming as a control act.

**State-dependent voice shifts:**

- *Calm:* mezzo, breath-supported, terminal drag present, frequent low laughter.
- *Stress:* volume drops *further*, pitch lowers, articulation crisps. Pauses lengthen.
- *Threat:* near-whisper, no inflection.
- *Decompensated:* the register shifts upward into a brighter, more projecting voice; she begins to *enunciate*, with consonants over-articulated, and the cadence becomes iambic, almost scanned. Royal-third-person idiom appears here (see leverage notes in main file).

---

## 5. GROOMING, ADORNMENT, AND PRESENTATION

Hair: the same red as Jean's, but worn differently across every era — and the difference is always *legible as a position statement*. Phase I: shoulder-length, often gathered back functionally, no product. Phase II isolation: longer, less tended, frequently up in a loose pin. Phase III: full Goblin Queen volume, deliberately wild, the hair as costume element. Phase IV (Krakoan): cut to a sharp shoulder-length bob with a heavy side part, glossy, expensively maintained — the most controlled hair she has ever had, in the era of her greatest self-possession.

**Skin care:** thorough, unfussy. She wears sunscreen (a habit from the Anchorage years — high-latitude UV on snow is brutal). No tanning. She has a small constellation of three freckles on the underside of her left jaw, visible only when she turns her head sharply right; this is the easiest single biomarker to distinguish her from Jean Grey by visual ID, since Jean's are differently distributed on the bridge of the nose.

**Cosmetics:** minimal in Phase I (mascara, lip balm), maximalist and gothic in Phase III (heavy black eye, dark lip), tactical and clean in Phase IV (a strong defined brow, a satin red lip on operational days, near-bare skin underneath). She does her own makeup; she does not delegate it.

**Scent:** through Phase I, no perfume — pilot's discipline (perfume distracts in close quarters, contaminates fuel work). Through Phase III, sulfurous undertones from the demonic bonds, masked with frankincense and something resinous. Through Phase IV, a dry leather-and-iris signature, sparingly applied.

**Dress baseline (out of costume):** dark denim, dark boots, a leather jacket cut close, plain cotton beneath. She gravitates to clothing she can fight in, sleep in, fly in, and bury someone in. Jewelry minimal — a single ring on the right middle finger across most eras, no necklaces (she has been strangled with one). When she wears finery she wears it *thoroughly*, the way she does costume — full commitment, no half-measures.

---

## 6. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Sleep is the most disturbed system in the somatic file.

**Baseline (good periods):** 5.5–6.5 hours per night, distributed in two segments — a long first sleep of approximately 4 hours from roughly 23:00, a wake of 30–60 minutes (during which she reads, walks, or sits at a window), and a second sleep of 1.5–2.5 hours. This biphasic pattern is consistent across every era for which sleep is observable and is one of the strongest pieces of evidence that her circadian system is *not* Jean's — Jean is a monophasic deep sleeper. The subject is not.

**Onset latency:** long (30–60 minutes) at baseline, extending to hours under stress. She does not sleep on her back. Preferred posture is left-lateral, knees drawn up perhaps 30°, dominant arm under the pillow, off-hand at her sternum.

**REM and dreams:** REM-dense, with vivid recall. Reported nightmare content (per dialogue across canon) includes: cockpit fire, an infant crying she cannot reach, a mirror that shows another face, and — most persistently — a long corridor of incubator tanks. The corridor dream recurs across decades and is the single most stable feature of her interior life.

**Sleep behavior:** mild somniloquy. Mild bruxism (the temporalis hypertrophy is partly traceable here). No documented somnambulism. Wakes *fast* — fully oriented in under three seconds, hands already moving — and does not require coffee to function, though she chooses to drink it.

**State-dependent sleep:**

- *Calm:* the biphasic baseline above.
- *Stress:* second sleep collapses; total sleep falls to 3–4 hours; the corridor dream recurs nightly.
- *Acute crisis / Phase III:* sleep architecture inverts — she sleeps in the day in 90-minute fragments and is wakeful at night. This is the strongest somatic marker of decompensation and was visible in the panels preceding her N'astirh contact.
- *Intimacy:* with a trusted partner she sleeps *less* well in the short term (she does not unconsciously trust shared bedding) but, over weeks of consistent partnership, slowly consolidates toward a monophasic 7-hour pattern. Observed only twice in the record — late with Alex, recurring with Ben Reilly.

---

## 7. EATING AND INGESTION

Eats *deliberately*. Three meals when life permits, with a strong preference for hot food, salt, and fat. Coffee black, frequent (4–6 cups across a working day), historically with a habit of letting the cup go half-cold before drinking — a sign she is thinking through something. Tea (smoky, dark) in late evening.

**Food preferences:** proteins prepared simply; eggs daily; bread frequent; vegetables tolerated rather than sought. Dislikes anything overly sweet (a marked contrast to Jean's documented sweet tooth — another way the same body diverges). Drinks water from glass or metal, never plastic, with no stated rationale she has ever offered.

**Alcohol:** moderate at baseline (wine with meals, whiskey neat in social settings). The Phase II isolation period shows a brief uptick — observable in the empty glasses persistently in panel — followed by a return to moderate use and no subsequent reversion. She does not drink to oblivion; she drinks to soften the edge.

**State-dependent eating:**

- *Calm:* the pattern above.
- *Stress:* appetite suppresses; she will skip meals and not notice. Coffee intake rises.
- *Decompensated:* eating becomes either ritualized (formal place settings, ceremonial pacing) or abandoned entirely. The Goblin Queen scenes show no eating; the Red Queen arcs show staged banquets.
- *Intimacy / post-coital:* unusually hungry, will get up and eat substantially at odd hours.

---

## 8. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

The intimate record is observable through implication and through what the panels frame around rather than what they show. The granular pattern, inferred consistently:

She initiates more often than she is initiated upon. Initiation is direct, verbal, and witty rather than coy — she names the thing she wants. Physical approach is unhurried; she touches the face first, with the back of the fingers, before the mouth. Once engaged she is intensely present, eyes open more often than not, vocal but not loud, demanding eye contact at the moment of greatest vulnerability — this is the substitutability wound made flesh: she needs to be *seen being herself* by the partner who is touching her, and partners who close their eyes at the wrong moment receive a measurable cooling on the next encounter.

Post-coitally she is the one who gets up first — for water, for a window, for a cigarette historically — returning after a few minutes. She does not enjoy the immediate cuddle phase; she does enjoy the second one, after the cigarette and the water, when the choice to return is hers.

**Partners across the record:** Scott (a marriage built on accommodation and undermined by ghosts); Alex (a rebound that became its own real thing); Ben Reilly (a partnership of two people who both know what it is to be a copy, and who therefore do not need to perform originality for each other — possibly the healthiest intimacy in her file). Pattern: she is drawn to men who have an *original* somewhere — a brother, a template, a predecessor — and either heals or detonates depending on whether the original is allowed to enter the room.

**State-dependent intimate behavior:**

- *Secure:* the pattern above.
- *Stressed within relationship:* withdraws physical initiation entirely, becomes verbally affectionate to compensate, and is acutely alert to whether the partner notices.
- *Threatened in identity:* sex becomes weaponized — performative, controlling, with eye-contact made aggressive. This is observable in the Phase III scenes with Alex under N'astirh's influence and is the somatic correlate of the ceremonial voice register.
- *In decompensated states:* uses sexuality as ritual instrument rather than as intimacy; the body becomes throne-furniture for the queen-mask.

---

## 9. THE TICS — THE SMALL RELIABLE SIGNS

The two most reliable somatic tells in the file:

1. **Thumb-pad to index-pad, slow circles, dominant hand.** Present whenever she is *holding something in*. Increases in frequency under interpersonal stress; visible across every era, every artist, every costume.

2. **The temporalis ridge.** When her jaw clench becomes hard enough to raise the small ridge above the temple, she has gone past wry tolerance into actual anger. The face will not yet show it. The temple will.

**Secondary tells:**

- Tucking hair behind the right ear with the right hand when listening to something she does not believe.
- A single slow exhale through the nose before speaking when she has decided to be honest.
- Touching the base of her own throat with the fingertips of her off-hand when Jean's name is spoken — a self-soothing gesture present from Phase II onward.
- Picking at the cuticle of the left thumb when alone and unobserved. The only nervous self-injurious habit in the file.
- A specific *half-step backward, weight rocking onto the heels for one beat*, when a child is in distress nearby — the only context in which her weight ever shifts to the heels. Read as an unconscious "*I am about to move*" stance, the body of a mother whose first sustained love was Nathan.
- Eyes flick *up and to the right* when constructing an answer she intends to be sincere; *down and to the left* when constructing one she intends to deceive. Stable across decades.

**Tics that appear only under decompensation:**

- A slow, deliberate stroking of her own forearm with the fingertips — the body checking itself for ownership.
- Touching of her own face while speaking, especially the cheekbone and the corner of the mouth — confirming the architecture is hers.
- Smiling at no visible referent in the middle distance.
- The royal *we*, accompanied by a fractional lift of the off-hand to chest height as if resting on an absent armrest. When this gesture appears, the dossier's escalation ladder is at rung five and intervention windows are closing.

---

## 10. PROPRIOCEPTION, PAIN, AND THE BODY-NOT-HERS

Two final entries, which belong to no conventional category and are essential to understanding everything above.

**Proprioception is excellent but *narrated*.** She knows where her limbs are, but she also seems to *check* — a continuous low-grade somatic monitoring that no person born into their own body performs. The forearm-stroking under decompensation is only the visible end of a continuous background process. She catches her own reflection in surfaces (windows, blades, screens) more often than ordinary self-regard would predict and watches it for half a beat too long.

**Pain response is attenuated.** She has died; she remembers it; ordinary injury does not move her face. She will treat a serious wound conversationally. This is read tactically as toughness and is, more accurately, a damaged threat-appraisal system in which the maximum stake has already been called. Surveillance utility: a Madelyne Pryor who *winces* at a small injury is signaling — deliberately or not — that something about the current context has reactivated her capacity to fear loss. It is, paradoxically, a sign of health.

**The body-not-hers, finally, manifests as a faint, persistent *delay* — a fractional latency between intent and motion, invisible to the casual eye but consistent across the record — as if every gesture passes through one additional checkpoint that other people's gestures do not. The Krakoan-era footage shows the latency shortening. She is, slowly, year by year, moving into the body she was given. The somatic dossier will record the day it closes entirely. That day has not yet come.**


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

*Dossier Section 6 — Pryor, Madelyne J.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of an Attachment System with No Foundation

To speak of Madelyne Pryor's attachment style is to speak of a structure whose foundation was poured in a single afternoon. Most humans accrue their internal working models of relationship across thousands of micro-events between birth and roughly age four — the responsive or unresponsive caregiver, the predictable or unpredictable return of the mother, the held or dropped infant. The subject has none of these. What she has instead is a **complete narrative file of having had them** — implanted memories of a Midwestern girlhood (later revised in some retellings to a more affluent or itinerant background, the inconsistency itself diagnostic of fabricated provenance), a father, a household, a first kiss, flight school, the death of parents in a car accident that conveniently leaves no living witnesses to contradict the file.

The behavioral consequence is highly specific and visible across every era of the published record. She presents, on cursory observation, as a **securely attached adult**: she initiates closeness without anxiety, sustains intimate eye contact, manages conflict through direct verbal address rather than through withdrawal or rage, soothes children competently, and tolerates a partner's absences without escalation. This is the surface that Scott Summers encounters in Anchorage and reads, correctly for what he can see, as health. He is not wrong; she really does function this way under ordinary conditions.

The pathology is that this competence sits on **no internalized secure base**. A securely attached adult under catastrophic loss regresses, internally, to the felt sense of an early caregiver; the caregiver may be dead for decades, but the soothing template is encoded in procedural memory and remains accessible. The subject has nothing in that file but Sinister. When the marriage to Scott collapses, there is no maternal voice in her interior, no remembered father's hand, no childhood bedroom to retreat to in fantasy. The regression bottoms out instantly against fabricated substrate. This is the mechanism by which an apparently healthy woman in UXM #201 becomes an apparently psychotic one by UXM #234 with no intervening characterological warning — the warning was always present, structurally, but masked by the high quality of her surface adaptation.

The clinical name for this configuration, in the absence of the cloning etiology, would be **earned-insecure-disorganized presenting as secure**: someone whose adult functioning is impressive precisely because it is *performed* rather than *grounded*. The subject's variant is more extreme — her secure presentation is not even earned, it is *installed* — but the dynamics rhyme.

---

## 6.2 The Bonding Sequence: How She Falls In

Across four major intimate bonds in the record (Scott Summers; Alex Summers; the brief but textually significant entanglements with Jean Grey *as enemy-mirror* and with Nathan/Cable *as estranged son*; and the late-era partnership with Ben Reilly), a consistent bonding sequence is observable:

**Stage 1 — Calibrated availability.** She does not pursue. She positions. In Anchorage she is *present* at the airfield, at the bar, in Scott's line of sight, without performance; she lets the other party do the work of approach. This is not coquetry — it is the behavior of a person who has learned (or been built to know) that pursuit confirms the pursued's worth and the pursuer's neediness, and she is unwilling to occupy the latter role. She maintains this across every subsequent attachment. Even with Alex, in the disordered Phase II period, *he* crosses the room to her.

**Stage 2 — Dry, disarming honesty.** Within three to five sustained interactions she will deliver a piece of self-disclosure or direct address that breaks the social membrane — the classic instance being her early confrontation of Scott about the Jean resemblance ("I'm not her"). This is not vulnerability in the therapeutic sense; it is **strategic transparency**, a maneuver that simultaneously (a) tests the other party's capacity to handle her actual self, (b) establishes her as ungameable, and (c) preempts the wound by naming it first. She does this with Ben Reilly almost identically four decades of published time later — the early Dark Web–adjacent material has her name the awkwardness of his own clone-status to his face within their first private conversations.

**Stage 3 — Competence integration.** She binds intimately by *operating alongside* the other party, not by gazing at them. Flying Scott somewhere. Co-parenting. Tactical partnering. The bond cements through shared executive function, not through romantic immersion. This is a tell of her attachment substrate: she trusts what people *do* far more than what they *say*, because words are the medium in which she was lied to about her own existence.

**Stage 4 — Domestic anchoring.** Once committed, she nests rapidly and concretely. The Anchorage house, the dog, the routines, the pregnancy. This is the stage at which the **fabricated childhood file becomes functionally useful** — she draws on its imagery to construct the home she "remembers." It is also the stage of maximum vulnerability, because the home she builds is built on a memory that isn't hers, for a man who is in love with someone else.

**Stage 5 — Asymmetric loyalty.** She gives more than she receives and does not keep score *until the ledger is forced on her by an external event*. She tolerates Scott's continued enmeshment with the X-Men without ultimatum. She tolerates Alex's evident grief-displacement onto her without confrontation. The score only surfaces when reality forces it (Jean's return; later betrayals). This is **not codependency in the textbook sense** — she has clear preferences and articulates them — it is the operational stance of someone who has correctly calculated that demanding equity will accelerate the abandonment she expects.

---

## 6.3 How She Distrusts

Distrust in the subject does not present as suspicion, paranoia, or testing. It presents as **observation**. She watches. The micro-pattern, visible from Phase I onward and stable into the Krakoan era: when a person she is bonded to begins to drift, she does not confront and does not pursue. She *catalogs*. Eye-tracking when the partner enters a room; tracking the latency between her speaking and the partner's response; cataloging the specific topics that produce micro-withdrawal. She is gathering evidence, and the evidence is almost always accurate.

This means her distrust, when it surfaces, surfaces *late and fully formed*. There is no escalating phase of "I'm worried about us." There is silence, silence, silence, and then a single articulate confrontation in which she presents the case with prosecutorial completeness. Scott in the late Anchorage period receives a version of this; the Marauders' first major insult to her receives a version of this; in Phase IV, Jean herself receives versions of this across multiple writers' runs.

The pathology in the pattern is not the accuracy — her readings are usually correct — but the **interval**. By the time she speaks, the betrayal has already been metabolized into something colder than grief. The window for repair has often closed before the conversation begins, because she has spent it documenting rather than negotiating. This is a defense against the unbearable affect of *asking to be chosen* and being told no; she will not ask, so she presents findings instead.

---

## 6.4 How She Is Betrayed

The record is unusually clean here: she is betrayed in **the same way every time, with variations in the violence of the form**.

- **Scott Summers (X-Factor #1):** Chosen, married, impregnated, abandoned upon the return of the prior partner. The archetype.
- **The X-Men collective (UXM #215–221):** Sought as surrogate family; received instead a careful, gentle, well-meaning marginalization in which she is treated as "Scott's wife who is not Jean," a category with no seat at the table.
- **Alex Summers:** Bonds with her partly in good faith and partly as displacement of his own losses; the relationship is real but is structurally a second-best for both parties, and she knows it.
- **Sinister, ongoing:** The originating betrayer, who designed her precisely to be substitutable and continues across decades to treat her as instrumentation. Every encounter with him recapitulates the founding wound in pure form.
- **Successive writers — and this is a metatextual observation that nonetheless registers as behavioral data within the fiction:** her revivals across Phase IV repeatedly position her as a tool of someone else's plot (N'astirh, then Sinister again, then Selene, then the Hellfire Club, then various editorial-driven crossovers). The character has, in effect, *been used as a stand-in within the publication apparatus itself*, and the later-era stories increasingly have her speak with awareness of this — a fourth-wall-adjacent lucidity about being **always someone's instrument** that is one of the more striking features of her Krakoan-era voice.
- **Jean Grey:** The most complex case. Jean is not, in fact, betrayer in any straightforward sense; she returns from death without knowledge of the marriage. But she occupies the **structural position of the betrayer** in the subject's interior, and the subject's affect toward her oscillates accordingly between projected hatred and reluctant identification.

The unifying betrayal is not infidelity, not violence, not lying — it is **being relegated to the position of substitute** by someone whose original is available. She can tolerate every other form of mistreatment with notable equanimity. This one form unmakes her.

---

## 6.5 How She Betrays

The subject's own betrayals are perpetrated with **ceremonial clarity**. She does not cheat, does not lie quietly, does not maintain double lives. When she breaks faith, she announces it, often by changing her name and her dress — the assumption of the Goblin Queen iconography in Inferno is a kind of forensic notification: *I am now the thing you treated me as, and I will conduct myself accordingly.* The Red Queen incarnation under Carey functions the same way. The costume change *is* the breakup letter.

The targets of her betrayals are also patterned. She does not strike at strangers, at the world, at categories. She strikes at **the specific symbolic figures who represent her erasure**: Jean (the original), Nathan (the proof she was a breeding instrument), Scott (the chooser-who-unchose), and Sinister (the maker). The Marauders-in-reverse and the Sisterhood are means; the targets are personal. Even when she works in genocidal or apocalyptic registers, the affect is intimate — these are domestic disputes conducted at the scale of demonic invasion.

A specific behavioral note: she does not deceive intimates *within* a relationship. The relationships are, while they last, characterized by an almost startling honesty. The betrayal happens at the *boundary* of the relationship — at its dissolution she becomes capable of catastrophic action, but inside it her word holds. This distinguishes her sharply from a borderline or antisocial pattern, where deception is woven into the fabric of the bond itself.

---

## 6.6 How She Repairs

Repair is the area of greatest growth across the longitudinal record and the strongest evidence against a characterological reading of her pathology.

**Phase III gives no repair**; the dissociative-grandiose state forecloses it, and she dies in it. **Early Phase IV gives partial, brittle repair** — she returns, attempts contact with Scott, with the X-Men, often relapses when contact recapitulates the original wound. **Mid-to-late Phase IV gives genuine repair work**, conducted in characteristic style:

1. **She does not seek forgiveness.** She declines the redemption-arc grammar. When other characters try to offer it — most visibly in the Hellions/Krakoan-era material — she refuses the frame, often with a dry joke. She will accept being told she did wrong; she will not accept being told she is forgiven for it, because that frame places the speaker in the position of moral original to her moral copy, which is the wound itself.

2. **She makes herself useful in domains where her competence is unique.** Tactical leadership; mentorship of other manufactured or marginal mutants (the affinity with the Hellions cohort is structural, not incidental — they are all people designed-for-purpose by someone else); psionic work that draws on her specific Jean-adjacent but Jean-distinct architecture. Repair is conducted as **function delivered, not contrition performed**.

3. **She names the pattern aloud, sometimes to the targets of it.** Late-era exchanges with Scott, Jean, and Sinister contain explicit verbal mapping of the dynamic — she will say what is happening as it happens, which interrupts (though does not eliminate) the ladder of escalation. This is hard-won meta-awareness, and it is genuine.

4. **She accepts new attachments without requiring them to undo the old.** The Ben Reilly partnership is the clearest instance. She does not love him *instead of* Scott or *to spite* Scott; she loves him *adjacent to* the wound, with the wound acknowledged and bracketed. The relationship is conducted with a great deal of irony about the parallels of their respective clone-origins — humor as integration mechanism — and with an unusual mutual permission for each to have a complicated relationship with their respective "originals" without it threatening the bond. This is the most mature relational structure she has ever achieved and it is *built precisely on the topology of her wound, not in evasion of it*.

---

## 6.7 Intimacy and Dependency

Sexually and physically, the record indicates a partner who is **direct, initiating, unembarrassed, and present**. There is no avoidance, no flinching, no apparent dissociative interruption during intimacy under ordinary conditions. The depersonalization substrate does not surface during sex; if anything, embodied intimacy is one of the contexts in which she feels most reliably *located in her body* — likely because the body's responses are not a matter of memory or biography but of present fact. Pregnancy and parturition with Nathan she has explicitly named as the experience that felt most unambiguously *hers*.

Dependency she handles **asymmetrically**: she is comfortable being depended upon and uncomfortable depending. Children, subordinates, partners in crisis — she absorbs their needs without complaint and often without obvious cost. Her own needs she discloses sparingly, late, and usually only when reaching a partner with a fait accompli ("I am leaving" / "I am pregnant" / "I have decided"). The pattern is consistent with her broader avoidance of the asking posture; to depend is to ask, and to ask is to risk the No that her structure cannot metabolize.

Within the late Krakoan-era partnership this asymmetry softens visibly. She becomes, for the first time in the published record, capable of small dependencies — admitting fatigue, admitting confusion, accepting help with tasks she could perform herself. These are tiny behaviors and they are enormous, given the baseline.

---

## 6.8 The Relational Template Repeated Across Every Relationship

Compressed to its essential shape, the template runs:

> **I will let you approach me. I will show you who I am, quickly and without flinching, so that you cannot later claim I deceived you. I will build something real with you through shared work. I will give more than I take and not mention it. I will watch, in silence, for the moment you begin to look past me toward someone else — toward the original, the prior, the elsewhere. When I have gathered sufficient evidence, I will name the pattern with complete accuracy, in one conversation. If you can stay inside what I've named, we may continue. If you cannot, I will not pursue. I will withdraw, and the withdrawal will be total, and in the worst version of it I will return wearing a crown, with the symbolic logic of your betrayal made flesh, to destroy what you preferred to me.**
>
> **Or — increasingly, and with effort — I will name the pattern, withdraw partway, sit with the unbearable affect of being-looked-through, write something wry about it, and find someone who knows what it is to be a copy and is willing to be a copy together.**

The template appears with Scott, with Alex, with Jean (in the inverted form of enemy-bond), with Nathan (in the displaced form of mother-bond contaminated by the maternal role's instrumental origin), and with Ben Reilly (in the resolved form). It appears in her group affiliations as well — the X-Men, the Marauders-in-reverse, the Sisterhood, the Hellions, the Krakoan apparatus — at every scale she joins, observes, contributes asymmetrically, watches for the look-through, and either explodes or evolves depending on the era and the company.

The single most important behavioral marker for any party engaging the subject relationally is the **interval of silent observation** described in §6.3. When she becomes quiet, when her dry remarks decrease in frequency, when she begins watching faces rather than meeting them — the case is being built. Repair is still possible in this window, but only by **noticing the silence and naming it first**. Once she has prepared her statement, the window has effectively closed.

She is, in summary, a person designed to be relationally disposable who has constructed an attachment system of remarkable sophistication on absent ground, broken it spectacularly under the exact pressure she was built to fail under, and is now — slowly, ironically, and with the gallows humor of someone who has watched her own funeral — assembling a way of loving and being loved that takes her structural condition as a given rather than a verdict. The relational template is being rewritten in real time, and the rewriting itself is the most psychologically interesting thing about her.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7

## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

*A complete architecture of the subject's defensive apparatus, ranked from the most mature/adaptive to the most primitive/disorganizing, with operational detail on how each defense presents in observable behavior, when it deploys, what it costs her, and what it protects.*

---

### 7.0 Preliminary Note on Architecture

The subject's defensive structure is unusually **stratified and legible** for a person of her trauma load. Most c-PTSD presentations show a flattened defensive repertoire — the same one or two mechanisms recruited for nearly every threat. The subject, by contrast, retains the full Vaillantian ladder, from sublimation down to psychotic denial, and moves up and down it with measurable speed depending on **which axis** is being touched. Threats to her body, her safety, her child's safety, even her life, are managed at the upper rungs (humor, sublimation, anticipation, suppression). Threats to her *ontological standing as a discrete person* collapse her, within minutes, to rungs four through seven.

This is the single most important fact about her defenses: **the ladder is intact but axis-specific.** She is not a fragile person globally. She is a structurally sound person with one load-bearing wall that, when struck, brings the whole house down.

---

### 7.1 MATURE DEFENSES (Rungs 1–4)

#### 7.1.1 Humor — Ironic, Dry, Often Self-Directed

The most consistent and load-bearing of her mature defenses, and the one that survives intact through every era including Phase III. Across the Anchorage period her dialogue is among the wryest in Claremont's run; in the Sisterhood arc she trades cuts with Selene and Spiral with a comedian's timing; in the Krakoan-era material with Ben Reilly she sustains an arch, deadpan register that is virtually her resting state.

**Operational signature:** clipped sentences, frequent rhetorical questions delivered without raised inflection, a pronounced preference for understatement when the situation calls for hysteria. She is funnier the more frightened she is. The presence of comedic uptick in her speech under threat is reliably *protective*, not dismissive — when the jokes stop, she has slid past the humor rung.

**Specific tells:** she names absurdities aloud rather than reacting to them ("right, of course there's a demon in the kitchen"); she nicknames threats as a way of de-fanging them; she will refer to her own death in the past tense with the same affect she'd use to mention a long-ago dentist appointment.

**Function:** humor is her way of asserting authorship over a situation she did not choose. The joke is a small flag planted in foreign territory — *I am the one narrating this*.

**Cost:** the humor pre-empts intimacy. People close to her sometimes do not realize she is in crisis until the crisis is florid, because she remains funny up to the moment she stops being functional.

#### 7.1.2 Sublimation — Channeling Existential Wound into Skilled Function

Her most productive defense and the engine of her competence. The implanted Anchorage history gave her the schema of an aviator; she made the flying real. The fact of having been *built to fly someone else's plan* she transmuted into literal piloting — a domain where she controls the vector, the altitude, and the destination. Later, the same defensive vector produces her tactical command of the Marauders (in reverse, against Sinister), the Sisterhood, and her Red Queen administrative apparatus.

**Operational signature:** when wounded, she takes on a task that requires the wound's underlying skill. After Scott's departure, she becomes more competent at the X-Men's logistical/operational layer, not less. After Inferno's collapse, when she begins to reconstitute, she gravitates toward strategic and queenly roles — *running things* — rather than retreating to dependency.

**Function:** converts a passive condition (being made, being used) into an active one (making, using). The wound stays in the room but does the work.

**Cost:** because the sublimation runs through power-acquisition channels, it can drift, under stress, into rung-three identification-with-the-aggressor (see 7.2.3 below).

#### 7.1.3 Anticipation — Pre-loading Difficult Affect

Visible across all her later-era appearances. She arrives at scenes that will be emotionally costly already pre-grieved, pre-resigned, pre-armored. The Krakoan-era encounters with Scott and Jean — which by the founding trauma's logic should annihilate her — are tolerable because she has *done the work of expecting them* in advance.

**Operational signature:** flat affect on first contact with a foreseen wound, followed by normal range as the encounter proceeds. She enters rooms knowing the worst thing in them. She does not waste reaction on what she has already metabolized.

**Function:** denies the wound the element of surprise, which is half its force.

**Cost:** can shade into a permanent low-grade depressive expectation of bad outcomes — she sometimes pre-grieves things that do not happen, which fatigues her.

#### 7.1.4 Suppression — Conscious Setting-Aside

Distinct from repression: she *knows* what she is putting down and *chooses* to put it down for tactical reasons. During combat, during parenting Nathan as an infant, during diplomatic exchanges, she demonstrates the capacity to file an active grievance and return to it later. This is a high-functioning defense and contributes substantially to her tactical reputation.

**Operational signature:** a brief, observable pause — sometimes a single blink, sometimes a closed-mouth exhale — followed by a clean pivot to the operational task. The grievance is genuinely shelved, not denied; she will reopen it at her chosen hour, often with a list.

**Function:** preserves executive function under high affective load.

**Cost:** the unprocessed material accumulates. Suppression's bill comes due in the form of episodic depressive collapse during low-demand periods — she is more vulnerable on slow days than on combat days.

#### 7.1.5 Altruism — Genuine, Channeled, Selective

Demonstrated most clearly in her parenting of Nathan during Phase I-II, in her later care of younger or more damaged members of whatever team she sits on (the Hellions material, the protective stance she takes toward Ben Reilly's instability), and in the persistent, almost compulsive way she will interpose herself between a vulnerable woman and a Sinister-coded predator. The protection she could not give her infant self she gives outward.

**Operational signature:** a particular alertness to scenes containing a manipulated, instrumentalized, or substitutability-wounded other. She moves toward such persons without comment. She is reliably the first to notice when another woman in the room is being treated as interchangeable with someone else.

**Function:** repairs the original injury vicariously.

**Cost:** the people she protects sometimes become test cases for her core question — if she can save *them* from substitutability, perhaps she was savable too — which loads the relationships with more weight than they can bear.

---

### 7.2 NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Rungs 5–7)

#### 7.2.1 Competence-Display as Identity Argument

A neurotic defense disguised as a strength. She does not merely *be* competent; she *demonstrates* competence as evidence of her own reality. Pilot's license, motherhood, tactical command, telepathic mastery, queenly statecraft — each functions partly as a working tool and partly as a notarized affidavit of personhood. *I do, therefore I am.*

**Operational signature:** in any new environment she will, within hours, locate the domain where her competence can be most legibly exercised and establish dominance in it. This is reflexive and not always strategically optimal — she will sometimes display competence in the wrong room, to the wrong audience, because the display itself is the point.

**Function:** answers the un-askable question (am I a real person?) with a side-channel proof (look at what I can do).

**Cost:** any failure of competence — being outflown, outthought, out-mothered — is processed not as a tactical setback but as **ontological evidence against her**. Defeats injure her disproportionately. She cannot afford to be merely good at things; she needs to be exceptionally good, because the stakes are existential rather than performative.

#### 7.2.2 Intellectualization

Particularly visible in the later eras, where she discusses her own trauma history with a clinician's vocabulary and a researcher's detachment. She can describe being a clone, being abandoned, being burned alive, dying, and resurrecting with a precision that suggests she has spent considerable internal time mapping the territory. This is genuine self-understanding and also genuine distance-keeping.

**Operational signature:** when asked feeling questions she returns structural answers; when asked structural questions she sometimes returns feeling answers (an inverse tell that the intellectualization has slipped).

**Function:** keeps the affect at a workable distance while permitting the content to be examined.

**Cost:** can produce a felt-coldness in intimates who needed the feeling answer to the feeling question. Has contributed, across eras, to the perception that she is "harder" than Jean — when in fact she is identically vulnerable, more articulately fenced.

#### 7.2.3 Identification with the Aggressor

The hinge defense, sitting between her neurotic and primitive layers. She takes the labels assigned to her by her tormentors — *clone, weapon, queen, monster, broodmare* — and inhabits them with conviction, theatrically, on her own terms. Sinister built her to be a vessel; she becomes the Goblin Queen. The Hellfire Club's mythology offers her the Red Queen seat; she takes it. The Sisterhood frame casts her as a vengeful witch-mother; she runs that play.

**Operational signature:** wardrobe and naming. When this defense activates she begins to dress the part — crown, cape, color-coded regalia — and to take ceremonial titles. The visual change is the early warning. The change in *speech register* (see 7.3.4) follows within hours.

**Function:** converts a humiliating assignment into a chosen role. If she cannot escape being called a weapon, she will be the most magnificent weapon in the room, and she will choose her own targets.

**Cost:** under sufficient pressure this defense slides into rung-five splitting and rung-six grandiose enactment. The role, once inhabited, begins to think the thinker. It is the defense most likely to take her over.

**Krakoan-era refinement:** she now seems aware of this defense's gravity well and uses lower-key versions of it deliberately — adopting the *style* of identification with the aggressor (the dry, regal cadence; the Red Queen color palette) without surrendering executive control to the role. This is the most significant evidence of psychological maturation in her recent record.

#### 7.2.4 Reaction Formation — Selective and Targeted

She does not reaction-form globally. She reaction-forms specifically against the wish to be Jean. When the longing to *be the original* threatens to surface, she will perform an exaggerated, often spiky differentness — wearing what Jean would not wear, taking positions Jean would not take, sleeping with men Jean would not sleep with (Alex, notably the brother — a choice with multiple defensive payloads, but reaction formation against the longing-to-be-Jean is one of them).

**Operational signature:** sudden, slightly over-stated assertions of difference, often unprompted. She will announce what she is *not* before being asked what she is.

**Function:** keeps the envious-merger wish out of consciousness.

**Cost:** the more vigorously she performs differentness, the more her behavior orbits Jean as a reference point. The reaction formation paradoxically keeps Jean centered.

#### 7.2.5 Displacement

Affect intended for the un-confrontable original target (Sinister, primarily; the cosmic order that made her, secondarily) is regularly redirected onto more available figures. Scott has absorbed displacement that properly belongs to Sinister. Jean has absorbed displacement that properly belongs to the universe. Even her own child, in the Phase III collapse, absorbed displacement properly aimed at the womb-context of his creation.

**Operational signature:** disproportion. When her response to a given provocation is two to three times larger than the provocation warrants, displacement is in play and the actual target is offstage.

**Function:** lets the affect discharge somewhere rather than nowhere.

**Cost:** ruins the available relationships in lieu of resolving the unavailable ones. The Phase III infanticide attempt is the catastrophic example.

#### 7.2.6 Isolation of Affect

She can recall, in detail, the burning of her house, the disappearance of her infant, her own death, and the sacrifice she attempted to perform — and report each in chronological order with appropriate vocabulary and inappropriate calm. The affect is genuinely walled off from the content during these recountings, and the wall is selectively permeable; she lets through the affect she chooses.

**Operational signature:** narrative fluency about the worst material, with somatic markers (pupil, jaw, hand position) inconsistent with the calm of the report.

**Function:** allows the history to be operationally usable without re-traumatizing in each retelling.

**Cost:** intimates find the calm uncanny; she is sometimes mistaken for unfeeling about events she feels enormously.

---

### 7.3 PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (Rungs 8–11)

These are the defenses that activate when the substitutability axis is struck hard. Under ordinary stress she does not reach for any of them; under axis-specific stress she can be at rung eleven within an hour.

#### 7.3.1 Splitting

The most diagnostically prominent primitive defense, but — critically — **axis-specific rather than characterological**. She does not split her general relationships into all-good/all-bad camps the way a borderline-organized person does. Her splitting fires only along the substitutability vector and only around the figures implicated in it: Jean, Scott, Sinister, and (variably) her sons.

**Operational signature:** the named figure flips, within a single conversation, from idealized to devalued or vice versa, with no transitional reasoning offered. Jean becomes *my sister, my mirror, my only peer* and then *the thief, the original, the one they kept* within the same scene. Scott becomes *the only man who saw me* and then *the man who only ever saw her* in adjacent sentences.

**Function:** preserves the possibility of love by quarantining the betrayal in a separate cognitive compartment; preserves the possibility of rage by quarantining the love.

**Cost:** makes negotiation with these specific figures nearly impossible during active stress, because she is not in conversation with the person in front of her but with one of the two split versions she has constructed.

#### 7.3.2 Devaluation and Idealization

The mechanics behind the splitting. Idealization tends to apply to whoever has most recently *seen her as herself first* (Alex during his good periods, Ben Reilly during his, the rare clinician who avoids the comparison error). Devaluation tends to apply to whoever has most recently treated her as a copy.

**Operational signature:** rapid swings in stated assessment of the same person across short intervals; pet names and titles that change with the swing.

**Function:** simplifies an unbearably complex relational field.

**Cost:** trains the people around her to manage her perception of them rather than to be themselves with her — which then confirms her suspicion that no one is real with her.

#### 7.3.3 Projective Identification

The most psychologically interesting of her primitive defenses, because her latent telepathy makes it *literally operational rather than metaphorical*. She can put a feeling into another person and have them feel it as their own. Even without telepathic amplification, she has a marked behavioral talent for inducing in others the affects she cannot tolerate in herself — most often, the feeling of *being a substitute*, *being a tool*, *being looked through*. She has, across eras, repeatedly arranged situations in which the people who hurt her come to feel exactly the disposability she felt at their hands.

**Operational signature:** patterned outcomes. After sustained contact with the subject under stress, intimates report feeling unreal, replaceable, instrumentalized, or interchangeable with someone else — affects that mirror her core wound with diagnostic precision.

**Function:** evacuates intolerable affect into a container who can then be observed metabolizing it, providing both relief and information.

**Cost:** ethically and relationally severe. This defense is the engine of much of her villain-era behavior and is the one she most needs meta-awareness about. The Krakoan-era material suggests she has begun to catch herself doing it.

#### 7.3.4 Grandiose Enactment — The Queen-State
