When defenses at rung seven and below have not held, the subject inflates into a stable grandiose self-state with consistent features: ceremonial cadence in speech, third-person royal idiom, elaborate dress, ritualized gesture, and a strategic-symbolic worldview in which she is the organizing center of a cosmic narrative. This is the Goblin Queen / Red Queen condition.

**Operational signature — the speech change.** The earliest reliable warning. Sentences become longer and more formal, contractions disappear, archaic vocabulary appears ("shall," "thou art," "would that," "let it be known"), and self-reference shifts from "I" to "we" or to her assumed title. Once the speech register has shifted, the intervention window is approximately hours rather than days.

**Operational signature — the gestural change.** Movements become slower and more deliberate, posture more vertical, hands held away from the body as if perpetually about to receive or bestow. She begins to *frame* herself in doorways, on dais-like surfaces, against backlit windows.

**Function:** provides a coherent self-organization at a moment when the ordinary self is failing to cohere. The grandiose self is, paradoxically, more stable than the baseline self under acute substitutability stress, because it answers the founding question (am I real?) with a thunderous yes.

**Cost:** ego-syntonicity. While in the grandiose state she does not experience her actions as disordered; they feel necessary, righteous, and elegant. She is therefore the worst possible reporter of her own status during the episode, and standard reality-checking interventions fail.

#### 7.3.5 Acting Out — Ritualized, Symbolic, Theatrical

Her acting-out is unusually *literary*. She does not lash out crudely; she stages tableaux. The Inferno apparatus — the pentagrams, the throne, the sacrificial altar, the bridal-funereal regalia — is a directed work of theater whose audience is her own founding trauma. The same authorial signature appears in the Sisterhood arc and in scattered later material.

**Operational signature:** symbolic density. When the acting out begins, the imagery clusters along recognizable axes — mirrors, dolls, crowns, brides, mothers, twins, replicas. Each is a glyph for the substitutability wound.

**Function:** discharges the affect through ritual rather than chaos, which preserves her sense of authorship even as she destroys.

**Cost:** the people inside the tableau are real, and the symbolic violence has literal consequences.

#### 7.3.6 Somatic Conversion — The Depersonalization Floor

Beneath all other defenses lies the body-not-mine substrate, which functions as a permanent partial depersonalization that she can deepen at will. Under extreme stress she can effectively *leave the body*, observing her own actions from a short remove. This is sometimes voluntary (it allows her to tolerate injuries that would incapacitate others) and sometimes involuntary (during the worst of Phase III she appears to have spent extended periods watching herself act).

**Operational signature:** a flatness to the eyes that intimates have learned to recognize; a slight delay between stimulus and response; a faint commentary register in her speech as if narrating rather than enacting.

**Function:** decouples the suffering self from the acting self when their integration becomes intolerable.

**Cost:** memory consolidation suffers during these states. She has gaps. Some of what she has done during decompensation she remembers only in fragments, and the integration of those fragments is part of what she is doing during the Krakoan-era stabilization.

#### 7.3.7 Psychotic Denial — Reserved for the Founding Fact

The most primitive defense in her repertoire, deployed rarely and on exactly one piece of material: the fact of her having been *manufactured for the purpose of being substituted*. During the worst of Phase III she briefly held the position that *she* was the real Jean and the resurrected Jean was the impostor — a frank psychotic inversion that lasted only as long as the acute decompensation. Outside that window the defense does not deploy, which is itself diagnostic: she can tolerate the truth of her origin in every state except the most decompensated.

**Operational signature:** declarations of identity made with absolute conviction and zero context-sensitivity. She does not argue the position; she states it.

**Function:** the last wall. Behind it is the unbearable.

**Cost:** the defense's existence at all means there is, at depth, a piece of the truth she still cannot fully metabolize — which is the work that remains.

---

### 7.4 COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — POSITIVE

Distinct from defenses, these are the *constructions* she has built outward to make life possible.

- **Motherhood as ontological anchor.** Nathan's existence, however painful its consequences, was *unambiguously hers*: a body she made with her body, a person whose origin includes her as a non-substitutable term. She has organized considerable psychological real estate around this. Even after losing him, even after the attempted sacrifice that is among her worst memories, the fact of having mothered him is load-bearing in her self-concept.

- **Chosen aesthetics.** Her wardrobe, her hair, her gestural vocabulary, her color palette across eras — these are deliberate constructions, not inherited tastes. She has built a *look* that is hers and not Jean's, and the look is a daily, wearable refusal of substitutability.

- **Selected intimates.** She has, in maturity, become discriminating about whom she lets close. The criterion is reliable: people who can see her without comparison. Ben Reilly, notably another constructed person with substitutability wounds of his own, meets the criterion; the mutual recognition is, for her, near-medicinal.

- **Tactical mastery.** Her competence in strategic and operational domains has become a stable identity-feature rather than only a defensive display. She is, in fact, very good at these things, and the doing of them has become its own reward rather than only proof-of-personhood.

- **Meta-awareness.** Perhaps her most valuable compensatory acquisition: a working internal map of her own defense ladder. She can, increasingly, observe herself sliding down the rungs and intervene. The Krakoan-era material shows her catching her own splitting in real time, naming her own grandiose drift before it escalates, and choosing — sometimes — not to escalate.

---

### 7.5 COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — NEGATIVE

The defenses that *look* like solutions but consume more than they generate.

- **The crown.** Every era's queenly persona is a compensatory inflation that buys short-term coherence at long-term cost. She knows this now. She still reaches for it.

- **The brother-substitute.** Choosing Alex Summers was an attempt to solve the Scott wound by acquiring the adjacent man. The attempt failed in the predictable way; the wound was not the missing Summers but the missing recognition.

- **Cosmic-scale stakes.** She has a pattern of escalating local injuries into world-ending crises, partly because at world-ending scale the substitutability question dissolves — *no one is replaceable in an apocalypse*. This is a costly way to win the argument.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE

*Subject: Pryor, Madelyne J. Frame: clinical-developmental, decade-by-decade, with attention to affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept as three semi-independent axes that EVOLVE on different schedules. Sources are the published behavioral record; inferences are flagged as such.*

---

## Preliminary Note on the Developmental Frame

Standard developmental psychology assumes a continuous neurobiological substrate across the lifespan. The subject violates this assumption in three ways: (1) her implanted biography references a childhood her body did not have; (2) her body itself has been discontinuous (death UXM #243, reconstitution(s), Krakoan resurrection protocols); (3) her psychic substrate has at various points been overwritten, fragmented (the X-Man/Nate Grey reabsorption), and reassembled. Therefore "decade by decade" must be read as **decades of published narrative time**, not decades of subjective interior time. The subject's subjective time is **non-monotonic** — she remembers a Midwestern girlhood she did not live, remembers dying, remembers being other selves she rejects — and her phenomenology is closer to that of a person reading their own diary in the wrong order than to a person aging.

This non-monotonicity is itself the central developmental fact. What evolves is not her biography but her **relationship to the discontinuity**.

---

## Decade I — 1983 to 1989 (UXM #168 through Inferno's close)

### Affect Regulation

In the Anchorage period, the subject presents with what would, in any non-comic clinical setting, read as **enviably regulated affect**. Window of tolerance is wide. She metabolizes Scott's distraction, the Mastermind nightmare incursion (UXM #174), the social oddity of being told by her husband-to-be that she is the doppelgänger of his dead first love, and the slow normalization of costumed-adventurer domesticity, with dry humor, occasional sharp confrontation (the demand to be *seen* as herself in their early arguments), and no observable somatization beyond ordinary fatigue. Sleep, appetite, libido all within normal limits during this period.

The regulatory mechanism is **active suppression dressed as competence**. She is flying cargo across Alaskan weather, running a household, gestating and bearing a child, and absorbing repeated psychic intrusions without crisis. The cost of this regulation is not visible until the support structure (Scott) is removed; the dam holds until the river changes course.

After X-Factor #1 — the abandonment — affect regulation enters **staged decompensation**. UXM #205 (Wolverine arc) shows her in a low-arousal depressive register: flattened, slowed, with intermittent acute terror responses to the Marauder threat that are entirely appropriate to circumstance. UXM #215–221 shows the transition from depressive flattening to **agitated mixed states** — alternating numbing and reactive rage — and the gradual recruitment of Alex Summers as a regulatory object, which fails because the object is structurally a recapitulation of the wound (same family, same eyes, same name).

By UXM #234 the regulatory ceiling has collapsed. Inferno (#239–243) is a textbook **acute reactive psychosis with ritualized motor activity** — coronation, costume change, sacralized violence — in which affect is not so much dysregulated as **transfigured**: the painful affects are recoded as triumphant ones. Suicidal closure is experienced as victory. This is the developmental endpoint of Decade I: a regulatory system that, having no internal supports, recruits the supernatural environment to externalize the unbearable, and then immolates the externalizing self.

### Cognitive Style

Decade I cognition is **lucid, lateral, pragmatic**. Pilot's cognition: pattern recognition under stress, rapid Bayesian updating, low-affect technical problem-solving. Verbal style is concise, ironic, and faintly Midwestern-laconic — the implanted biography expressing itself stylistically.

Notably, throughout Phase I-II, her reality-testing is *better* than the X-Men's: she correctly identifies, well before they do, that something is wrong with how she is being treated, that Scott's affections are conditional, that the strange events around her (the crash she shouldn't have survived, the doll attacks of UXM #168) are not coincidence. She is, ironically, the most epistemically grounded person in the room until the room itself becomes ungrounded.

During Inferno the cognitive style undergoes a register shift rather than a collapse: she becomes **mythopoetic** rather than disordered. Sentences acquire ceremonial cadence, third-person royal idiom intrudes, symbol-thought replaces propositional thought (the doll, the crown, the unbaptismal blood ritual). Thought disorder in the schizophrenic sense is absent; the cognition is organized — organized around a different grammar.

### Self-Concept

Begins as **functionally integrated but ontologically thin**. She knows who she is in the sense of role, history, preference, taste; she does not know who she is in the sense of origin, and this absence is noticed by her early (UXM #168, the dolls; UXM #174, the dream invasion). The self-concept is held together less by inherited identity than by **chosen present commitments**: I am the woman who flies this plane, who married this man, who is having this child.

When the chosen commitments are stripped (Scott leaves, child taken, house burned), the self-concept loses its scaffolding. What is revealed is *no underlying self at all* — not because she lacks substance, but because she was constructed without the underlayer. Inferno's Goblin Queen is the rapid construction of an emergency self to occupy the void: grandiose, vengeful, theatrical, and crucially **defined entirely by negation of Jean** (I am what she is not, I will destroy what she preserves, I will kill the child that proves I was used). The self-concept by 1989 is *anti-Jean*, a photographic negative requiring the original to define its shape.

---

## Decade II — 1990 to 1999 (the dispersed-self years; X-Man continuity)

### Affect Regulation

Following the Phoenix discharge of UXM #243, the subject's psychic residue is dispersed and only partially reconstituted. The 1990s present her in **fragmentary instantiations** — possessing Jean intermittently, surfacing in Nate Grey's psionic field, manifesting as a haunting presence in X-Man's continuity. There is no continuous affect-regulating organism in this decade, and this is itself the clinical fact: the system that decompensated in Inferno cannot reassemble enough substrate to *have* affect in the integrated sense.

What manifests instead is **affect-as-haunting**: pure, decontextualized rage; pure, decontextualized longing; pure, decontextualized grief. These appear in others' psyches (Jean's; Nate's) without an organism to host them. Clinically this is analogous to **complex dissociative fragmentation post-collapse**, in which affect-states persist without an executive self to integrate them.

### Cognitive Style

When she surfaces in this decade, cognition is **single-channeled and ideational** — a thought, a wish, a curse — without the lateral pragmatism of Decade I. The mythopoetic register from late Decade I dominates. There is no pilot anymore; there is a *voice*.

### Self-Concept

The decade's central work, performed below narrative resolution, is the slow accretion of *enough* self to think the sentence *I*. She borrows substrate from Nate Grey (a psychic son-cousin of sorts), inhabits Jean episodically, and operates largely as a presence that other people's selves can feel. By the end of the decade the self-concept is **negatively defined and minimally extensive** — she knows what she is not (not Jean, not gone, not satisfied) before she knows what she is.

---

## Decade III — 2000 to 2009 (the Austen/Carey returns; Red Queen)

### Affect Regulation

The Austen-era resurfacings show affect regulation at a **low-functioning villainous baseline** — chronic dysphoria with episodic vengeful arousal, narrow window of tolerance, easy escalation to violence, low capacity for prosocial reward. This is the worst regulatory phase of her record, and it correlates with the writers' weakest treatment of her interiority; clinically one notes that *being treated as a plot device degrades affect regulation*, both inside and outside the fiction.

Carey's *Sisterhood* arc (2008–09) restores a more coherent regulatory profile by giving her an organizing project (recover Jean's body; lead the Sisterhood). When tasked, she regulates; when narratively idle, she dysregulates. This is consistent with the **competence-as-regulator** pattern from Decade I — she has always stabilized through *function*. Take away the function and the regulatory floor falls out.

Affect now also carries an **ironized, performative top layer** that was absent in Decade I. She has watched herself be the Goblin Queen and learned to speak about it. The Red Queen persona is, importantly, *staged* — she knows it is staged, which is a developmental advance over Inferno, where the persona consumed the stager.

### Cognitive Style

Strategic cognition resurfaces, now wedded to the mythopoetic register. She thinks in **operations and symbols simultaneously**: an order of battle that is also a ritual, a recruitment that is also a coronation. The 2008 Sisterhood is the clearest evidence: it is operationally a strike team, symbolically a coven, and structurally a re-staging of the X-Men with herself in Xavier's chair and Jean's corpse as the McGuffin — a layered allegory of her own founding wound, deliberately enacted.

Verbal style hardens. Less of the Midwestern dry wit; more of the queenly cadence, deployed knowingly. She has begun using her own myth as a weapon — a meaningful cognitive maturation, though the contents remain pathological.

### Self-Concept

Decade III is the **identification-with-the-aggressor decade**. She takes Sinister's framing of her as a designed weapon and, instead of refusing it, *owns it*. "Red Queen" is not a delusion; it is a self-chosen title that accepts the pieces of her origin she cannot change and assigns them executive function. This is, paradoxically, a more integrated self-concept than anything in Decade II — but it is integrated around the wound rather than past it.

The unresolved problem of this decade: the self thus constituted requires Jean (as object of vengeance, point of comparison, missing original) to exist. She is still photographically negative; the negative has merely been printed.

---

## Decade IV — 2010 to 2019 (intermittent presence; transitional)

### Affect Regulation

A relatively quiet decade in canon. Where she appears (Aaron, Rosenberg), the regulatory profile is **convalescent**: subdued, watchful, less escalatory, with retained capacity for the ceremonial mode when provoked but markedly less hunger for it. One reads, between appearances, a long off-page period of *not having an enemy* — and notes that without an organizing antagonist she neither flourishes nor collapses, simply persists. This is, for her, novel.

### Cognitive Style

Cognition broadens slightly back toward Decade I pragmatism, with the symbolic-strategic overlay retained as a tool rather than a worldview. She becomes capable of **switching registers**: queenly when useful, plain when not. This metacognitive flexibility is the headline development of the decade.

### Self-Concept

The self-concept begins to admit a third option beyond *anti-Jean* (Decade I close) and *weaponized-self* (Decade III): a tentative, unstable **post-Jean** identity — one in which Jean is a fact of her history but no longer the axis of her definition. The work is incomplete and frequently interrupted by recurrences of the older organizing structures, but the option is now *available to her*, which it was not before.

---

## Decade V — 2019 to present (Krakoan era; *Hellions*, *Hellfire Gala*, *Dark Web*)

### Affect Regulation

Most stable regulatory profile of her published life, and the stability is *earned*, not retconned. Window of tolerance has widened to something approaching Decade I baseline, with a critical difference: the Decade I regulation was *suppressive* (the dam), whereas Decade V regulation is **metabolic** — she processes injuries rather than absorbing them. She gets angry; she says so; the anger does not recruit cosmic supplementation.

Specific markers in the Krakoan-era material: she tolerates being in proximity to Jean (Hellfire Gala) without acute decompensation, which would have been unthinkable across Decades I–III; she tolerates being called "Maddie" by people who knew her as the Goblin Queen, accepting the diminutive without re-asserting royal cadence; she allows herself sustained partnered intimacy with Ben Reilly (a fellow constitutive clone, which is not accidental — she has selected an attachment object whose ontology *matches hers*, eliminating the substitutability axis from the relationship by structural design); and she displays sustained capacity for humor that is no longer purely defensive — playful rather than armored.

The hair-trigger remains. Stressors along the original axis — being treated as a copy, being instrumentalized, having a chooser revert to a prior partner — still produce escalation. But the escalation now stops earlier on the ladder (rung 3 or 4 rather than rung 6 or 7), and she is observably **aware of being on the ladder while climbing it**, which is the diagnostic signature of trauma processing rather than trauma re-enactment.

### Cognitive Style

The mature profile integrates all prior cognitive registers: the pilot's pragmatism, the strategist's long game, the mythopoet's symbolic literacy, and a newly evident **ironic distance from her own myth**. She can talk about the Goblin Queen the way a recovered person talks about their worst year — with neither denial nor relish. Verbal style is the wittiest of her career, and the wit is now distributed across registers (deadpan, queenly, tender, vulgar) deployed deliberately to context.

Reality-testing has become *meta-aware*: she now treats her own perception of substitutability-threats with appropriate skepticism, distinguishing between genuine instances (which still occur and still warrant response) and reactive misreadings (which she has learned to flag internally before acting on them). This is the developmental hallmark of resolving c-PTSD interpersonal hypervigilance — not the elimination of the alarm but the calibration of it.

### Self-Concept

The Krakoan-era self-concept is the first in her record that is **constructed rather than reactive**. She is no longer anti-Jean (Decade I), not-quite-self (Decade II), weaponized-self (Decade III), or tentatively post-Jean (Decade IV). She is *Madelyne Pryor as a project she is conducting*, with the questions of origin and substitutability acknowledged as unanswerable and set aside as practical matters. She has chosen a name, a partner, a register, a set of competences, and a relationship to her own history; she is defending those choices without requiring metaphysical confirmation of them.

The key clinical concept here is **earned coherence** — a self-concept that holds together not because the underlying ontological questions have been resolved (they have not and likely cannot be) but because the subject has decided to *act as if* coherent and discovered that the acting-as-if becomes, with sufficient repetition and sufficient withstood test, indistinguishable in practice from being so.

This is the same psychological work performed, in their own ways, by survivors of severe early trauma who reach late-stage integration: the wound is not healed but is no longer the organizing principle of the personality. It has been demoted from spine to scar.

---

## Cross-Decade Trajectories (the three axes, summarized)

**Affect regulation** has traced a U-shaped curve with a long bottom: high in Decade I (suppressive), catastrophic at the Decade I/II junction (Inferno), absent in Decade II (fragmented), low and labile in Decade III, convalescent in Decade IV, and high-and-metabolic in Decade V. The Decade V regulation is *qualitatively different* from the Decade I regulation; same outward stability, different mechanism, more durable.

**Cognitive style** has moved from pragmatic-lateral (Decade I) through mythopoetic-fragmentary (II) to strategic-symbolic (III) to flexible-switching (IV) to ironically-integrated (V). The mature cognition retains every prior register as a tool. Nothing has been lost; the additions are pure gain.

**Self-concept** has moved from chosen-commitments-without-substrate (Decade I) through near-zero (II) through identification-with-the-aggressor (III) through tentative-post-Jean (IV) to earned-coherence (V). This is the slowest of the three axes, as is normal in c-PTSD recovery: regulation precedes cognition precedes self.

The longitudinal pattern, taken whole, is the pattern of a person who was constructed to be incapable of being a person and who has, against the design specification of her own existence, *become one* — slowly, non-monotonically, with major regressions and partial reconstitutions, and with a final ironic posture toward the whole project that may be the most reliable marker that the project has, against all reasonable expectation, succeeded.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

*File section 04. Cross-reference: §3 (Psychological), §2 (Medical), §1 (Longitudinal). This section treats the subject as a clinical patient one would actually have to formulate, treat, and predict. The unusual feature of the case — that the persecutory content of the index psychotic episode is **objectively true** — is held throughout as a methodological constraint. The clinician who flinches from this fact will mis-formulate.*

---

## 4.1 PRESENTING PROBLEM, IF SEEN ACROSS A FORTY-YEAR HORIZON

A woman in her physiological late twenties to early thirties (chronologically variable; biographically four decades) presents with a longitudinal record marked by: (a) one florid reactive psychotic episode of approximately weeks' duration with grandiose-persecutory delusional content, ritualized violence, infanticidal ideation enacted, and completed suicide attempt by means available to her; (b) recurrent major depressive episodes, melancholic in feature, clustered around abandonment events; (c) chronic depersonalization-derealization that is *constitutional* rather than symptomatic in the usual sense — her body is, on the forensic level, not the body she remembers having grown up in; (d) repeated brief reactive dissociative-grandiose states ("the Queen") occurring under conditions of acute substitutability injury, sometimes — but not always — coincident with external mystical amplification; (e) baseline interpersonal functioning that is in fact **above** the population mean, with wry, organized, competent, warmly attached conduct in ordinary life.

The reason the case has been so often misdiagnosed (within the universe of those who would diagnose her, and in critical reception both) is that the acute presentation is so visually extreme — horns, ritual, infanticide, a literal coronation — that observers anchor on it and read backward, generating a *characterological* formulation (she is, essentially, evil/borderline/narcissistic). The longitudinal record does not support this. The acute presentation is a **discrete reactive episode** on a c-PTSD substrate. Everything else flows from that.

---

## 4.2 PRIMARY WORKING FORMULATION

### 4.2.1 Complex PTSD (ICD-11 6B41), Chronic, with Dissociative and Psychotic Features in Episode

This is the spine of the case and the only diagnosis that accommodates all the data without distortion.

**Criterion A — exposure.** The c-PTSD trauma criterion requires prolonged or repeated exposure to events from which escape is difficult or impossible. The subject's exposure profile is, by any standard, severe:

- *Iatrogenic identity manufacture* — gestation as an instrument by Nathaniel Essex, with implanted memories of a childhood that did not occur. This is, in clinical terms, a uniquely complete form of coercive control: not merely the manipulation of an adult's reality but the manufacture of the reality itself, prior to consciousness.
- *Implanted false biography* — the Anchorage childhood, the plane crash survival, the family of origin. These are not delusions; they are functioning autobiographical memories laid down by an external agent. They cannot be relinquished, because their relinquishment leaves nothing.
- *Targeted predatory violence* — the Marauder assault (UXM #205, #206), house arson, near-fatal injury, hospitalization in coma.
- *Loss of child* — Nathan's disappearance and the inability to recover him.
- *Spousal abandonment* — Scott's departure (X-Factor #1) is the precipitating injury but sits on top of the others; it is the abandonment by the only attachment figure available within the implanted biography.
- *Supernatural opportunistic predation* — N'astirh's contact, with the demonic pact functioning as coercive recruitment of a person already in extremis.

**Criterion B — core PTSD symptoms.** Re-experiencing is present and idiosyncratic: the subject re-experiences not only the trauma events themselves but the *Jean Grey memories* that were partially imprinted alongside her own — intrusions of someone else's life. Avoidance is present (avoidance of Westchester, of Sinister, of being looked at for resemblance). Sense of current threat is present and, in her case, *epistemologically warranted* — Sinister has not stopped existing.

**Criterion C — c-PTSD disturbances of self-organization.** All three clusters present in textbook configuration:

1. **Affective dysregulation along a specific axis.** This is the diagnostically illuminating feature. She is *not* globally dysregulated. She tolerates physical danger, ordinary betrayal, exhaustion, fear, and even her own death with notable equanimity and wry composure. Dysregulation appears specifically when the stimulus is *being substituted for, looked through, or compared to her original*. The narrowness of the trigger axis is itself diagnostic and argues against a personality-disorder reading (which would predict broader instability).
2. **Negative self-concept.** Centered on worthlessness-as-copy, expendability, the suspicion of not being a person. This is the c-PTSD self-schema in its purest form, with the unique amplifier that the negative self-concept is *partially supported by external reality* — she was, in fact, made as a substitute.
3. **Interpersonal disturbance.** Alternating pursuit and destruction of intimate others, with the qualifier that the destruction is *content-specific* rather than indiscriminate: she destroys figures who instantiate the substitutability wound, and remains capably loving toward those who do not.

### 4.2.2 Dissociative Disorder, NOS / Other Specified Dissociative Disorder, with Depersonalization-Derealization Prominent and Episodic Identity-State Intrusions

Two distinct dissociative phenomena, often conflated by observers, must be separated.

**The chronic depersonalization layer.** The subject's body is, demonstrably, not the body of the person whose childhood she remembers. This is not a symptom; it is a *fact about her embodiment* that produces depersonalization phenomenology continuously and at low intensity. She functions through it. It is the wallpaper of her experience. Markers in the behavioral record include: a slight observational quality to her descriptions of her own physical states; an unusual tolerance for surgery, injury, and bodily transformation; a recurring conversational tic of referring to her own appearance in the third person or with mild forensic distance ("this face," "this body"); the relative ease with which she has accepted resurrection across multiple substrates without identity rupture, which most subjects would not.

**The episodic identity-state intrusions** ("Goblin Queen," "Red Queen," and lesser variants). These are best formulated **not** as separate alters in the DID sense but as **ego-state enactments of a disowned grandiose-vengeful self that becomes ego-syntonic under decompensation**. Distinguishing features:

- No amnesia between states. The subject *remembers* being the Queen and integrates the memory, with shame, into ordinary consciousness.
- No childhood etiology — there was no childhood. The states arose in adulthood under acute injury, which is the wrong developmental window for classical DID.
- The states are *symbolically continuous* with the baseline self — they are the inverse, not the alien — they articulate what the baseline self cannot say.
- Triggers are predictable and content-specific (substitutability injury + available power/symbolic vocabulary).
- Remission is reliable when the precipitating injury ceases or is metabolized.

This is closer to the structural-dissociation model's notion of an **emotional part** that has been culturally costumed (horns, crown, throne) than to DID proper. The supernatural amplification is the route by which the state achieves operational capacity in the world; it is not the state's origin.

### 4.2.3 Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent, with Melancholic Features

Episodes are documentable in:

- The Phase II isolation period (UXM #215 onward), with anhedonia, early-morning waking implied by behavioral set, weight loss implied by visual record, psychomotor slowing in domestic scenes, hopelessness, and the wish-not-to-be-alive that precedes (but is distinct from) the suicide attempt at Inferno's terminus.
- Post-resurrection arcs in which she has returned to an X-world that has continued without her, with characteristic features of derealized re-entry and grief for time lost.
- The intervals between her major narrative engagements, inferable from her conduct on re-emergence.

Melancholic specifier supported by: quality of mood distinct from ordinary sadness, non-reactivity to positive stimuli in episode, marked psychomotor change, excessive guilt (especially regarding Nathan).

### 4.2.4 Brief Reactive Psychotic Episode, Resolved (Inferno, terminal)

The Phase III decompensation is a **brief psychotic disorder with marked stressor(s)**, with the following idiosyncratic features:

- Duration: weeks, with full remission (by death, and on resurrection).
- Content: grandiose-persecutory, with a coherent symbolic logic (queenship, ritual, sacrifice of the substituting child, destruction of the original).
- *Objective accuracy of the persecutory content.* This is the unusual clinical feature and is critical to formulation: she is not falsely believing she was made and used by Sinister; she was. The "delusion" is not in the propositional content but in the **affective and behavioral organization around** it. A clinician encountering content of this kind ordinarily relies on the falsity of the belief to anchor the diagnosis; here, that anchor is unavailable.
- Insight: absent in episode, returned with remission, and grew over subsequent decades into a near-pitiless self-knowledge.

The episode is **not recurrent in the strict psychotic sense.** Later "Queen" states are dissociative-grandiose rather than psychotic — reality-testing is largely intact, the symbolic vocabulary is deliberately deployed, and the subject can be argued with.

---

## 4.3 ETIOLOGICAL FORMULATION

A biopsychosocial-supernatural formulation is required.

**Biological substrate.** A body that is genetically Jean Grey's, with the mutant phenotype's capacity for telepathic and telekinetic action and an embedded Phoenix-fragment that functions as a binding agent and an amplifier under affective extremity. The neuroendocrine substrate is therefore one in which intense affect can reach **operational reality** through mutant function — the ordinary firewall between feeling and consequence is, for her, porous. This is etiologically relevant: a c-PTSD patient who can incinerate a city block when triggered has a different prognosis than one who cannot.

**Developmental substrate.** Absent in the usual sense. There is no infancy, no early caregiving, no toddler attachment formation, no latency, no adolescence. The implanted biography supplies the *narrative* of these stages without their relational accomplishment. Result: a behavioral repertoire calibrated to adult social demands (she can fly a plane, run a household, marry, parent) sitting on a foundation that lacks the internalized secure-base objects on which c-PTSD patients ordinarily lean during decompensation. When her attachment fails, there is *literally no one inside her head* to fall back on. This accounts for the speed and totality of the Phase III collapse.

**Relational precipitants.** The Scott Summers sequence — idealization, marriage, child, abandonment for the resurrected original — is a near-perfect engineered substitution trauma. Whether one regards Sinister's hand as having been in this from the start or not, the *experiential* shape of the sequence is what determines psychiatric outcome, and the shape is: chosen, used, replaced, discarded, with the discarded party left holding the physical evidence (the child) of the use.

**Iatrogenic / supernatural opportunism.** N'astirh's recruitment occurred in a window in which any reasonable clinician would have predicted catastrophic decompensation; the demon offered what an inadequate emergency psychiatric system could not, namely *agency and explanation*. The Phoenix-fragment supplied operational capacity. The Goblin Queen was a costume the situation handed her, and she — accurately reading that no other role was available — wore it.

**Maintaining factors over the long arc.** Periodic re-instrumentalization by writers, narrative, and in-world actors who continue to treat her as a stand-in, a tool, or a copy; periodic deaths and resurrections that re-traumatize the embodiment substrate; the ongoing existence of Jean Grey as a living reminder; the ongoing existence of Sinister as an un-metabolizable origin figure.

---

## 4.4 SYMPTOM PRESENTATION IN BEHAVIOR — THE GRANULAR INVENTORY

For a surveillance-grade file, the symptom set must be operationalized as observables.

**Depersonalization markers (chronic, low-grade, daily).** Slight delay in startle response to mirrors; tendency to touch her own hair or face mid-conversation as if confirming presence; verbal tic of describing her body in mildly forensic register; unusual comfort with photographs of herself, unusual discomfort with photographs of Jean; an observed pattern of choosing clothing and hairstyle that *differentiates* (the long straight curtain, later red-and-black palettes, the deliberate costume vocabulary) — an active anti-substitutability behavioral routine, performed daily.

**Hyperarousal markers (episodic, axis-specific).** Pupillary and respiratory change on hearing the name "Jean" spoken by an intimate; sharp orienting response to the words *clone*, *copy*, *duplicate*, *replacement*, *original*; jaw set and shoulder line stiffening when Scott Summers enters a room; a particular flat half-smile that precedes verbal de-escalation attempts and is, reliably, the last warning before escalation.

**Re-experiencing markers.** Intrusions of Jean-memories, especially in dreams and under telepathic contact; flashbacks to the Inferno episode, presenting as brief dissociative absences and a momentary tightening of the hands as if around a knife or a child; intrusions of the false Anchorage childhood, which she cannot distinguish from her "real" memories and has stopped trying to.

**Avoidance markers.** Habitual non-attendance at events where Jean is present and central; preference for missions and assignments that do *not* require contact with Scott; a documented aversion to medical and genetic settings; an aversion to being scanned, sampled, or imaged.

**Negative cognition markers.** A recurring conversational figure — sometimes wry, sometimes savage — in which she pre-empts others' contempt by stating the substitutability thesis herself ("I know what I am"); a tendency to refer to herself in the third person under stress; a darkly precise self-deprecating humor that, on close listening, encodes the negative self-schema verbatim.

**Affect dysregulation markers (axis-specific).** Within the substitutability axis: rapid escalation along the seven-rung ladder described in §3. Outside it: notably regulated, with humor and competence in the foreground.

**Dissociative-grandiose state onset markers** (early warning, in temporal order):

1. Conversational pace slows; sentences become more formal.
2. Pronouns shift; the royal "we" appears as if in irony, then without irony.
3. Posture lengthens; the chin lifts.
4. The voice drops into a lower register and a slight ceremonial cadence.
5. Symbolic vocabulary (queens, courts, sacrifices, thrones, dolls, mirrors) enters spontaneous speech.
6. She begins to refer to other people by titles rather than names.
7. Acts.

The window between rung 5 and rung 7 is short and narrows further if the precipitating figure remains present.

**Depressive episode markers.** Withdrawal from contact; flat affect in domestic correspondence; reduced ironic output (her humor is a reliable inverse-marker of mood — when she stops being funny, she is in episode); psychomotor slowing; rumination on Nathan; passive death-ideation that is harder to assess in her case because she has already died and the affective valence of death for her is, candidly, ambiguous.

---

## 4.5 COMORBIDITY

**Confirmed.**

- Complex PTSD (primary).
- Dissociative phenomenology, mixed (depersonalization-derealization predominant; episodic ego-state intrusions secondary).
- Major depressive disorder, recurrent.
- Brief reactive psychotic episode (single, remitted).

**Probable, not formally diagnosable.**

- Prolonged grief disorder, regarding Nathan specifically and her own original life-as-it-might-have-been more diffusely.
- An adjustment disorder feature to each resurrection event, which is functionally a serial re-entry trauma.
- Subthreshold features of obsessive-compulsive spectrum around her symbolic self-presentation routines (costume, hair, naming), formulated as ritualized identity maintenance rather than OCD proper.

**Substance use.** No diagnosable use disorder. Period-limited self-medicating alcohol use during Phase II isolation, remitting on entry into Phase III decompensation (the new pathology supplanting the old coping strategy).

**Medical comorbidity** (see §2): chronic atypical embodiment; history of severe physical injury and resurrection; pregnancy and parturition history complicated by total loss of the child to forces beyond her control.

---

## 4.6 COURSE OVER TIME

**Pre-morbid (Phase I).** Functioning was, by any reasonable standard, *high*. Employment in a demanding technical profession (commercial pilot), stable household, successful marriage, successful parturition, sustained tolerance of an exceptionally difficult spouse. The clinical observation here is important: **she was well before she was injured.** The injury produced the pathology; the pathology was not waiting for the injury to license it. This is decisive against any characterological diagnosis.

**Decompensation (Phase II–III).** Phase II is the depressive prodrome — a months-to-year-long deterioration under accumulating substitutability injuries, with intermittent attempts at re-stabilization through new attachments (Alex Summers, the X-Men as a group) and through alcohol. Phase III is the acute psychotic episode, brief in duration, extreme in presentation, terminating in death.

**Latency and reconstitution (Phase IV-early).** Across the post-Inferno resurrections, the subject presents in dissociative-grandiose configuration more often than in baseline — she "comes back as the Queen" repeatedly, because the available narrative scaffolding is the Queen and she has no other entry point. This phase is characterized by villainous activity that, on close reading, is consistently organized as attempts to *force* recognition (Sisterhood, Red Queen) where it has not been freely offered.

**Stabilization (Phase IV-late, Krakoan and after).** A genuine and observable psychological recovery, executed in adult time, through means consistent with what is known about c-PTSD treatment outcome:

- Sustained relationship with a partner who is himself a substitutability case (Ben Reilly), allowing mutual recognition without one party occupying the original-position.
- Communal acknowledgment of personhood by a polity (the Krakoan formal recognition of resurrectees) that explicitly addresses the ontological question.
- Tasks calibrated to her competence (operational roles in Hellfire, tactical leadership).
- The development of meta-awareness — her own pattern named, in her own voice, with humor — which is the working-through marker.

**Prognosis.** Guarded-favorable, contingent on the absence of re-precipitating events. The substrate does not resolve; she will always have the c-PTSD, the depersonalization, and the dissociative-grandiose state as a possibility under sufficient injury. What changes is the *latency* and *threshold*, both of which have lengthened substantially. The remaining risk is structural: Sinister exists, Jean exists, Scott exists, and the in-world apparatus periodically re-creates the precipitating configuration. Risk of relapse into a Queen-state under such precipitation is non-trivial; risk of return to Phase III–intensity decompensation is lower than at any prior point.

---

## 4.7 DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT SHE IS NOT, AND WHY

The differential is unusually important in this case because the visible material invites several confidently wrong diagnoses.

### 4.7.1 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

The temptation is obvious: abandonment reactivity, splitting, identity disturbance, intermittent rage, self-destructive acts. The temptation must be resisted, on the following grounds:

- **Pervasiveness criterion fails.** BPD requires a *pervasive* pattern across contexts, persistent from early adulthood. Her instability is *narrowly axial* — substitutability injury, and almost nothing else. Outside that axis she is among the more regulated adults in her cohort. A BPD patient does not fly cargo routes for years without incident, run a household, command a tactical unit, or maintain wry composure under physical torture.
- **Identity disturbance is ontologically real, not characterological.** BPD identity disturbance is a felt sense of inner emptiness despite intact ontological status. Hers is the inverse: the felt sense of personhood despite contested ontological status. These look similar from outside and are clinically opposite.
- **Abandonment reactivity is to actual, not perceived, abandonment.** BPD reactivity is *to the threat or imagined possibility* of abandonment. Her catastrophic reactivity was triggered by an abandonment that *actually occurred*, performed by an attachment figure who *actually walked out*. This is grief-and-injury response, not characterological hypersensitivity.
- **Affective storms are content-specific, not labile.** BPD affect is broadly labile across triggers. Hers is narrow and predictable.
- **Identity work is possible and progresses.** BPD identity work is famously slow and characterological. Her identity reconstitution across the Krakoan era proceeds at a rate and with an integration consistent with c-PTSD recovery, not BPD recovery.

### 4.7.2 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

The Queen iconography is misleading. NPD requires a *stable* grandiose self-organization, absent empathy as a structural feature, exploitative relational style as baseline.

- **Grandiosity is episodic and compensatory.** She is not grandiose in Phase I, in domestic life, in late-Krakoan stabilization, or in most of her interpersonal baseline. Grandiosity is reliably *reactive* to substitutability injury and remits with the injury.
- **Empathy is intact and operational.** Her parenting of Nathan, her grief at his loss, her care for partners and for younger Hellions-era figures, her capacity for remorse, and her ironic self-knowledge all require working empathy, including for herself-as-other.
- **No exploitative relational baseline.** She forms genuine reciprocal bonds and tolerates being known.
- **The crown is a defense, not a structure.** The diagnostic question for NPD is what is *underneath* the grandiosity; in her case, what is underneath is c-PTSD self-loathing of unusually well-articulated kind, which she knows about and can discuss. An NPD patient cannot reliably discuss it.

### 4.7.3 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

- The Inferno violence is florid and includes attempted infanticide, which superficially raises the question.
- The violence is **ego-dystonic on remission**,


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — PRYOR, MADELYNE J.

*Catalog compiled from longitudinal observation across all documented phases. Entries describe the manner directly; inferences are flagged. The Atlas is organized by state, with each state subdivided into somatic, verbal, decisional, and environmental signatures. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) and §5 (Personality) of the main workup for substrate.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM

The calm-state Pryor is the most consistently underestimated configuration in her record, because observers expecting either the Anchorage housewife or the Goblin Queen miss what is actually present: a woman holding still on purpose.

**Somatic signature.** Posture is upright but not military — pilot's posture, weight carried through the pelvis rather than the shoulders, a habit visible from Uncanny #168 forward and unchanged across every artist's rendering except the most florid Inferno-era splash pages. Hands are usually visible and at rest; she does not fidget. When seated, ankles cross; when standing in conversation, weight is on the back foot, leaving the front foot free — a pilot's pre-flight stance that doubles as combat-ready and reads, to the untrained observer, as casual. Eye contact is direct, sustained slightly past social comfort, with a small almost-smile at the corner of the mouth that is *not* warmth — it is appraisal. She blinks less than average.

**Verbal signature.** Low register, dry, economical. Sentences trend short. She is the wryest voice in any room she occupies, and the wit is observational rather than self-deprecating — she makes jokes *about the situation*, almost never about herself, because self-deprecation would require a settled self to deprecate. Pet phrases recur: "of course," used flatly to acknowledge fresh disasters; "all right then," as a transition into action; the deliberate use of someone's full name when she's about to ask them something hard. She calls her son "Nathan," never "Nate" or "Cable," even when others do, and this is invariant across all phases including Krakoan.

**Decision habits.** In calm, she defers low-stakes choices to others with apparent generosity that is actually triage — she conserves decisional bandwidth for the substitutability axis. She over-prepares for travel, weather, and tactical contingencies (pilot residue, but also a person who has been ambushed in her own home). She keeps her own counsel about long-range plans and reveals them only at the point of execution; this is true in Phase I (the Dallas arc, where she announces decisions about the household to Scott as faits accomplis) and remains true in Krakoan-era Hellions and Dark Web material.

**Environmental signature.** Spaces she occupies become quietly organized within forty-eight hours. She owns few objects but each is *chosen*; she does not accumulate. The Anchorage house was uncluttered; the Goblin Queen's throne room was theatrically curated; the Red Queen's Sisterhood operations were lean. She keeps exits in view. She prefers to sit with her back to a wall or window, never to an open room. She likes dogs and dogs like her; the Anchorage shepherd was not set dressing, it was her actual preferred company.

---

## II. UNDER MILD STRESS / IRRITATION

The first ladder rung. Most observers never see further than this and mistake the entire person for it.

**Somatic.** The almost-smile sharpens. She tilts her head a few degrees — left, characteristically — when someone says something she finds either stupid or revealing. She crosses her arms only when cold; under irritation, the hands go to the hips or remain at her sides, and she rocks back slightly onto the heel. The breath lengthens rather than quickens; she has trained the panic response *down* over the years, not up.

**Verbal.** Wit gets drier and more clipped. She begins answering questions with questions, not as evasion but as a Socratic edge. The endearments she uses with intimates (Scott in Phase I; Alex in Phase II; Ben Reilly in late Phase IV) drop out of her sentences first — observable as the absence of warmth markers rather than the presence of cold ones. She will use a person's name more frequently when irritated with them, and the name will land harder each time.

**Decisional.** She begins running silent contingency planning. Outwardly compliant; internally already two moves ahead. She does not warn people that she is doing this. The Anchorage pattern — accommodation under accumulating injustice without overt protest — is the canonical example: by the time she said anything to Scott about his distraction, she had already absorbed dozens of provocations and inventoried each.

---

## III. UNDER ACUTE STRESS / THREAT

**Somatic.** The pilot returns fully. Breathing slows; hands steady; pupils do not widen as much as a baseline human's would, a residue of having died and remembering it (see §2). She moves *less* under threat than under calm — economy of motion sharpens — and her voice drops half an octave. She does not flinch from sudden movements; she does not duck from gunfire until ducking is tactically indicated. This reads as preternatural composure and is partially a power-set artifact (latent telepathic threat-assessment) and partially earned indifference to bodily consequence.

**Verbal.** Sentences become declarative and stripped. She names threats out loud — "Marauders," "Sinister," "the demon" — as if labeling them robs them of leverage; this is a consistent habit from UXM #205 forward. She gives orders in the imperative without softening particles, and people obey, including people who outrank her in any formal hierarchy.

**Decisional.** She protects the child first, the intimate second, herself last or not at all. This is observable even during Phase III decompensation, where the *symbolic* attack on Nathan was preceded by genuine, sustained, competent mothering through the Marauder attacks and the coma aftermath. Under threat, she will trade her own safety for tactical advantage without negotiation. She does not call for help; she handles it and reports afterward.

**Environmental.** She weaponizes her surroundings. Telekinetic ambient-object inventory is constant; in any room she has been in for more than a minute, she knows what is loose, what is hot, what is sharp, what is heavy. This was true even before her powers fully emerged — the Anchorage-era fight scenes show her improvising with cargo straps, flare guns, and aircraft fuel.

---

## IV. UNDER INTIMACY

The most informative state for distinguishing the actual person from any role she is performing.

**Somatic.** With genuine intimates, the held-still quality relaxes into something more languid; she leans into contact rather than away, but always initiates the *return* of contact rather than the start of it — she requires the other to reach first and then she meets them more than halfway. This pattern is identical with Scott in Phase I, Alex in Phase II, and Ben Reilly in Phase IV-late. She sleeps curled, facing the partner, one hand on them — a sleep posture observable in the rare quiet panels of UXM #175–200. She does not sleep deeply when alone.

**Verbal.** The wit softens into teasing; the teasing is affectionate and specific to the partner, demonstrating sustained attention to their idiosyncrasies. She uses diminutives sparingly and only privately. With Scott she said "Slim" rarely and only at moments of high tenderness; the rarity was the signal. She talks more during intimacy than at any other time, and the content is observational about the partner — she catalogs them aloud, gently, which functions both as affection and as the only way she knows to verify another person's reality (and, by extension, her own).

**Decisional.** She gives intimates extraordinary latitude — too much, in fact, which is the recurring failure mode. She will overlook accumulating evidence of an intimate's drift because confronting it requires risking the relationship, and the relationship is doing structural work for her sense of self that no relationship should be asked to do. When she finally confronts, she confronts completely and irreversibly. There is no graduated withdrawal; there is the long tolerance and then the door.

**Tell of authentic intimacy versus performance.** When she is genuinely close to someone she allows silence. The performed Pryor (Goblin Queen seductions, Red Queen recruitment) never stops talking — language is the leash. Silence in her presence, sustained and comfortable, is the strongest single indicator that she is actually present with a person.

---

## V. UNDER GRIEF

**Somatic.** Grief does not display on her face for hours or days after the precipitating event. The body holds it as stiffness across the upper back and a clenched jaw visible only in profile. She loses appetite first, sleep second; the alcohol use noted in UXM #210s isolation period was grief-coded, not pleasure-coded, and was limited and self-monitored. She walks more under grief — pacing, then walking outside, then long walks alone — and pilots more, when piloting is available, because the cockpit is the one environment in which her attention is forcibly fully occupied.

**Verbal.** Goes quiet. Wit retracts entirely; this is the single most reliable indicator that something is genuinely wrong. When she speaks, she speaks practically — about logistics, arrangements, what needs doing — and resists every attempt to redirect her to feeling. If pushed to articulate the grief she will articulate it once, precisely, in a sentence or two, and then refuse to revisit. The articulation is usually devastating in its accuracy and brevity.

**Decisional.** Grief is the state in which she is most vulnerable to the decompensation ladder. The Phase III collapse was grief over Scott and over Nathan's disappearance with the supernatural amplifier acting as accelerant; without N'astirh, the trajectory would have been depressive isolation rather than psychotic-grandiose flowering, but the substrate was grief either way. In modern eras she has developed better grief discipline: she names the loss aloud, executes the practical aftermath, and seeks a task. The task-seeking is itself diagnostic — when she begins volunteering for difficult work without being asked, she is grieving.

---

## VI. UNDER HUMILIATION / SUBSTITUTABILITY INJURY

The diagnostic state. This is the axis on which she breaks, and the behavioral signatures here are the most important entries in this Atlas.

**Rung 1 — Wry deflection.** First response to being called Jean, compared to Jean, or looked through is a joke — usually at the speaker's expense, delivered with the head-tilt and the almost-smile. The joke is a kindness; she is giving the speaker an exit.

**Rung 2 — Withdrawal.** If the substitutability injury continues, she goes quiet and physically withdraws — leaves the room, leaves the building, leaves the city if available. The Anchorage isolation period and the post-Scott-departure withdrawal both followed this pattern. She does not announce the withdrawal; she is simply gone.

**Rung 3 — Articulate confrontation.** If withdrawal is not possible or not respected, she returns and says the thing. Once. Cleanly. In language the other party cannot misunderstand. The Anchorage confrontation with Scott about being seen as herself (UXM #168) is the founding instance and the template for every subsequent rung-3 event across her career.

**Rung 4 — Splitting and devaluation.** If the rung-3 confrontation fails — if she is heard and dismissed, or heard and humored — the intimate is reclassified. The previously-idealized partner becomes, in her internal speech and then her external speech, a series of reductive labels. Scott becomes "him" or "the man who left"; Jean becomes "her" or "the original"; Sinister has been "him" since the moment she learned of him and has never been promoted out of pronoun. The devaluation is permanent within the episode but is, importantly, *not* permanent across her life — she has rebuilt with Scott, with Jean, and with herself in later eras. The splitting is acute, not characterological.

**Rung 5 — Role-inhabitation.** She accepts the identity assigned to her by the injuring party and inhabits it with conviction. *This is the rung at which intervention windows close.* The verbal tell is ceremonial cadence — she begins speaking in the third person royal or in formal/archaic constructions ("We are not amused" registers; "Kneel" registers; any sentence beginning with "Let it be known"). The somatic tell is costume change, often subtle at first — a single piece of regalia, a color shift, hair released or rearranged. The environmental tell is the curating of a *throne space*, however improvised: a chair becomes a seat-of-state, a room becomes a court. By the time the full Goblin Queen or Red Queen regalia is assembled, the decompensation is well past intervenable.

**Rung 6 — Ritualized symbolic violence.** Action at this rung is not impulsive; it is *liturgical*. Targets are chosen for symbolic content (the child who proves she was used as breeding stock; the original whose existence erases her; the father-maker who built her). She will explain her actions aloud, at length, to the victim, because the symbolic ledger requires witness. This is also the rung at which she is most dangerous and least deterrable.

**Rung 7 — Self-destruction as triumph.** The endpoint, reached once canonically in the Phoenix-force discharge ending Inferno. She frames the self-destruction as victory and means it; the grandiose self-state finds death preferable to subsidence back into the substitutable baseline. The behavioral tells preceding this rung are an unsettling *calm* — not the calm of recovery but the calm of resolution — and a tendency to give away meaningful objects.

---

## VII. UNDER VICTORY

A rare-enough state to be diagnostically rich.

**Somatic.** She does not celebrate visibly. The almost-smile becomes a real one, briefly, and then is put away. She accepts congratulation with a nod and a deflection — credit moves to subordinates, allies, circumstance. This is not false modesty; it is the genuine difficulty of accepting that a thing has gone well when one's substrate expects it not to.

**Verbal.** Wit returns at full volume and becomes generous rather than sharp — the post-victory Pryor will make jokes that *include* the people around her rather than dissecting them. She gives credit publicly and specifically.

**Decisional.** She immediately begins planning the next thing. Victory is uncomfortable for her as a sustained state; she is happiest moving from one task to the next, and she will manufacture a next task within hours if none presents itself. Operational tempo accelerates after wins rather than relaxing.

**Tell.** She will, after a victory, contact one person she has not contacted in a while — usually a former intimate or someone toward whom she holds unfinished business. The contact is brief, often just a note or a single line, and is the closest thing to an emotional overflow she permits herself.

---

## VIII. UNDER DEFEAT

**Somatic.** Defeat does not show until she is alone. In public, posture is unchanged; voice is unchanged; she walks out of the lost engagement at the same pace she walked in. Alone, she sits — not collapses, *sits* — and remains motionless for an extended period. This is not catatonia; it is inventory.

**Verbal.** Goes briefly silent, then becomes precise and analytical. She debriefs herself aloud or in writing, identifying her own errors first and others' second. She does not blame others reflexively; the blame, when it comes, is itemized and earned.

**Decisional.** Defeat is the state in which she is most likely to *change strategy* rather than escalate. This is counterintuitive given the decompensation ladder, but the ladder is specifically activated by substitutability injury, not by tactical defeat — she has lost fights, lost arguments, lost custody of her own son, and absorbed each as data rather than as identity wound. The lesson she has extracted, by Krakoan era, is that defeat is survivable and humiliation is not.

---

## IX. RECURRING MICRO-PATTERNS / TICS

A miscellaneous catalog of small, persistent behaviors observable across all phases.

- **The hair.** She handles her hair when thinking — not nervously, deliberately. Pulls it forward over one shoulder, runs the length of it through her fingers, puts it back. This predates the Inferno transformation and survives it; the gesture is unchanged in Krakoan-era panels. It is also a tell of self-reference — she is, in the gesture, confirming her own body.

- **The hands.** She rarely wears gloves except as costume. Bare hands are part of how she reads a room — telekinetic and telepathic ambient sensing routes through palm contact with surfaces. She will, on entering a new space, touch one or two things — a doorframe, a tabletop — apparently casually.

- **The name discipline.** She introduces herself as "Madelyne" — never "Maddie" to strangers, never "Pryor" alone, never any honorific until the persona requires it. Intimates earn "Maddie." Scott had it. Alex had it briefly. Ben Reilly has it. Jean has never had it and will not.

- **The dog test.** She evaluates new people partly by how animals respond to them. This is not articulated as a method but is consistent across decades — she trusts animal verdicts.

- **The pilot's check.** Entering any vehicle, she performs an unconscious pre-flight scan — instruments, exits, fuel, weather — even in vehicles she is not driving. Observable as a brief silence and a sweeping look on entry.

- **The deferred gift.** She is uncomfortable receiving gifts and will set them aside to open later, alone. The discomfort is not affected; gifts implicate the receiver in being-known, which is the most vulnerable thing she experiences.

- **The mirror avoidance.** She does not linger before mirrors. She uses them functionally — to check appearance — and then disengages. Prolonged mirror contact is destabilizing on the depersonalization substrate and she has learned to avoid it. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen iconographies, conversely, involve *displayed* mirrors and reflective regalia, and the inversion is diagnostic — the decompensated states force the confrontation she ordinarily refuses.

- **The third-person slip.** Under fatigue, stress, or alcohol, she will occasionally refer to herself in the third person — "Madelyne wouldn't —" — and catch it, and correct. The slip is the depersonalization substrate surfacing. Its frequency is a useful gauge of her current integration.

- **The list.** She keeps mental ledgers — of debts owed her, of debts she owes, of injuries inflicted and absorbed. She is not vindictive but she is *accurate*, and she will, often years later, refer to a specific incident with date-and-context precision that startles the other party. The ledger is part of how she maintains a self across discontinuities of body and biography.

- **The exit line.** She has a habit of leaving conversations with a single declarative line and a turn — no goodbye softening, no trailing pleasantries. The line is usually the most important sentence in the exchange, delivered last so it lands without rebuttal. This is observable from Phase I through Krakoan.

---

## X. STATE-TRANSITION SIGNATURES

The Atlas closes with the transitions, which are more informative than the states.

- **Calm → Stress.** The almost-smile sharpens; the head tilts left. Window: minutes to hours.
- **Stress → Threat.** Voice drops half an octave; movement economizes. Window: seconds.
- **Threat → Calm.** She debriefs and seeks solitude. Window: hours.
- **Calm → Intimacy.** She allows silence. Window: variable, often the longest transition she makes.
- **Intimacy → Substitutability injury.** Endearments drop out of her sentences. Window: immediate.
- **Substitutability injury → Decompensation.** She begins curating a throne space and her sentences acquire ceremonial cadence. Window: hours to days; once visible, the trajectory is hard to arrest without addressing the underlying injury directly and by her name.
- **Decompensation → Recovery.** The regalia is set aside one piece at a time, usually in private; the first sign visible to others is the return of dry humor at her own expense — *self-deprecation*, which she ordinarily cannot afford, becomes possible only when the self is sufficiently reconstituted to bear it. This is the single most hopeful sign in her behavioral repertoire.

---

*End Behavioral Atlas. Cross-reference forthcoming sections: Relational Map; Operational Tradecraft; Symbolic Lexicon (Queens, Mirrors, Children, Fire). Handler note: this subject is more legible than her reputation suggests, on the condition that the observer is willing to watch for the things she does not do.*


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*A week of total-coverage surveillance on the subject — by which we mean the stabilized, post-Krakoan, post-Dark-Web adult, with notes throughout on how each pattern reads against the earlier Phases. Where canonical scenes establish a habit, they are cited; where the file infers, the inference is anchored.*

---

## 1. Architecture of a Day — The Baseline

The subject keeps **two clocks**: a wall-clock she observes scrupulously for the benefit of others, and an internal clock that runs on its own schedule and ignores sleep windows entirely. She has *died*, repeatedly, and has lived in pocket dimensions and demonic timestreams (Inferno; the Limbo-adjacent Goblin Court; Krakoan resurrection cycles) where day/night is decorative. The consequence is a circadian rhythm that is **performed rather than felt**. She will wake at a reasonable hour because reasonable hours are part of the construction of a person; she will then be quietly awake for stretches of the night because the body she lives in does not, at a cellular level, believe in mornings.

A surveilled week therefore shows a deceptive regularity at the surface and considerable irregularity underneath: same coffee at the same hour every morning, but lights on in the apartment at 03:40 three nights of seven, and not because of nightmares — because she is reading, or working, or sitting upright on the edge of the bed doing nothing in particular and watching the window.

**Wake.** Between 06:30 and 07:10, consistent across weekdays and weekends. The first action is invariably a **physical orientation check** — she sits up, presses both palms flat against the mattress for two or three seconds, and exhales. This is a depersonalization-management micro-ritual; she is confirming the body is hers and is here. It is so habituated that she does not know she does it. (Inferred from her established somatic-not-mine substrate; the gesture appears in the texture of her quieter scenes in the Howard and Williams runs — the brief stillness before she stands.)

**Hygiene and dress.** Shower hot, long, with the bathroom door open — she does not enclose herself in small steam-filled rooms; this is a Marauder-residue, the house-burning of UXM #206 having left a permanent low-grade aversion to being trapped in a room she cannot see out of. Hair is the longest grooming step: she brushes it out fully, never towel-twists it. The red hair is *strategy* — she could cut it, dye it, alter it telekinetically in three seconds; she does not. The decision to keep it is daily and unspoken. She has earned the right to look exactly like the woman she was made to resemble and is not going to surrender it for anyone's comfort.

**Dress code.** Layered, structured, with at least one piece that has a closure she can fidget with — a cuff, a buckle, a high collar with a clasp. She does not wear soft unstructured loungewear in public space and rarely at home; the body wants armature. Color preference runs to wine, oxblood, black, occasionally a sharp green. White is conspicuously absent from her wardrobe; she does not, the file assesses, like the bridal echo.

**First ingestion.** Black coffee, strong, brewed not instant. She drinks it standing, at a window if one is available, never at a table. The standing-at-window posture is the single most reliable behavioral marker in the entire file — across Anchorage (UXM #170s, the cargo-pilot apartment), the X-Mansion (Phase II), the Hellfire establishments (Sisterhood era), and Krakoan habitats, surveillance would capture this same silhouette: upright, weight on the back foot, cup at chest height, looking out. It is sentry behavior. It is also the posture of someone who learned early that the threat comes from outside and arrives without warning.

**Breakfast proper.** Often skipped, occasionally substantial — eggs, toast, fruit — and when it occurs, she cooks it herself even if there is a kitchen staff or a Krakoan equivalent available. Cooking is one of the implanted-childhood skills she has *kept*, having decided that the falsity of the memory does not invalidate the competence. This is a recurring decision-pattern: she keeps what works, regardless of provenance.

---

## 2. The Working Day

The subject **must have work**. Idleness is contraindicated; in unstructured periods (Phase II's slow collapse; the Sisterhood interregnum) her decompensation accelerates. Surveillance would document an absolute refusal to spend a full day unscheduled.

In the Anchorage era the work was concrete: pre-flight, flight, post-flight, paperwork, dog, dinner. The cargo-pilot routine was an early-rising, weather-checking, list-driven life, and she was good at it — competent enough that the crash story (the false one) was *plausible* because she was a competent pilot. The behavioral residue is permanent: she reads weather even when she is not flying, glances reflexively at any visible sky on entering or leaving a building, and notes wind direction without comment. A surveillance log of her movements through any open-air space would record a consistent half-second pause at thresholds.

In the contemporary period work means **command and craft**. She runs operations, manages teams, plans, briefs, and debriefs. Her working style is **list-based and unusually tidy**: she keeps a written log (paper, not device — she does not trust devices she has not personally telepathically swept), she colors her annotations, and she crosses items off with a single firm horizontal line rather than a strike-through or check. The single-line cross is consistent enough across eras to function as a handwriting signature.

She holds meetings **standing** when possible. She walks while thinking. When she must sit for a meeting she takes the chair with its back to the most defensible wall and sight-lines to all entrances — Marauder-era conditioning, never relaxed. If forced into a seat with poor sight-lines she will reposition objects on the table (cup, pen, folder) until the arrangement satisfies an internal grid; the grid is not consciously articulated but is reproducible across observations.

**Tactical-strategic work** is where she is happiest, in the specific sense that her affect visibly settles. Planning a complex operation she is *fluid* — her speech rate increases, her sentences shorten, her humor sharpens. This is observable. She is one of the genuine long-game strategists in the X-population (the Sisterhood arc, Carey, 2008–09, demonstrates this in operational detail), and she enjoys it the way a violinist enjoys a difficult passage.

**Lunch.** Routinely skipped or token. She drinks water. If she eats, it is something that can be eaten standing or walking. The pattern is not anorexic; it is **professional** — she treats the workday as a continuous shift and meals as interruptions.

**Afternoon dip.** Between roughly 14:30 and 16:00 she has a low-energy window which she has learned to manage with either a brisk walk outdoors (preferred) or a second coffee (acceptable). She will not nap. Naps deliver her to that liminal half-sleep state where the depersonalization is worst and the intrusive imagery — Inferno fragments, the Phoenix-discharge moment, Nathan-as-infant — is most accessible. She has, file assesses, made a categorical decision against daytime sleep.

---

## 3. The Evening Architecture

Evenings are when the **person she has chosen to be** is most visible, because evenings are unstructured and she structures them anyway.

**18:00–19:30.** Decompression. She changes clothes — not into loungewear but into a *different* structured outfit, less formal but still composed. She cooks dinner more often than not, and cooks more elaborately than a single person needs to, regardless of whether she is currently partnered. The leftovers are managed competently; nothing is wasted. (The Anchorage domesticity was real even though it was built on false memory; she has kept it.)

**19:30–22:00.** **Reading.** This is the most consistent voluntary activity across her entire post-Phase-III existence. She reads broadly — fiction, history, tactical literature, occasional poetry. She holds books in her left hand and turns pages with the right; she dog-ears rather than uses bookmarks, which file notes as mildly out of character with her otherwise meticulous habits and assesses as a *deliberate* small disorder, a way of marking the book as *hers* by minor damage. She underlines in pencil. She talks back to the page under her breath — a quiet dry running commentary, occasionally a single short laugh.

**22:00–23:30.** Variable. Bath (long, hot, with the door open — same logic as the shower). Wine, one or two glasses, never more in routine periods. (Phase II shows heavier solitary drinking; she has consciously corrected this and the correction has held.) Music, low, instrumental more often than vocal — she does not want lyrics narrating her evening at her. If partnered, this is conversational time; she is a good late-night talker, dry and patient.

**Bedtime.** Nominal 23:30–00:30. Actual sleep onset variable. She does not perform sleep hygiene rituals beyond turning out lights; she does not meditate, does not journal, does not pray. She does, file infers, often lie awake for forty to ninety minutes in a state of composed wakefulness — not insomnia-as-distress but *vigil*. She has been resurrected enough times to find the act of yielding consciousness non-trivial.

---

## 4. The Week — Patterns at the Seven-Day Scale

A surveillance log over seven days would resolve the following:

- **Two to three nights of disturbed sleep**, with lights observed between 03:00 and 04:30, usually accompanied by reading, occasionally by quiet movement through the residence — she walks the perimeter of her own home in the dark, checking nothing in particular, an entirely automatic Marauder-aftermath behavior.
- **One full day of operational work** that runs long — fourteen to sixteen hours, with no real meal breaks, ending in either a sharp triumphant mood or an unusually flat one.
- **One day in which she does not leave the residence** voluntarily. This is not depression; it is restoration. She reads, cooks, listens to music, sometimes draws (she sketches — pencil, small format, never shows anyone, file infers from the presence of well-used pencils and the absence of visible product).
- **One outing to a public commercial space** — a bookstore, a market, occasionally a bar.
