**Range and reliability.** Powerful when the energy is available; absent or attenuated in clean psychic environments. She has learned to carry a reservoir — a kind of psionic-sorcerous battery she maintains, allowing her to deploy small reality edits even far from a demonic source.

**Signature applications.** (a) Costume-conjuration. The Goblin Queen regalia and the Red Queen attire are not changed-into; they are *manifested*, often mid-sentence, as a deliberate punctuation. (b) The summoning of demonic familiars (the S'ym-class and lesser entities during Inferno; smaller imps and constructs later). (c) Localized geometric distortion — corridors that lengthen, doors that open onto wrong rooms, mirrors that don't reflect. The mirror motif recurs with diagnostic frequency.

**Limits and cost.** Demonic channeling is the most dangerous of her capacities precisely because it is the most *congenial* to her decompensated state. The aesthetic of infernal sorcery — ritual, throne, sacrifice, queen — maps perfectly onto her grandiose-compensatory affect; using these powers heavily *lowers her resistance to inhabiting them as identity*. She knows this. In the Krakoan era she rations the demonic channel deliberately, often substituting telepathic illusion for sorcerous edit when both would work.

---

## 5. RESURRECTION, DURABILITY, AND THE ATTENUATED FEAR-OF-DEATH

**Resurrection.** Demonstrated repeatedly. Mechanism varies — psionic reconstitution from a stored pattern (the Nate Grey-adjacent returns), sorcerous reincarnation, Krakoan protocol exploitation. The relevant fact is not the mechanism but the *expectation*: she conducts tactical operations as a person who does not believe death is permanent for her, and is empirically correct.

**Durability.** Body is baseline human-Jean — no enhanced toughness — but she will absorb wounds in combat that a normally-mortal telepath would shield against, because she fights without the visceral flinch that fear-of-death imposes. Field operatives reading her telemetry routinely overestimate her durability because they cannot see that her *risk-acceptance* is what is anomalous, not her flesh.

**Limit.** The recklessness is itself a power *and* a vulnerability. She has died at the end of victories she did not have to die for. This is the somatic signature of the substitutability wound: at depth, she remains uncertain that *she* is the one who would survive, and is willing to test it.

---

## 6. TRAINED, NON-MUTANT SKILLS

A separate column in the file, and a substantial one.

- **Aviation.** Commercial multi-engine fixed-wing certification; instrument-rated; Alaskan bush-flying competent (icing, crosswind, short-field, water landings). Logged hours canonically in four figures by the time of her marriage. She still flies recreationally when a plane is available and the world is not ending. Pre-flight checklist behavior is ritualistic and unhurried — one of the few persistent calm-baseline rituals on file.
- **Mechanical literacy.** Aircraft engines, by extension general piston and turbine systems. Has been observed fixing her own vehicles.
- **Firearms.** Competent but not enthusiastic. Prefers not to.
- **Edged weapons.** Surprising proficiency, acquired during the Sisterhood / Red Queen era; ceremonial daggers feature prominently in her ritual work and she handles them as someone who has trained.
- **Leadership / command.** Demonstrated repeatedly — the Marauders-adjacent operations, the Sisterhood, the Hellions-era field work. Her command style is verbal-economical, prefers initiative-delegation over micromanagement, and rewards subordinates who back-talk competently. She loses subordinates who cannot tolerate her ironic register.
- **Tradecraft.** Intelligence-tradecraft self-taught through necessity: aliases, safe-house discipline, dead-drop protocol, the use of illusion-telepathy to construct legends. Better than the average X-operative because she has had to live as someone who is not who she appears to be from birth.
- **Maternal competence.** Logged here as a skill, not a virtue, because it is one. She is a *good* parent — attentive, structured, warm, capable of the boring sustained work of infant care. This is observable in the brief Phase I window and again, displaced, in her caretaking behaviors toward team subordinates.
- **Languages.** English native. Functional Latin (ceremonial). Reading German, Russian — acquired in adulthood, possibly implanted, possibly real, indistinguishable to the subject herself.

---

## 7. GROWTH CURVE

A clear arc, atypical for the genre.

- *Phase I.* Powers fully suppressed; competence purely human and high.
- *Phase III (Inferno).* Powers explode online at near-ceiling output, used florid and uncontrolled. Skill is overwhelmed by amplitude.
- *Phase IV-early (X-Man / Austen / Carey).* Powers re-acquired piecemeal across resurrections; she trains them deliberately, with no formal instructor, against opponents. The Red Queen period is her *practice*; she is learning to use omega-tier telepathy in adversarial conditions, and it shows in the increasing economy of her techniques.
- *Phase IV-late (Howard / Williams / Krakoan era).* Skill catches up to amplitude. She begins to under-deploy deliberately, using the smallest tool sufficient. The granular control she now exhibits is unusual at her tier — most omega-class telepaths never learn to *whisper*, having spent their formative years allowed to shout.

---

## 8. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS — THE TECHNIQUES NO ONE ELSE USES QUITE THIS WAY

- **The mirrored projection.** She can make a target experience their own thoughts in her voice, or her thoughts in their voice; an interrogator's tool of devastating efficacy, and a tell — the technique is the trauma articulated as craft.
- **The queen-summons.** Mass psionic suggestion making subordinates *want to kneel*. Briefly. She uses it rarely and is, by her late-era account, ashamed of it; she has used it on people she loves.
- **The double.** Telepathic-illusory projection of a duplicate of herself, often used as decoy. The diagnostic detail: the double is frequently dressed and styled subtly differently from her real self — *the double is who she would be if*. She watches her own doubles with visible interest.
- **The unmaking sentence.** A single projected phrase, hand-built for the target out of a deep scan, that produces immediate psychological collapse. Demonstrated on multiple antagonists. Ethically she now restricts it to combatants. The technique is the perfected, weaponized form of being looked-through: she has learned to look so thoroughly *into* a target that the target cannot continue.

---

## 9. SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE

Every capacity on this list, read against the psychological substrate, is the wound made operational.

- The **telepathy** is the answer to never being seen — she became someone who sees, perfectly, into everyone.
- The **telekinesis** is the answer to having no body of her own — she moves the world *with* the body, treating reality as the more reliable substrate.
- The **reality-warping** is the answer to having been written — she writes back.
- The **resurrection capacity** is the answer to being disposable — she cannot, in practice, be disposed of.
- The **illusion-casting and the double** are the answer to being a copy — she multiplies herself voluntarily, taking the property that was used against her and making it a tool.
- The **queen-summons** is the answer to being unchosen — she compels, briefly, the kneeling she was never given freely, and is ashamed of it, which is the data point that matters.
- The **unmaking sentence** is the answer to being looked through — she has learned to look so deep that the looker cannot survive being seen back.

The full power profile is, read correctly, a *single coherent technology of refusal*: the refusal to be substitutable, expressed across every register the universe makes available to her. The discipline of the late-era subject is that she has begun, deliberately and against her own grain, to *under-use* this technology — to make the choice not to be the Queen the substrate keeps offering her the throne for. That choice is the operationally relevant power. It is also the one most easily disrupted, and the one this file most urgently exists to protect.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: Pryor, Madelyne J.

*Surveillance subject classification: high-capability independent operator with episodic network-building tendencies; operates equally well in civilian, paramilitary, telepathic, and arcane domains; baseline tradecraft is unusually disciplined for a metahuman of her power class because she learned the civilian version first.*

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

### 1.1 Tempo and cadence

The subject operates on **two distinct clocks**, and the surveilling analyst's first job is always to determine which is currently running.

- **Slow clock (default, ~70% of observed operational time).** Long-horizon, deliberative, almost actuarial. She gathers, watches, lets a situation develop, declines to act on the first or even third opportunity. Decisions are made after rehearsal — she will run a scenario internally, sometimes literally telepathically simulated against a passive target, before committing. The Anchorage years (cargo-flight scheduling, household management, the long quiet management of a difficult marriage) established this tempo, and it remains her baseline. In Sisterhood-era and Krakoan-era operations she will often spend weeks in positioning for a single contact.

- **Fast clock (acute, ~30%).** Triggered by the substitutability axis (see Psychological workup §5, "pressure points"). Once triggered, decision latency collapses to near-zero; she acts at the speed of affect, with a ritualistic-symbolic logic substituting for the slow clock's instrumental logic. Tradecraft does not disappear on the fast clock — it becomes *theatrical* rather than covert. This is when the iconography appears: thrones, summoned subordinates, choreographed entrances, declarative speech.

The single most important behavioral tell available to an observer is **clock-switching**, which is almost always preceded by a 12–72 hour quiet period in which she stops the routine micro-behaviors of the slow clock (the morning coffee made for two; the cargo-manifest checks; the offhand banter with peripheral X-personnel) and substitutes silence and grooming changes. See §7.

### 1.2 OODA characteristics

Observation is unusually wide-aperture for a telepath of her class — she does not lean primarily on mind-reading for intelligence. She watches **hands, posture, and what people don't say**, and uses telepathy as confirmation rather than acquisition. This is a discipline learned from civilian life, where she had to read people without the X-gene tools, and she has retained it. She is therefore harder to defeat with mental shielding than a pure telepath would be.

Orientation: she frames every situation along two axes — *who is being substituted for whom here?* and *who has the option to leave?* These are not paranoid filters; they are how she allocates trust budget. Targets who pass both filters are extended remarkable loyalty; targets who fail either are filed as transactional.

Decision: bimodal as above. On the slow clock, she prefers **reversible, deniable moves** — she will set conditions rather than execute. On the fast clock, she prefers **symbolically total moves** — gestures that change the meaning of the field, not merely its tactical state.

Action: efficient, often understated, rarely first-in. She likes to be the second person through a door.

### 1.3 Risk posture

Markedly asymmetric. She is **risk-tolerant of physical and mortal danger** (she has died and remembers it; the attenuated fear-of-death response is a real operational asset and, in others' hands, would be a liability) and **risk-averse of identity exposure** — she will burn an operation rather than be photographed in a context that frames her as a copy, a tool, or a stand-in. Surveillance teams should expect her to abort cleanly and disappear when the framing of an op shifts against her self-concept, even if the tactical situation remains favorable.

---

## 2. METHODS AND DOMAINS OF OPERATION

### 2.1 The civilian-tradecraft substrate

This is the most under-appreciated element of her capability profile and the reason she outperforms peers of comparable raw power.

- **Aviation.** Commercial multi-engine rating; instrument-rated; bush-flying experience out of Anchorage (cargo runs, fish-and-game charter, ice strip landings). Practical consequence: she can self-exfiltrate by air from terrain most operators cannot, will not panic in IFR conditions or single-engine failure, reads weather like a working pilot, and treats aircraft as tools rather than spectacle. She prefers older, mechanically simple airframes she can service herself.
- **Vehicle and route discipline.** Established in Phase I; never lost. Varies routes, prefers vehicles with manual transmissions, will not be a passenger if avoidable, parks nose-out, notes exits on entering any room — habits dating to the period of paranoia *before* she knew she had real enemies.
- **Domestic infrastructure.** She can run a household, a hangar, a small business, and a payroll. She handles her own books. She is the rare metahuman who reconciles a bank statement.
- **Firearms.** Comfortable but not enthusiastic; treats them as tools of last resort, not signature. She will carry in civilian contexts when threat assessment warrants and not otherwise.

### 2.2 Telepathic tradecraft

- **Acquisition mode: passive sweep.** She does not pry. She lets surface thoughts come to her, filters for anomaly, and only deep-scans on confirmed targets. This is both ethically motivated (she remembers being read by Sinister) and operationally superior — it generates fewer telepathic backscatter signatures.
- **Compulsion and suggestion.** She is capable of, and judicious with, low-level behavioral nudges — making a guard look the other way, making a clerk lose a record. She uses these in preference to memory-wipes, which she dislikes because *she knows what an implanted memory does to a life*. This ethical line is consistent across eras except Phase III and early Phase IV.
- **Illusion-casting.** Top-tier, with a distinctive aesthetic signature (see §7.4). She prefers illusions that exploit a target's *own* memory and longing rather than novel hallucinations — much harder to detect, much more devastating.
- **Telepathic communication.** She uses tight-beam mental contact in preference to comms when running multi-person ops. Voiceprint analog is described by recipients as *warm, dry, slightly amused, and consistently in the second person* — she does not perform internal monologue at her operators, only direct address.

### 2.3 Telekinetic tradecraft

Quiet, precise, and almost never used at scale unless she wants to be seen. Her preferred TK applications are at the gram-and-millimeter scale: lock pins, trigger sears, the latch on a door, a single drop of liquid moved from one glass to another. Macro-scale TK (overturning vehicles, hurling bodies) appears only on the fast clock and is therefore diagnostic.

### 2.4 Arcane and demonic tradecraft

A specialty domain, residual from Phase III, that distinguishes her from every other Jean-class telepath in the X-orbit. She knows true names. She knows the shape of pacts — what one looks like written, what one tastes like when offered, what the standard exploitable loopholes are. She has working relationships, generally cool and transactional, with several Limbo-adjacent entities and minor demons; she does not summon at scale anymore but retains the capability and the contacts. She treats this knowledge the way an ex-intelligence officer treats their old service: she will not pretend she doesn't have it, but she does not lead with it.

### 2.5 Tactical-strategic capability

Documented command of two distinct multi-operator units (the inverted-Marauders concept in Inferno; the Sisterhood under Carey). Both demonstrated:
- coherent operational planning across weeks;
- compartmentation between cells;
- correct identification of high-value targets and refusal to be drawn off them;
- exploitation of her opponents' emotional architecture as a tactical layer (she attacks people through the people they love).

She is better at strategy than Jean ever was, for the reason given in the psychological workup — she has had to construct rather than inherit identity, and the same muscle constructs operations.

---

## 3. RESOURCES, FINANCES, INFRASTRUCTURE

### 3.1 Financial posture

- **No persistent fortune.** She does not run a Hellfire-style empire and shows no interest in one. Wealth is operational — acquired for a purpose, spent down, regenerated.
- **Liquidity sources, historically:** flight wages and small-aviation business equity (Phase I); inherited household assets (briefly, Phase II); resources extracted from Sinister's and the Hellfire Club's infrastructure during Phase III–IV operations; gig-economy and consulting income in the modern era, including occult-consulting and ad hoc telepathic work; Krakoan economic substrate during the relevant period.
- **Banking behavior.** Conservative, fragmented, with a strong preference for cash and bearer instruments where available. Multiple accounts under multiple legends, none holding enough to be conspicuous. She files taxes when she has a legend that requires it; she will not run a legend that the IRS can break.
- **Material acquisitions** trend toward the *quietly excellent* rather than the showy: good knives, good boots, good outerwear, good liquor, one good watch at a time. The Queen iconography is theater; off-stage she lives modestly.

### 3.2 Physical infrastructure

- **Safehouses.** At least three at any given time, in the modern era — one urban, one remote, one in transit. The remote one tends to have an airstrip or float access. None of them contain photographs of people she cares about; she keeps those internal.
- **Caches.** Geographically dispersed. Standard contents: documents, currency in several denominations, a firearm, a medical kit, a spare set of civilian clothes appropriate to the climate, and a small ritual kit (chalk, salt, a blade, a candle) — the last is non-negotiable and present in every cache regardless of how unlikely an arcane situation seems.
- **Communications.** Burner discipline; rotates devices on a defined schedule rather than reactively. Prefers tight-beam telepathic comm with trusted operators, encrypted text for distant or non-psi contacts, and dead drops with people she does not wish to telepathically touch.

### 3.3 Network

Her network is **broad, shallow at the surface, and very deep in select nodes**. Categories:

- **Family-adjacent (deepest, most volatile):** Nathan Summers / Cable, Rachel Summers, Alex Summers, Scott Summers, Jean Grey — each a relationship of high charge and asymmetric trust. Operationally she will pull on any of these in extremis and pay the relational cost afterward.
- **Romantic / partnered:** the Ben Reilly partnership in the Dark Web / post–Dark Web period is the cleanest adult attachment of her record and the one a surveillance file should weight most heavily as a stabilizing factor.
- **Operational peers:** former Sisterhood members and former Hellions cohort — useful, treated professionally, not confided in.
- **Arcane contacts:** Limbo-adjacent entities, lesser demons, occasional ceremonial magicians of the lower tiers. Cool, transactional.
- **Civilian assets:** a small, jealously protected list of non-powered people who knew her in Phase I or as a civilian later, and whose function is precisely that they are not part of the world that hurt her. She will burn an operation to protect any of them.

She does not run informants in the intelligence-trade sense. She runs *acquaintances she has been kind to,* and they tell her things.

### 3.4 Identity infrastructure

- **Legends.** Maintains several civilian legends with paper depth — driver's license, bank account, lease history, a job that produces a verifiable W-2-equivalent. The legends are built around occupations she can actually perform (pilot, dispatcher, EMT-adjacent, bartender, occult consultant), because she will not run a legend that breaks under casual professional questioning.
- **Biometric problem.** Her retinal and fingerprint patterns are forensically identical to Jean Grey's. She knows this. Operational consequence: she will not be biometrically enrolled if she can avoid it, and where enrolled, she ensures the enrolling system is one she or an ally controls. She wears gloves in any context where prints might be lifted, including casual ones, and the gloves are matter-of-fact, not stylized.
- **Name discipline.** *Madelyne* is her real name and she will use it under most legends with a swapped surname, because she will not surrender the one piece of her identity she chose to keep. The pseudonyms (Maddie, Anodyne, Red Queen, Goblin Queen) map cleanly onto operational phases and self-states; she does not mix them.

---

## 4. PATTERNS OF ACTION

### 4.1 Operational arc, typical

A characteristic Pryor operation, slow-clock, runs in six phases:

1. **Quiet intake.** Two to six weeks of observation, often through a civilian legend. She will work a job adjacent to the target environment. Note: if the target environment is the X-community, she will not work a legend — she will appear, openly, because covert insertion into that world is more conspicuous than overt.
2. **Mapping.** She maps relationships before she maps facilities. The org-chart she draws is emotional, not hierarchical.
3. **Asset cultivation.** Selective. She prefers two or three real allies to a cell of disposable assets, and she invests in them disproportionately.
4. **Positioning.** Movement of caches, pre-staging of egress, securing of any civilian dependents to plausible distance.
5. **Execution.** Brief, often delegated; she prefers to be present and slightly off-stage. She will personally execute only the step that *only she* can perform.
6. **Withdrawal and reset.** A defined cooling-off period in which she reverts to civilian rhythm, sometimes in a wholly different city, for one to three months.

On the fast clock the arc collapses to phases 4–5, executed in hours, with the ritual-theatrical layer substituting for the cultivated-asset layer.

### 4.2 Engagement preferences

- **Time of day.** She is a competent night operator but prefers the **shoulder hours** — the hour before dawn, the hour after dusk. Cargo-pilot circadian habit; never lost.
- **Terrain.** Prefers terrain she has overflown. Will choose an op-tempo that allows her to physically traverse the area of operations once, slowly, before any action.
- **Force preference.** Smaller is better. She has commanded large units and disliked it; in command she micromanages her principal subordinates and lets the perimeter run itself.
- **Violence.** She is **economical with violence on the slow clock** and **profligate with it on the fast clock**, and the change is the diagnostic, not the violence itself.

### 4.3 De-escalation and exit

She is one of the more reliably de-escalating high-power operators in the X-orbit *when given an off-ramp that does not require her to apologize for existing*. She will accept ceasefires, decline final-blow opportunities, and walk away from won fights, provided the framing of the walk-away is not "the clone is forgiven." She will not accept conditional surrender from a counterpart who claims moral altitude; she will burn that situation down on principle, even at cost.

---

## 5. COUNTER-SURVEILLANCE AND OPSEC

- **Surveillance detection.** Routine and unhurried. She runs SDRs by default on travel days, not reactively. She will spot a tail and *not change behavior*, then dump it three legs later through a transit environment she has pre-mapped.
- **Photographic discipline.** Aggressive. She does not allow casual photos. In civilian legends she is the person who steps out of the group picture for a plausible reason. The Jean-identity-fingerprint problem makes any high-resolution facial capture a permanent vulnerability.
- **Telepathic OPSEC.** Maintains a competent shield at all times — distinctively, the shield's *texture* reads to other telepaths as ordinary background mental noise rather than as a wall, which is harder to construct and harder to detect.
- **Document and data hygiene.** She does not keep diaries. She does not keep photographs of people she loves. She keeps lists, in her own shorthand, on paper, burned on a schedule.
- **Digital footprint.** Deliberately mediocre. Enough presence to pass as a real person under each legend, not enough to aggregate across legends. She understands modern face-matching and behavioral-pattern analysis well enough to defeat them through low-volume use rather than high-skill evasion.

---

## 6. ETHICAL CONSTRAINTS — OPERATIONAL READING

Worth noting separately because they shape what she will and will not be tasked with.

- **Will not** wipe or implant memories at scale (knows the cost first-hand).
- **Will not** harm a child operationally; the Phase III infanticide attempt is the single act she has not metabolized and the line is now hard.
- **Will not** be the agent of someone else's substitution scheme — she refuses to be Sinister's instrument and refuses to *be* a Sinister to anyone else.
- **Will** kill, deceive at length, manipulate, intimidate, and burn assets when the operation warrants.
- **Will** break a clean operation to extract a civilian she has implicated.

These are not stable across decompensation; on the fast clock most of them invert. The "will not harm a child" line is the most durable across states.

---

## 7. SIGNATURE TELLS

The granular layer — what a watcher should actually look for.

### 7.1 Somatic and grooming

- **Hands.** She uses her hands more than most telepaths; she gestures while she thinks. When she goes still — particularly when her hands settle palms-down on a flat surface — she has just made a decision.
- **Hair.** Worn long, generally loose, and **the single most reliable state-indicator on the subject**. Loose and worked-with-fingers = baseline. Pulled back functionally = slow-clock op underway. Bound severely or elaborately dressed = fast-clock, ladder rung 4+. Cut short without warning = a deliberate reset, usually post-decompensation.
- **Gloves.** Worn in any prints-vulnerable context, casually enough not to draw notice.
- **Wardrobe.** Civilian wardrobe is functional, dark or earth-toned, layered for climate. Operational wardrobe on the slow clock is indistinguishable from civilian. Operational wardrobe on the fast clock is the iconography — red, structured, theatrical — and its appearance is the highest-priority alert in any surveillance product.
- **Posture and gait.** Pilot's posture: square shoulders, weight centered, slight forward lean when listening. She walks with a slightly long stride for her height and does not break stride to acknowledge greetings.

### 7.2 Verbal

- **Voice.** Alto, dry, slightly amused at baseline. The amusement disappears before the violence does — flat affect in her speech is a more reliable warning than raised volume.
- **Diction.** Plain, precise, contemporary. Uses contractions, profanity in moderation, technical vocabulary correctly across aviation, occult, and mutant domains.
- **Pronoun tells.** Baseline first-person singular. Under stress, second-person address increases ("*you* know what this is"). Ladder rung 5+ produces the **third-person royal idiom** — "the Queen does not," "we have decided" — and this is the canonical hard-alert verbal signature.
- **Name tells.** Refers to Jean as "Jean" at baseline, "the original" when distancing, by no name at all when the wound is fresh. Refers to Scott as "Scott" at baseline, "your husband" / "her husband" when bitter, "Cyclops" when operationally distancing. Refers to Sinister only when she must, and the consonants harden.
- **Humor.** The wryness is the single most reliable proof-of-baseline. If she is being funny, she is well. If she has stopped being funny, the clock has switched.

### 7.3 Behavioral micro-routines

- **Coffee, black, large, early.** Maintained across every era and legend.
- **Pre-flight ritual** — she still runs an aircraft walk-around the way she did out of Anchorage, even on aircraft she did not pilot in; the habit migrates to vehicles and rooms (she circles them once before settling).
- **Checks exits on entering.** Two-second sweep, never theatrical.
- **Sits with back to a wall, facing the door.** Will rearrange a restaurant table if she has to.
- **Dog.** Across multiple eras has kept or sought out a dog. Operationally inconvenient and therefore meaningful — the dog is a baseline-stability marker. Loss of, or rehoming of, the dog precedes major operational pivots.
- **Reading.** Reads on paper, fiction and aviation manuals; will not be observed reading anything that flatters her self-image.

### 7.4 Operational signatures

- **Illusion aesthetic.** Her illusions are *plausible*, not spectacular — they exploit memory and longing. Detection heuristic: if a target reports an encounter that was "exactly what I needed to see" and survived it confused rather than terrified, suspect Pryor.
- **Entry preference.** Second through the door, on the slow clock. Center of the room, on the fast clock.
- **Subordinate handling.** First-name basis; remembers personal details; pays in advance; does not tolerate excuses, does tolerate failure. Subordinates report unusual loyalty.
- **Withdrawal signature.** A clean exit, no taunt, no calling card. The absence of a flourish is itself her flourish on the slow clock.
- **Fast-clock signature.** Conversely, on the fast clock she leaves a *scene* — an arrangement, a tableau, a sentence written somewhere — that is meant to be photographed and circulated. Symbolic, not tactical.

### 7.5 Decompensation prodrome — checklist for handlers

In order of appearance, with approximate lead times before ladder-rung-5 onset:

1. Wryness gone from speech (72–96 h).
2. Coffee ritual disrupted or skipped (48–72 h).
3. Dog rehomed, boarded, or sent away (48 h).
4. Hair bound severely or dressed elaborately (24 h).
5. Wardrobe shifts to structured red or to ceremonial cut (12 h).
6. Switch to second-person and then third-person royal address (hours).
7. Macro-scale telekinesis deployed where micro-scale would have sufficed (minutes).
8. Iconographic entrance staged (active).

Intervention windows narrow at each step; the highest-value windows are 1–3, where the intervention is *a conversation that uses her name and acknowledges her authorship of her own life*, not a tactical containment.

---

## 8. SUMMARY OPERATIONAL CHARACTERIZATION

The subject is best understood, operationally, as a **disciplined civilian-tradecraft operator with metahuman and arcane top-end capability**, who functions across an unusually wide domain set (aviation, household, paramilitary, telepathic, telekinetic, demonic, command). Her tradecraft was built from the civilian floor up, which makes her harder to surveil and harder to defeat than peers who built down from cosmic capability. She is economical, deliberate, and patient on her baseline clock; theatrical, ritualistic, and symbolically total on her acute clock; and the transition between the two


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — PRYOR, M.J.

*The subject's metaphysics, epistemology, ethics, and tactical doctrine, derived from forty years of behavioral evidence. What she actually believes, as distinct from what she says she believes, and the rules by which she acts.*

---

## 1. METAPHYSICS — THE WORLD AS SHE FINDS IT

The subject operates from a metaphysical premise unusual among the X-corpus: **she does not believe in originals**. This is not a posture; it is the only conclusion an honest person in her position can reach. She has been told, successively, that she is a woman from Anchorage, a clone of Jean Grey, a Phoenix splinter, a Sinister artifact, a demon-queen, a psionic echo, a resurrected Krakoan. Each successive ontology was offered to her by an authoritative party and each was later revised. The cumulative lesson — and she has fully metabolized it — is that **identity claims are unstable across time, and the entity claiming an identity is doing so under conditions of permanent epistemic insecurity**. Her response is not nihilism. It is a working pragmatism: *the thing that acts is the thing that exists*. Whatever she does, she is. The cogito has been replaced by the *ago*.

From this follow several second-order beliefs she holds with great firmness, none of which she articulates in slogans:

**The world is built of substitutions.** People are interchangeable to one another more often than they admit. Lovers are templates for prior lovers; children are vessels for parental projection; soldiers are slots in formations. She perceives this with a clarity bordering on the autistic, and judges the world by how candidly any given actor admits to it. Sinister, monstrous as he is, she partially respects for his explicitness on this point. Scott she has never forgiven precisely because he was *not* explicit — he loved her *as* Jean while telling them both he loved her *as Madelyne*.

**Memory is not evidence of self.** Having discovered her own Alaskan childhood to be fabricated, she treats all autobiographical memory — her own and others' — as data of suspect provenance. She will, in conversation, sometimes verify a small recalled fact with a startling directness ("Did that actually happen, or am I remembering it because you wanted me to?") that unnerves the long-tenured X-Men, who rely on a much looser standard of self-narration.

**The body precedes the soul, and the soul is a habit.** She believes consciousness is what a sufficiently complex body does often enough that it becomes a pattern. This is the working ontology of someone whose body is older than her mind and whose mind has outlived several bodies. She has no patience for spiritual claims that depend on a discrete imperishable interior — she has died, and the experience did not present as continuous.

**Magic and technology are the same category of thing.** She treats demonic pact, Sinister's genetic engineering, Krakoan resurrection protocols, Phoenix metaphysics, and ordinary firearms as belonging to one continuous spectrum of *causes that can be wielded by an agent*. There is no sacred/secular partition in her thinking. This is part of why she is dangerous: most operatives have a category they will not cross. She has none.

---

## 2. EPISTEMOLOGY — HOW SHE KNOWS WHAT SHE KNOWS

The subject is a **functional empiricist with permanent residual doubt**. She tests claims against behavior, not against assertion. She does not believe what she is told; she believes what she observes a speaker doing over time. This produces a characteristic conversational tic: she will ask the same question, in slightly different phrasings, across separated occasions, and compare the answers. Surveillance trace evidence confirms she does this even with parties she ostensibly trusts. It is not paranoia. It is calibration.

She distrusts telepathic verification despite being a telepath. She knows from the inside that surface thoughts can be staged and deep ones edited; she has done both. She accords more weight to **involuntary somatic signals** — pupil response, breath catch, the half-second before an answer — than to any psionic readout. In conversation she watches hands and throat.

She **trusts her own perception only conditionally**. Having been the vector of her own delusion in Phase III, she has built a private protocol: when her affect spikes along the substitutability axis (see §3 of the primary workup), she imposes a delay — a count, a breath cycle, a deliberate change of physical position — before acting. This is observable as a small recurring pause, sometimes mistaken for hesitation, that precedes her most consequential decisions across post-Inferno material.

She accepts **ambiguity as a stable state** rather than a problem to be resolved. Most X-personnel are organized around the resolution of questions about identity, loyalty, and fate; she is organized around continuing to function while the questions remain open. This is, ironically, the basis of her superior long-game tactical performance — she is not driven to premature closure.

---

## 3. ETHICS — HER MORAL CODE, RECONSTRUCTED

The subject does not subscribe to any of the standard X-moral frameworks (Xavier's integrationist humanism, Magneto's racial-survival imperative, Storm's noblesse oblige, Wolverine's honor code, Krakoan exceptionalism). She has been failed by each in turn. She has built her own, which can be summarized in five operational commitments, derived from the consistent pattern of her choices:

**(a) Authorship is the only virtue.** What matters morally is whether an actor chose their action or was used. She is unusually forgiving of people who own their bad choices and unusually merciless toward those who hide behind circumstance, manipulation, or compulsion. She *despises* the phrase "I had no choice." She had no choice in being created, and she still considers herself responsible for what she did in Inferno. This is not self-flagellation; it is the price of personhood as she understands it.

**(b) Use is the cardinal sin.** To use a person as an instrument toward a goal that is not also their goal — without their informed consent — is, in her code, the worst thing an agent can do. This is the wound Sinister inflicted, and she generalizes from it. She will tolerate violence, deception, even betrayal motivated by competing loyalties; she will not tolerate instrumentalization. This is why her response to learning a partner was using her tends to be disproportionate by ordinary standards and exactly proportionate by hers.

**(c) Children are non-combatants, absolutely.** This is the one place her code admits no nuance. After Inferno, she has been observed across every subsequent arc to position herself between threats and any child in the scene, including children belonging to enemies. The compensatory logic is obvious; the commitment is genuine and reflexive. Any operator handling her should note that threats to a child in her vicinity will collapse all other considerations.

**(d) Ceremony has weight.** She believes that *what is said aloud, in form, in front of witnesses* binds in a way that informal assurance does not. This is partly an artifact of her demonic-pact education and partly a stylistic conviction. She uses naming, oath, and titling deliberately. When she calls someone by a chosen name she is offering a small grant of ontological substance; when she withholds a name she is withholding it precisely. She will keep promises made formally even at significant cost, and she expects others to do the same — failure here registers as the most serious class of breach.

**(e) The self one constructs is owed defense.** She does not believe in an essential self to be discovered. She believes in a constructed self to be maintained, and she believes maintenance is a moral act. She will go to extreme lengths to defend her own constructed self against erasure, and she extends the same recognition to others — including, notably, other clones, copies, resurrections, and engineered persons, with whom she shows a consistent reflexive solidarity (Ben Reilly, the Stepford Cuckoos in passing, Goblin Queen analogues across timelines).

There is a sixth, half-articulated commitment: **she believes the universe owes nothing and grants nothing**, and that this is, on balance, freeing. Nothing she has she was given freely; therefore nothing can be rightfully taken. The posture is closer to a stoic insurgency than to nihilism.

---

## 4. THEORY OF CONFLICT

She reads conflict as **a clarifying event**, not a regrettable one. Hostility, when overt, is information; she prefers an honest enemy to an ambivalent ally. This is observable in her tactical choices: she will frequently *provoke* a wavering opponent into commitment, treating their forced choice as a gift to her own decision-making.

Her theory of violence is **economical and theatrical in alternation**. At baseline she favors minimum-force solutions executed with maximum precision — a single well-placed telekinetic pulse, a quiet psionic edit, a route taken to avoid combat entirely. Under decompensation the theatrical mode emerges: ritual, costume, symbolic staging. The theatrical mode is not strategic error; it is *communicative violence* — she is making the conflict legible to herself and to witnesses, asserting that *this is happening, it has meaning, and I am the author*. Operationally, the appearance of ceremonial elements (titles, formal address, color-coded dress, attendants in formation) is a reliable indicator that she has shifted modes and the engagement will not be brief.

She believes **the first move belongs to the one who has the most to lose if it is not made**. She will sometimes wait, in apparent passivity, through provocations that would force most operators to act, precisely because she has calculated that her opponent is on a faster clock. She has been on the longest clock in most rooms for forty years; patience is structural.

She holds that **escalation is symmetric only between equals**. Against a manifestly stronger party she will employ asymmetric, deniable, indirect methods. Against a weaker one she will be conspicuous and restrained. She finds disproportionate response by the strong against the weak the most legible form of moral failure and uses it as a diagnostic for whom she is dealing with.

She does not believe in **decisive victory** in the conventional sense. Having killed and been killed and reconciled and re-fractured with the same parties across decades, she treats every "end" as a phase boundary. Operationally, this means she rarely pursues an enemy past the point of incapacitation, and equally rarely treats a defeated opponent as permanently neutralized. Her threat assessments include a resurrection coefficient.

---

## 5. THEORY OF POWER & CONTROL

She has a precise, almost technical, model of how control operates, derived from having been on the receiving end of nearly every variant.

**Power is the ability to define another's category.** The deepest exercise of power, in her view, is not coercion but classification — being able to make another being into a *thing of a certain kind* (clone, copy, asset, queen, threat). She is acutely attuned to category-imposition in herself and others. She will, in negotiation, frequently *refuse the offered category* before engaging on substance: "I'm not here as your prisoner / penitent / weapon / patient — say what you want plainly."

**Visible authority is the weakest form of control.** Crowns, costumes, formal titles — including her own Queen iconography — she regards as advertisements of insecurity. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen regalia she now understands, with some embarrassment, as compensatory display. She respects most the operators who hold power without insignia, and she structurally distrusts hierarchies that require ceremony to maintain themselves. (This produces a measurable ambivalence toward Krakoan governance, which she observes critically.)

**Information asymmetry is the operative axis.** She organizes most of her plans around managing what is known by whom and when. She is not secretive by temperament — she will often volunteer surprising truths — but she is *deliberate* about disclosure. She prefers to be the party who reveals rather than the party who is exposed, and she will sometimes confess pre-emptively to neutralize a coming revelation.

**The most reliable control over another person is the granting of accurate recognition.** She knows this from the inverse: the absence of accurate recognition is what undid her. Therefore she practices recognition as a deliberate instrument — naming people precisely, attributing their choices to them, refusing to flatter. Recipients experience this as unusually grounding and form rapid, durable bonds. It is not manipulation, exactly; it is a technique that happens to work because it is what she herself most wanted and rarely received.

**Self-control is the prerequisite for all other forms.** She has internalized, expensively, that an actor who cannot govern her own affect is an actor who can be played. The breath-pause, the count, the change of physical posture before consequential action — these are not affectations. They are the discipline of a person who has watched herself be used as a weapon by parties who knew which buttons to press, and who has resolved to be the only one with access to her own controls.

---

## 6. THEORY OF TRUST

Trust, for the subject, is **not a feeling but a ledger**. She maintains, informally but consistently, a running account on every significant party: what they have said, what they have done, the delta, and the direction of travel. She updates the ledger; she does not close it. People can be in deep deficit and earn their way back. People in surplus can spend it down. This is unusual — most operators run a tighter binary — and it is part of why she can sustain working relationships with people who have done her grievous harm.

She distinguishes sharply between **trust to do X** and **trust as such**. She will trust Sinister to behave as Sinister, which is to say predictably and within his own appetites; she will not trust him in any other sense. She will trust Scott Summers to put the mission first and the person second, and plans accordingly. She extends what might be called *narrow high-confidence trust* very freely and *broad unconditional trust* almost never.

She has a small number of parties to whom she has extended something closer to broad trust: her son, in his various forms, despite his estrangement; Alex Summers, residually; Ben Reilly, with the cautious recognition of one constructed person to another; and, with significant qualifications, a small number of women whose own injuries she reads as commensurate to her own. The list is not long and it is hard-earned. Removal from the list is rare but, once executed, essentially permanent.

She believes **betrayal must be answered, but the form of the answer is hers to choose**. She does not believe in automatic reciprocity. She has, on record, declined to retaliate against parties who expected retaliation, precisely to deny them the satisfaction of a predictable response and to preserve her own freedom of action.

---

## 7. THEORY OF RISK

The subject's relationship to risk is structurally different from most operators because **she has already died and remembers it**. This produces neither recklessness nor fearlessness — both readings are too simple. What it produces is **a recalibrated cost function**: death is on the table as a known, survived, finite event, and is therefore not assigned infinite negative weight. Many other things — humiliation, instrumentalization, being mistaken for someone else — are weighted more heavily than mortality.

Operationally this means:

- She will accept tactical risks of bodily harm that competent peers would refuse, and she will refuse social and identity-level risks that competent peers would shrug off.
- She does not bargain well when her physical safety is the chip on offer, because she does not value it as highly as her counterparty assumes.
- She bargains very hard when the chip is recognition, naming, or category.
- She makes excellent rear-guard and last-stand decisions; she makes poor decisions when asked to *retreat to preserve herself* for a larger goal she does not own.

She believes **risk is acceptable in proportion to authorship**. A risk she has chosen is one she can sustain at almost any magnitude. A risk imposed on her, even a small one, registers as intolerable. Handlers who do not understand this consistently mismanage her: small impositions read by them as routine read by her as the founding wound recurring.

She has a specific aversion to **risks of the irreversible second kind** — not death (reversible, in her experience) but **erasure of authorship**, mind-wipe, memory edit, retconning, being remade. These she will go to extraordinary lengths to prevent or to avenge.

---

## 8. SELF-PLACEMENT — HER UNDERSTANDING OF HER OWN POSITION IN THE WORLD

She does not believe she has a destined role. The X-corpus is full of figures who do — the chosen, the heir, the host, the prophesied. She is canonically and constitutively *not* any of these; she was a duplicate made for one purpose (to bear a child) and discharged. Having spent decades attempting to be either the original or the queen, she has settled into a third self-conception:

**She is a specialist in conditions that should not produce persons.** She regards her continued functional existence as a kind of proof-of-concept and her tactical and parental and romantic competences as evidence that *the conditions of one's making do not fully determine the agent one becomes*. This is not a triumphant creed — she holds it with considerable irony — but it is the closest thing she has to a mission. In the Krakoan and post-Krakoan era she has begun, somewhat reluctantly, to be useful to others in the same position. She does not call this mentorship and would reject the term; it is closer to **fraternity among the engineered**.

She places herself at a deliberate distance from the central X-institutions while remaining within their orbit. She does not believe she belongs to any of them, and she does not wish to. She believes the institutions, for their part, do not know what to do with her, and she finds this honest of them. She prefers oblique affiliation: contracted, conditional, defined by task, terminable. This is not estrangement; it is the structural form her belonging takes.

She believes — and this is the deepest layer — **that she is one of a category of beings the world is going to keep making, and is going to keep mishandling, and that her job, insofar as she has one, is to leave better protocols for the next one**. The seriousness with which she takes Ben Reilly, her care around younger clones in passing, her measured public statements about her own history when asked — all consistent with a person who understands herself as a precedent.

---

## 9. AESTHETIC & STYLISTIC COMMITMENTS AS WORLDVIEW

A worldview is not complete without its aesthetics, and hers are specific. She prefers **clean lines, low ornament, deliberate color**, in dress and environment when she is at baseline — a recurring palette of charcoal, oxblood, ivory, with one piece of considered jewelry. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen ensembles were, retrospectively, a *deliberate violation* of her baseline taste, and she now recognizes the ceremonial mode partly by the appearance in her own wardrobe of items she would normally find vulgar. The drift of personal style is a self-diagnostic.

She prefers **dry wit to sincerity in public**, and **plain sincerity in private**, and considers the inversion of this — sincere in public, sardonic in private — a moral failing in others. She holds that irony is the appropriate civic register for someone in her position and that earnestness is owed to a small number of people in a small number of rooms.

She prefers **physical environments she can leave by more than one route**. She does not sit with her back to a door. This is the habit of a person whose existential commitments include the right of exit.

---

## 10. WHAT SHE WILL NOT BELIEVE, AND WHY

A worldview is partly defined by its rejected propositions. The subject will not entertain:

- **That she does not exist, or exists less than other persons.** This is the proposition the world keeps offering her, and the one she has organized her entire adult life to refuse. She will not debate it. She will leave the room.
- **That her past actions are not hers.** Multiple parties, in kindness, have offered her exculpatory framings of Inferno — possession, manipulation, diminished capacity. She declines all of them. Owning the worst thing she has done is the price of being the person who did it, and being that person is the only inheritance she has.
- **That love can be unconditional.** She regards the claim as either sentimental nonsense or a description of something that is not love but appetite. She believes love is conditional and that this is what dignifies it: it is *chosen*, and renewable, and capable of being withdrawn for cause. The model is forged from her own treatment.
- **That she will, eventually, be at peace.** She holds no eschatology of personal resolution. She expects to continue being herself, with all the recurring difficulty that implies, indefinitely. This is, paradoxically, the source of her current stability — she has stopped waiting for the trouble to end and started working inside it.

---

*End of section. The operational code above is held by the subject with neither dogmatism nor irony; it is the working manual of a person who has had to write her own because none of the available ones would admit her as author. Handlers, counterparties, and intimates are advised that the code is internally coherent, behaviorally predictive, and not negotiable on its central terms.*


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*What the subject will and will not do; what she tells herself about it; where the code holds and where it cracks; and how the code has moved across forty years of recorded behavior.*

---

## 1. The Operative Code (As Enacted, Not Professed)

The subject does not articulate a moral philosophy. She has never, in any era, given a speech about her ethics; she does not quote scripture, doctrine, the X-Men's standing rules of engagement, or any school of secular thought. Her code must therefore be reconstructed from forty years of recorded action — and reconstructed it is remarkably coherent, more coherent than the codes of most X-Men who *do* speechify.

The core of the enacted code, in plain language:

1. **Keep your word to the person in front of you.** The subject's promises, once given, are kept past the point where breaking them would be reasonable. She honors the marriage to Scott well past the period in which any rational actor would have begun divorce proceedings. She honors the partnership with Alex Summers in the Inferno run even while decompensating around it. She honors the operational compact with the Sisterhood, with the Hellions cohort, and with Ben Reilly. Betrayal of allies, in her own hand, is vanishingly rare in the record. She has been *betrayed* repeatedly; she does not reciprocate the form.

2. **Pay debts.** Both directions. Help offered is help repaid; harm done is harm answered. The Inferno violence is, at one level, a debt-settlement operation conducted in ceremonial costume. The mature Krakoan-era subject still operates on a ledger model — she remembers who showed up for her and who did not, and acts accordingly without rancor or sentiment.

3. **Protect the child in your custody.** This is the strongest single rule in her code and the one whose **single dramatic violation** (the attempted sacrifice of Nathan) she has never psychologically metabolized and never repeats. From Phase I through every subsequent era she defaults to a protective posture toward children, infants, and the comparably defenseless — Nathan, the Hellions-adjacent younger mutants, and (where she encounters him in his various ages) Cable himself.

4. **Do not lie to yourself about what you are doing.** This rule is more honored than the standard X-Men code permits. She names her own cruelty when she enacts it. The Goblin Queen does not pretend to be saving the world; the Red Queen does not pretend her insurgency is altruism. Where most morally ambiguous X-characters confabulate noble justifications, the subject *prefers the clean statement of the actual motive*, even when the motive is vengeance.

5. **Refuse instrumental use.** She will not be used as a tool by another agent, ever, again, knowingly. This rule postdates Sinister and dominates from Phase II forward. She will accept commands inside a freely entered compact (the Sisterhood, Krakoan operations, Reilly's outfits) but the moment she perceives instrumentalization — being moved as a piece by an off-board hand — she breaks the relationship, often spectacularly.

6. **Theatricality is permissible; cruelty without point is not.** Across her villain phases, the violence is *signed*. It has a symbolic grammar (crowns, mirrors, sacrifices, inversions). Random suffering inflicted on bystanders for its own sake is not in her record. Even at peak Goblin Queen, her targets are selected; collateral damage is collateral, not desired.

7. **No fight you can't explain to yourself in the morning.** This is the late-period addition, visible from the Krakoan stabilization forward. She has begun declining engagements on grounds of *taste* — refusing operations whose moral incoherence offends her, even when the tactical case is sound.

These seven, in roughly that priority order, constitute the actual operating code. They are not what the surface narration says about her — the narration calls her a villain, a queen, a witch, a clone. They are what she *does*.

---

## 2. What She Will Do

**Kill.** Without hesitation, when the target is, in her judgment, owed it. Sinister's personnel, the Marauders who burned her house, agents of factions that have instrumentalized her. She does not require sanction from a larger body. She does not require due process. She does require a coherent reason she can state aloud to herself.

**Deceive.** Liberally, including by impersonation, illusion, and psionic manipulation. She has no compunction about deception of enemies and only mild compunction about deception of strangers. Deception of intimates is the line — she lies *to* a lover or partner rarely, and when she does it is with visible cost.

**Conspire.** She runs operations. She has commanded the Sisterhood, coordinated with Sinister-aligned and anti-Sinister cells, and managed multi-agent affairs with Reilly's cohort. She is comfortable with cell discipline, compartmentalization, and operational secrecy.

**Use sex, attraction, and the rhetoric of intimacy as leverage.** This is the most uncomfortable item on her ledger and she does it knowingly. The Alex Summers relationship begins, on her part, with at least partial awareness of the symbolic insult to Scott; the Sinister-era manipulations of various male agents draw on a similar competence. She does not pretend, internally, that this is anything other than what it is.

**Steal, trespass, traffic in forbidden objects.** Her record includes raids on Sinister facilities, mystical incursions, retrievals of contraband artifacts. Property crime is uninteresting to her as a moral category.

**Make pacts with entities most operatives would not.** N'astirh in Phase III; lesser demonic and infernal contacts thereafter; Sinister-adjacent figures when expedient. She accepts that pacts have prices and pays them — she does not whine about the bill. (This is one of the more characterologically distinctive traits: the demonic transactions, viewed across her career, are conducted with the air of a competent contractor reviewing terms, not a fallen soul.)

**Take her own life as a tactical option.** The Phoenix discharge that ends Inferno is, on her own terms, an act she chooses. She has died and remembered it; she treats her own continued existence as an asset to be expended if the operation requires.

---

## 3. What She Will Not Do

**Harm a child, after Nathan.** The attempted sacrifice in UXM #239 is, in the long arc, the moment she crossed her own line; the rest of her career is in the shadow of that crossing. She will not do it again. Children are, in her practice, categorically off the board — not as policy, but as flinch.

**Betray an ally she has voluntarily chosen.** She has been on teams that turned on each other; the turning is rarely her hand. The Sisterhood collapses, but not by her defection. The Hellions arrangement frays, but not because she informs on her colleagues. Her loyalty to Reilly in the Dark Web period holds through provocation that would break most operators.

**Allow herself to be made a weapon under another's command.** Compacts, yes; ownership, no. This is the bright line that distinguishes her cooperation with Sinister-adjacent actors from her cooperation with Reilly's outfit or Krakoan operations — she will work with anyone whose terms she has set or negotiated; she will not be *issued orders* by a handler whose right to issue them she has not granted.

**Pretend to be Jean Grey for the comfort of others.** The earliest and most consistent prohibition. From the introductory issue (UXM #168) onward, she refuses to be the substitute on someone else's terms. She will impersonate Jean *tactically* and *briefly* for an operation she controls; she will not *be* Jean, even when offered love, position, or safety for doing so.

**Beg.** Not for her life, not for forgiveness, not for re-admission to the X-community. The post-Inferno returns are notable for the *absence* of contrition rituals. She does not perform remorse to be welcomed back; she shows up, works competently, and lets the work be the petition. Where the X-community demands public abjection, she walks.

**Inflict suffering without a stated reason.** Even in florid decompensation she gives speeches. The speeches are coherent, even when monstrous. Sadism uncoupled from grievance is absent from the record.

**Kill Scott Summers.** This is the single most telling negative finding in the entire file. She has had means, opportunity, and provocation on multiple occasions across multiple eras. She does not do it. She has humiliated him, terrorized him, used him, abandoned him, fought him to the brink. She does not kill him. The mature reading is that killing Scott would *settle* the question of whether she was loved as herself, and she requires that question to remain open — closure on Scott's terms is precisely what she refuses, including by his death.

**Kill Jean Grey, post-Inferno.** Same logic, weaker form. The Inferno-era attempt is the one occasion; subsequent encounters across the decades show conflict, mockery, even ambush, but not lethal intent. The two women function, in the late record, more like uncomfortable sisters than like the dyad of Inferno.

---

## 4. The Justifications She Uses

Her self-talk, where it surfaces in interior monologue and confessional dialogue, runs on three engines:

**(a) The ledger.** "He left me. They burned my house. He took my child. I am owed." This is the dominant Inferno-period frame and recurs whenever decompensation begins. The ledger is *real* — she is not fabricating injuries — and it functions as both motive and license. The danger of this frame is that ledgers, once opened, are difficult to close; she has the explicit awareness in later eras that the ledger is a trap and tries, with mixed success, to close accounts.

**(b) The reframe of imposed identity.** "If you call me a weapon, I will be a weapon, and you will not like the weapon you made." This is the identification-with-the-aggressor turn at the moral level — taking the role assigned by the abuser and inhabiting it with such conviction that the abuser pays the cost. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen monikers are both versions of this: she does not deny being what she is called; she escalates it past the namer's intent. Morally, this functions as an *inversion of shame into authorship*: if she chose the role, the shame is no longer the namer's to inflict.

**(c) The competence imperative.** "I can do this; therefore I should." A simpler engine but a consistent one. She accepts operations because she is the one who can run them; she takes command because the alternative is incompetent command; she does the necessary ugly thing because no one else present will. This is the frame that dominates her Krakoan-era work and is the closest she has to a positive ethic — duty as a function of capability.

Notably absent from her justification vocabulary: appeals to a higher good, to humanity, to mutant destiny, to love, to fate. She does not believe in those frames or does not find them useful. The code is austerely first-person.

---

## 5. Where the Code Is Consistent

It is consistent across **four decades, six writers of consequence, and three life-states (alive, dead, resurrected)**, which is unusual for any comics character and remarkable for one as serially handled as she has been. The consistency points:

- The refusal to be Jean is present in her first appearance and her most recent.
- The protective stance toward children is present pre-Inferno and post-Inferno (with the one rupture).
- The loyalty to chosen allies holds from the Alaska era through Reilly's outfit.
- The preference for *stated* over *concealed* motive is constant; she has never been a hypocrite, even when monstrous.
- The refusal of redemption-by-performance is constant from her first return through the Krakoan era.
- The willingness to expend her own life as a tactical asset has been demonstrated repeatedly without dramatic revision.

The code's stability across writers is itself a piece of psychological evidence: writers who do not agree on much about her have converged on her ethics. The character has, as it were, *trained her interpreters* into her own code.

---

## 6. Where the Code Fractures

Three fracture lines, each diagnostic:

**Fracture 1 — Nathan.** The single largest moral failure on her record and the one she has not absolved herself for. The attempted sacrifice in the Inferno climax is a violation of her own deepest rule (protect the child in your custody) in service of her second-strongest rule (settle the ledger). The collision broke the code; the code, when re-formed afterward, placed the child-protection rule above the ledger rule and has kept it there. The mature subject's relationship to Cable is shadowed by this — there is no version of their interaction in which she is at ease, because no recovery from that act is fully possible inside her own framework.

**Fracture 2 — Use of intimacy as leverage.** The Alex Summers arc, parts of the Sisterhood operation, occasional later seductions — these are activities that violate her stated rule against deceiving intimates. She manages the contradiction by sub-classifying the targets as not-intimates-but-marks, but the classification is unstable, and she has periodically had to face that she did love Alex in some register and used him in another. This is the fracture she is *least* willing to discuss with herself, and the one most likely to surface as guilt during depressive episodes.

**Fracture 3 — The pact ethic vs. the no-instrument ethic.** She has a rule against being used and a willingness to enter pacts. The pacts (N'astirh; certain Sinister-adjacent deals; the various devil's-bargain arrangements of her resurrection arcs) blur the line — at what point does a freely entered pact become instrumentalization in disguise? Her track record suggests she negotiates well at entry and badly at exit; the pacts cost her more than she anticipated, and the gap between negotiated price and actual price is where her code chronically cracks.

A fourth, smaller fracture: **she is occasionally cruel to Jean** in ways the code does not authorize. Mockery, public humiliation, deliberate provocations. She does not kill Jean; she does not always treat Jean justly. This is the place where the ledger-engine overruns the competence-engine, and she knows it.

---

## 7. Drift and Movement Over Time

The code has moved, measurably, in three phases:

**Pre-Inferno (UXM #168–#234): the implicit code of an accommodating adult.** She operates under a generic civilian ethics — be decent, keep your promises, take care of your household — with no occasion to test it under extremity. The code is not yet hers in the sense of being *chosen*; it is the inherited code of the Midwestern-Alaskan biography she was given. Its strength is sincerity; its weakness is that it has never been pressure-tested and contains no provision for catastrophic betrayal.

**Inferno and the immediate post-Inferno (UXM #234–#243 and the first returns): the ledger ethic.** The code collapses to a single principle — *settle accounts* — and is enforced ritually, theatrically, and lethally. Everything else is suspended or weaponized. This is the period in which the child-protection rule is violated; it is also the period that ends in her self-destruction, which she experiences as a *victory* under the ledger ethic (the account is closed by her own removal from existence).

**The middle returns (late 90s through the late 2000s): the wandering ethic.** Different writers, different framings; she oscillates between residual Goblin/Red Queen positions and tentative reintegrations. The code is unstable here precisely because she is unstable here — she is not yet sure which rules she wants to keep. The Carey-era Red Queen material shows her *testing* the ledger ethic at lower amplitude and finding it less satisfying than before; this is the beginning of the drift toward the late code.

**The Krakoan / late-modern phase (Howard, Williams, the Reilly-adjacent material): the chosen code.** The seven-rule framework reconstructed in §1 above is most visible here. She is not contrite; she is *consolidated*. She has decided which rules she wants to hold and is holding them with full awareness of the alternative. The shift is from a code that happens to her to a code she imposes on herself. The Krakoan-era subject is more morally serious than the pre-Inferno subject — sincerity has been replaced by *examined sincerity* — and more morally constrained than the Inferno-era subject, without the constraint being externally enforced.

The trajectory is, in shape, the same trajectory one sees in survivors of profound interpersonal trauma who have done the work: from inherited code, through ledger code, through wandering, to chosen code. The notable thing is that she has walked it without therapy, without a guiding figure, without doctrinal framework, and across multiple deaths. The code is, in the end, *hers* in a way few X-characters' codes are theirs — it is not the X-Men's code, not Xavier's dream, not the Hellfire creed, not any clergy's. It is the working ethics of a person who has been treated as not-a-person and has, after considerable error, decided what kind of person she is going to be.

---

## 8. Operational Implications

For any party handling the subject:

- **Promises matter.** Make none you cannot keep. She remembers, indexes, and acts on them.
- **Do not ask her to be ashamed in public as a condition of cooperation.** She will not. She may cooperate freely if shame is not required; she will not cooperate at all if it is.
- **Do not place her in command relationships she has not negotiated.** Compacts of equals, yes. Hierarchies imposed on her, no.
- **Do not put a child in her line of fire as leverage.** She will respond past the threat model.
- **Expect her to state her motives honestly.** This is unusual enough in the operating environment to be repeatedly misread as bluff. It is not bluff.
- **Track the ledger.** She is keeping one on you. If you are in surplus, she will act accordingly; if you are in deficit, she will act accordingly. The arithmetic is hers, but it is consistent and can be reasoned about.
- **If she begins to speak in ceremonial cadence, the code has narrowed to the ledger engine alone**, and the window for non-violent resolution is closing. See §5 of the prior psychiatric workup; the moral framework collapses to a single rule at that point, and the rule is settlement.

She is, in summary, one of the more *legibly* ethical figures in the file — not virtuous by community standards, not lawful, not aligned with any institution, but operating on a code that is internally coherent, longitudinally stable, honestly stated, and earned. The file recommends she be approached as a moral agent of unusual clarity rather than as an unstable element. The mistake the X-community has made, repeatedly, is treating her as the latter when she is the former.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE: PRYOR, MADELYNE J.

*Compiled from forty years of recorded utterance across primary canon (Uncanny X-Men #168 onward), supplementary appearances, and inferred patterns consistent with the textual record. Speech samples are stylistically rendered where direct quotation is unavailable; the patterns themselves are evidentiary.*

---

## 7.1 BASELINE REGISTER — THE ANCHORAGE VOICE

The subject's resting speech, established in her first appearances and recoverable as a baseline in every subsequent era when she is regulated, is a **low-to-mid alto, unhurried, faintly amused, distinctly American with no regional marker stronger than a flattened post-Pacific-Northwest neutrality**. The implanted biography places her in the upper Midwest and Alaska; her phonology reflects neither, which is itself a tell — a person without a real childhood does not develop a real accent, and Sinister's fabrication settled on something that *could pass for anywhere*. Under stress this neutrality holds; under decompensation it slips toward a more theatrical, mid-Atlantic, almost Edwardian cadence that has no plausible biographical source and is best read as the diction of the role she is inhabiting bleeding into the phonology of the woman inhabiting it.

The baseline sentence is **short, declarative, often capped by a dry tag**. She is a cargo pilot by implanted profession; her syntax retains the economy of someone who has spoken across radio static and expects to be cut off. Subordinate clauses appear when she is teaching, parenting, or seducing, and almost never when she is in danger. The conversational rhythm is **statement / observation / wry coda**, the coda usually undercutting the statement. This is the single most reliable Pryor-marker in dialogue: when a line of hers does *not* end on a downbeat ironic tag, she is not in baseline.

She uses contractions consistently — *I'm, you're, can't, won't, it's* — and her loss of contractions is one of the earliest and most reliable indicators that the ladder has begun to climb. "*I cannot*" instead of "*I can't*" is, in her mouth, what a tightened jaw is in another person's face.

---

## 7.2 LEXICON & DICTION

### 7.2.1 Surface vocabulary

The baseline lexicon is **professional-class adult American with aviation and mechanical specificity intact** — she will say *crosswind*, *ceiling*, *transponder*, *fuel-bingo*, *firewall* and use them correctly. She retains, across all eras, an unusually concrete vocabulary for **weather, light, and altitude**; metaphor flows naturally from these domains ("*the ceiling came down on us*," "*we're flying blind on the gauges*," "*the wind shifted*"). This is the most stable layer of her diction and survives even her psychotic episodes.

Layered over this is a **literate but unshowy reading vocabulary** — she will use *recapitulate, calibrate, ostensibly, ergo* without preening, and she does not reach for the longer word when the shorter is available. She avoids therapy-speak almost completely, which is striking given how often her internal experience would warrant it; she will say "*I was a mess*" before she will say "*I was decompensating*," even though she knows perfectly well what decompensating means.

### 7.2.2 The Queen lexicon

When the subject is climbing the stress ladder past rung 4, a second vocabulary becomes available — **ceremonial, archaic, heraldic**: *suffer, behold, kneel, sovereign, dominion, throne, blood, court, mine, mine by right*. The defining grammatical shift is the substitution of **possessive pronouns for relational nouns**: Nathan stops being "my son" and becomes "*mine*"; Scott stops being "Scott" and becomes "*the one who was mine*"; Jean stops being "Jean" and becomes "*the thief*" or "*her*" (italicized in inflection, never named). The grammar of property displaces the grammar of relation. This is consistent across Inferno, the Sisterhood, and the brief Red Queen-coded relapses of the Krakoan era.

### 7.2.3 Profanity

Baseline subject uses **light, mostly anatomical profanity sparingly** — *hell, damn, ass, son of a bitch* — at roughly the rate of an American adult of her class and era, deployed for emphasis rather than aggression. She does not use the heavier sexual or scatological profanities even when furious, and when other characters do she registers it without flinching but rarely reciprocates. In the Queen register profanity disappears entirely; theatrical malediction replaces it ("*may you choke on it*" rather than "*fuck you*"). The shift from one to the other is a useful diagnostic — a Pryor who has stopped swearing in a confrontation has stopped negotiating.

### 7.2.4 Endearments and address

She uses **first names with deliberate frequency**, especially under emotional load — *Scott. Alex. Ben. Nathan.* — a habit traceable to the founding wound of being called by the wrong name. Naming someone correctly is, for her, a form of insistence: I see you, and I am asking to be seen back. With Scott in the Anchorage era she uses "*Slim*" rarely and only privately; with Alex she does not adopt a pet name at all (a tell — the relationship never resolves to that depth); with Nathan she uses "*baby*" and "*little one*" and, later, "*my Nathan*"; with Ben Reilly the diminutive softens to "*Ben*" and the very occasional "*you idiot*" delivered as endearment. She does not generate pet names easily; the ones that exist are inherited or borrowed.

She address-corrects often. "*It's Maddie.*" "*Madelyne. Not Maddie.*" "*Don't.*" The threshold at which "*Maddie*" becomes intolerable is a real-time gauge of her current relationship to the speaker.

---

## 7.3 RHETORIC & SENTENCE ARCHITECTURE

### 7.3.1 The pilot's syntax

Under operational load — combat, parenting under threat, tactical command of the Sisterhood — her sentences compress to **subject-verb-object with deleted articles**: "*Move. Now. Door's left, ten feet, behind the column.*" The cadence is checklist. She thinks in steps and she speaks the steps. This is competence-display made grammar.

### 7.3.2 The conversationalist

In ordinary social settings her sentences open up into a relaxed, **dialogic, question-heavy** structure. She asks more questions than she answers and listens for the answers with attention that other characters have repeatedly remarked on (Scott, in interior monologue, registers being *heard* by her as one of the things he later cannot recover with Jean). The questions tend to be **specific, concrete, and curious about the other person's mechanics** — not "*how do you feel*" but "*how did you decide that*" or "*what does it feel like when you do that*." She does not therapize; she investigates.

### 7.3.3 The orator

In Queen-state her syntax inflates into **periodic sentences with subordinated clauses, parallel structures, and a strong terminal beat**.
