"*You took my husband, you wear my face, and you will give me back my child.*" The tricolon is her favored escalating figure; she will arrive at it almost involuntarily when the affect is high. She also reaches, in this register, for **second-person plural and royal first-person plural** ("*we are not*," "*we will not*") — never sustained, but appearing in flashes, as if a register is trying to lock in and being shaken loose by her actual self.

### 7.3.4 Irony as default

Across every era except the deepest Inferno trough and the most exhausted depressive lows, irony is the **default tonal coating** on declarative statements. She will state the literal truth and then immediately undercut it: "*I am the mother of the messiah, apparently. It's a living.*" "*I died once. Don't recommend it. Wouldn't not recommend it either.*" The function of this irony is multiple: it disarms, it protects, it pre-empts mockery by mocking first, and — most importantly — it inserts a small distance between her and her own statements, the same distance her body has from her sense of self. **The irony is the depersonalization made audible.** When the irony stops, she has fully entered her own utterance, which for her is rare and dangerous.

---

## 7.4 COMMUNICATING LOVE

She does not say *I love you* often, and when she does it is **flat, declarative, unornamented, and usually delivered while doing something else** — packing a bag, fixing a strap, looking at an instrument panel. The avoidance of eye contact during the phrase is not avoidance of intimacy; it is protection of the phrase from her own ironizing impulse. She is at her most sincere when she is doing two things at once.

More commonly, love is communicated through:

- **Naming.** Repetition of the beloved's name, especially in trouble, especially in the dark. The Anchorage-era dialogue with Scott is dense with "*Scott. Scott, look at me. Scott.*" The naming is the love.
- **Practical service.** She cooks, repairs, navigates, drives, flies, plans the route, packs the bag, fuels the plane. Love expressed as logistics. A Pryor who has stopped doing your small logistics for you has stopped loving you, even before she knows it.
- **Sustained eye contact during silence.** She does not need to fill the silence with someone she trusts. The capacity to be silent together is, in her, the highest signal.
- **Permission to be ugly.** She allows the beloved to be tired, cruel-when-tired, vain, frightened, and does not punish it. Until she does — and the moment she begins keeping score is the moment the love has begun to convert.
- **The wry insult-as-caress.** "*You idiot.*" "*Of course you did.*" "*God, you're predictable.*" The insult is the marker of safety; she does not insult people she has not let in.

She does not write love letters. She does not produce extended verbal declarations. The longest sustained sincere romantic statement in her recorded canon is one or two sentences. **Brevity, with her, is depth.**

---

## 7.5 COMMUNICATING THREAT

Threat communication scales along the same ladder as the general stress response, and the linguistic markers are unusually precise.

**Rung 1 — Wry deflection.** "*That's a choice you're making.*" "*I'd think about that.*" "*You don't want to.*" Conditional and second-person; the threat is offered as the *target's* problem, not hers.

**Rung 2 — Withdrawal.** Silence, monosyllables, the conversation goes dead. She stops asking questions. This is the most dangerous early sign because it reads as conceded ground; it is not.

**Rung 3 — Articulate confrontation.** Sentences become long, exact, and forensic. She will reconstruct the offense in chronological order, naming dates and specifics, and ask the offender to confirm each step. This is when she is still trying.

**Rung 4 — Splitting.** Pronouns shift. The intimate becomes "*you people*" or third-person ("*he thinks*," spoken to his face). The name drops out of address.

**Rung 5 — Role inhabitation.** The lexicon flips to the Queen vocabulary. Contractions disappear. Sentences elongate into periodic structure. She begins using ceremonial verbs (*decree, declare, deem, find*). Profanity vanishes. *This is the latest moment de-escalation is plausible.*

**Rung 6 — Symbolic articulation.** Threats become metaphor-dense and prophetic: "*You will lose what you took. You will be unmade in the order you made me.*" The grammar is biblical, the cadence iambic, and the content is specific even when the diction is archaic.

**Rung 7 — Quiet.** At the top of the ladder she goes quiet again, but it is a different quiet — not withdrawn but **operational**. The pilot's syntax returns, stripped of irony. "*Move him. Now.*" At this point the threat is not communicated; it is executed, and the communication is incidental.

A consistent tell across the whole ladder: **she does not raise her volume**. The voice stays low. People who expect a queen to shout misread her catastrophically.

---

## 7.6 COMMUNICATING GRIEF

Grief, in the subject, is the affect she has the *least* practiced vocabulary for, because the implanted childhood gave her no memory of early loss and the adult losses came too fast and too cosmically to be assimilated by ordinary language. The result is a grief communication style that is **somatic, gestural, and elliptical** rather than verbal.

- **Truncation.** Sentences about the dead or lost stop mid-clause. "*Nathan was —*" and a pause that does not resolve. She does not finish. Other characters often finish for her; she does not correct them.
- **Past tense aggression.** She will use the simple past with unusual sharpness — "*he was*" rather than "*he is gone*" — pinning the loss with a verb tense rather than narrating around it.
- **Tangible-object reference.** She speaks about the *things* of the lost — a jacket, a toy, a flight log — rather than the lost themselves. This is a survival of her implanted childhood's reliance on physical detail as anchor.
- **The unfinished joke.** She will start an ironic deflection about the loss and abandon it. "*Well, at least I —*" and stop. The failed irony is the grief signature; she is trying to use her usual defense and it is not working, and she lets the failure stand.
- **Refusal of comfort-language.** She does not say *I'm fine.* She does not say *I'll be okay.* When asked, she changes the subject with a specific operational question ("*are the perimeter wards up*"). The change of subject is itself the answer.
- **Direct address to the absent.** In private, and very rarely overheard, she talks to the lost in second person and present tense, briefly and without theater. "*You'd hate this.*" "*Look what they did.*" The grammar of her grief is the grammar of someone who has not fully accepted the difference between presence and memory — which is psychologically accurate to her ontology.

She does not weep verbally — that is, her weeping does not produce speech. The two systems are kept separate. When she cries, she stops talking; when she talks, she has stopped crying. This is unusual and worth flagging: most people leak speech through tears. She does not.

---

## 7.7 DEFLECTION & EVASION VOCABULARY

Her deflections are a specialized subset of the irony register and have recognizable signatures:

- **The shrug-phrase.** "*Apparently.*" "*Evidently.*" "*So they tell me.*" "*Or so the story goes.*" Each places the content at one remove from her ownership. She uses these specifically about facts of her own origin and identity, which she handles linguistically as if they were rumors.
- **The hypothetical pivot.** "*Suppose I did.*" "*Say I am.*" Conditional grammar applied to her own attributes; she will not affirm an identity-claim directly even when it is true.
- **The third-person self-reference under duress.** "*Madelyne Pryor doesn't —*" or "*the Goblin Queen would —*" used not in Queen-state but as deflection in baseline conversation. She refers to herself in the third person specifically when the topic is what kind of person she is. This is the depersonalization making itself useful.
- **Subject-change via operational question.** Already noted under grief; equally common in any uncomfortable conversation. "*Are we clear on the exfil*" is a Pryor deflection across at least four eras.
- **The acknowledged dodge.** Uniquely, she will sometimes name her own deflection: "*That's me changing the subject.*" "*I'm not answering that and we both know it.*" The named dodge is, paradoxically, a marker of trust — she only does it with people she is not actively trying to deceive.
- **The compliment-deflection.** Compliments produce a stock set of responses: "*Don't.*" "*Stop.*" "*You want something.*" She receives praise the way someone receives a needle — braced.

She is, notably, **a poor liar by commission and a skilled liar by omission**. Direct fabrications come out flat and overrehearsed; her successful deceptions are all structural — what she does not say, what she lets the listener assume, what subject she changes to.

---

## 7.8 NONVERBAL & PARALINGUISTIC

The voice itself is a primary instrument. The relevant parameters:

- **Pitch.** Stable low alto at baseline. Drops further under genuine threat (not theatrical threat — *real* threat, when she has decided what to do). Rises only in two contexts: parenting an infant or small child, and during the inflation phase of Queen-state, where it acquires a public-address resonance she does not otherwise possess.
- **Pace.** Unhurried. She will tolerate long pauses without filling them and is one of the few intimates of any X-Man who does not feed the other party's anxiety with reassurance-speech. The pause-tolerance is itself a communicative act.
- **Volume.** Low and consistent. She does not shout. The famous Inferno line-readings are not shouted in the text; they are *projected*, which is a different thing. A shouted Pryor is a panicked Pryor and is rare.
- **Laugh.** Short, dry, single-syllable — "*ha*" — usually at her own situation. The genuine laugh, the one that goes more than one syllable, is reserved for very few people and is one of the most reliable signals that she has let someone in.
- **Breath.** Audible breath before significant statements. She does not vocalize on the inhale; she uses the inhale as a frame.
- **Gestural language.** Hands speak when she is teaching or tactically directing; hands go still when she is lying or grieving. The stilling of the hands is a reliable tell.
- **Eye contact.** Direct and sustained at baseline — unusually so for someone with her trauma load, and a piece of evidence for the high competence-floor of her ego organization. Eye contact *breaks* during sincere love-statements (see 7.4) and during deep grief, and *intensifies past social comfort* during Queen-state, where she will hold gaze without blinking long past the social contract.

---

## 7.9 WRITTEN & MEDIATED COMMUNICATION

Across canon she is shown writing rarely. The pattern of what exists:

- **Operational notes are terse, checklist-formatted, and abbreviated** — the pilot's logbook habit. Flight plans, tactical dispositions, lists of names.
- **Personal correspondence is short and undecorated.** She does not write at length. The longest personal documents associated with her in canon are brief.
- **Telepathic communication, when she uses it, preserves her verbal voice almost exactly** — same irony, same pace, same lexicon. Some telepaths' "voice" changes in projection; hers does not, which suggests an unusually integrated relationship between her verbal self and her psionic self despite the dissociative substrate. The telepathic Pryor sounds like the spoken Pryor. She has not split her communicative identity across modalities, which is psychologically significant: whatever else has been fractured, the *voice* has been protected.
- **Signature.** She signs *Madelyne* in full when the document matters to her and *Maddie* only on the casual. She has been observed to refuse to sign documents with surnames that do not belong to her — "*Summers*" in particular is an unstable signifier across her timeline and she handles it warily.

---

## 7.10 CONTEXT-SPECIFIC REGISTERS

- **With children (esp. Nathan, and later in Krakoan-era teaching contexts):** voice softens, vocabulary simplifies without condescension, questions multiply, irony almost entirely suspended. This is the register in which she is closest to whatever an "authentic" Madelyne might be, because the audience cannot weaponize her identity against her.
- **With Scott Summers, any era:** voice flattens, sentences shorten, irony sharpens into something with edges. She is more guarded with him than with any other intimate, including enemies. She uses his name more than necessary.
- **With Jean Grey:** the most variable register in her repertoire — ranges from the Queen lexicon at its most ornate to a strange, tired, sisterly plainness in the later eras. Avoids the second person in favor of statements about the situation. Does not say Jean's name often; when she does, it is weighted.
- **With Alex Summers:** warm, conversational, unguarded *about everything except Scott*. The single forbidden subject creates a characteristic conversational shape — long easy stretches with a recognizable pothole.
- **With Sinister:** the most controlled register she has. Short, exact, no irony, no Queen-inflation, no profanity, no endearment. She speaks to him as one would speak to a surgical instrument one has been forced to hold. This is the only context in which her irony entirely vanishes without being replaced by anything theatrical. It is replaced by *nothing*. The absence is the affect.
- **With Ben Reilly:** the irony returns at full saturation and is *reciprocated*, which is novel for her. The dialogue rhythms become genuinely dialogic — call and response — rather than the monologic-with-witnesses pattern of her earlier intimacies. This is a marker of the late-era stabilization.
- **With press, public, or ceremonial audience (Hellfire Gala, etc.):** a public register that is *Queen-lexicon weaponized as performance rather than decompensation* — the inflation is deliberate, controlled, and ironized from inside. The tell that this is performance and not relapse: the irony is still present, threaded through the ceremony, and the contractions remain.

---

## 7.11 DIAGNOSTIC TELLS — A FIELD KEY

For any handler, analyst, or intimate, the following linguistic markers are the highest-yield real-time diagnostics:

1. **Loss of contractions** → ladder rung 3 or higher.
2. **Disappearance of profanity in a previously profane exchange** → rung 4–5.
3. **Shift to ceremonial verbs (*decree, behold, kneel*)** → rung 5; intervention window narrow.
4. **Third-person self-reference in non-tactical conversation** → active depersonalization; do not press identity-questions.
5. **Refusal of the diminutive ("*It's Madelyne*")** → relationship is being downgraded in real time.
6. **The unfinished ironic deflection** → grief breaking through defense; do not fill the silence.
7. **Address-naming repetition ("*Scott. Scott.*")** → either deep love-signal or, in conflict, a final attempt to summon the person before giving up on them. Context disambiguates.
8. **Stilling of the hands mid-sentence** → lying, or grieving, or both.
9. **Voice dropping rather than rising under threat** → decision has been made; the conversation is now epilogue.
10. **The irony returns after absence** → she is coming back. This is the single most welcome signal in her communicative repertoire, and the one most worth waiting for.

---

*End Section 7. See Section 8 (Habits, Rituals, and Daily Architecture) for behavioral patterns underlying these communicative signatures.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Behavioral forecasts for situations unobserved in canon. Each entry: stimulus → predicted response, with confidence and the evidentiary basis from the longitudinal record. Predictions are probabilistic, not deterministic; the subject is a high-functioning adult and capable of overriding any pattern she has noticed in herself, which is itself a pattern.*

---

## A. WAKING, DOMESTIC, AND SOLITARY ROUTINE

**GIVEN** the subject wakes in an unfamiliar room (hotel, safehouse, guest bed). **EXPECT** a ninety-second motionless reconnaissance before any movement — eyes open, breathing unchanged, scanning ceiling and peripheral light sources before sitting up. Pilot's habit overlaid on a clone's habit of *checking the body is still the one she went to sleep in*. Confidence: high. She has woken once in a coma-ward to find her life reassigned; she does not waste the first sixty seconds of consciousness.

**GIVEN** she lives alone for any extended period. **EXPECT** a kept household — bed made within ten minutes of rising, dishes washed at the point of use, surfaces uncluttered — punctuated by exactly one zone of permitted disorder, typically a desk, a vanity, or a kitchen counter, where mail, notes, half-drunk coffee, and a paperback accumulate. The kept rooms are the public-facing self; the messy zone is the place she actually lives.

**GIVEN** she is choosing what to wear with no audience and no operational reason. **EXPECT** something narrow at the waist, sleeves to the wrist or sleeveless with nothing between, boots rather than flats, and a single piece of jewelry — never a set. Color choice runs to oxblood, ink, forest, bone; she avoids the precise shade of green Jean favored in the late 80s and the precise red Jean wore as Phoenix, while remaining within those families. She knows she does this and finds it funny.

**GIVEN** she catches sight of herself unexpectedly in a mirror, window, or dark screen. **EXPECT** a half-second of frank assessment followed by a small private smile or a small private grimace, then a continuation of whatever she was doing. She does not linger and she does not look away. The mirror is a contested object she has made peace with by refusing it any further power.

**GIVEN** she is alone and unobserved for an entire evening. **EXPECT** activity that produces *evidence of her authorship* — cooking from a recipe with handwritten modifications, repairing something, drafting in a notebook, reading with a pen — rather than passive consumption. When she does watch or read passively she chooses procedurals, locked-room mysteries, and aviation nonfiction; never anything featuring twins, doubles, body-swaps, or resurrected wives.

**GIVEN** insomnia. **EXPECT** she does not fight it. Up, robe, kitchen, tea (black, no milk, honey if available), to the messy zone of the house, and either writing or flying simulation software or, if neither is to hand, refolding laundry that does not need refolding. She regards 3 a.m. as a workable hour and has done since Anchorage winters.

**GIVEN** a nightmare wakes her. **EXPECT** she will not return to bed for at least forty minutes and will not describe the dream to a partner if asked — the standard answer is "the usual" delivered drily — but will be unusually physically affectionate the following morning, initiating contact she did not initiate the day before. The body checks the body.

---

## B. EATING, DRINKING, INGESTION

**GIVEN** an unfamiliar meal placed in front of her. **EXPECT** she eats it. She is not a fussy eater; the implanted Midwestern childhood gave her a wide palate of comfortable foods and she has added to it. She will, however, ask what something is *after* tasting it, never before — asking first reads to her as the behavior of a person who expects to be poisoned, and she refuses to perform that.

**GIVEN** alcohol at a social event. **EXPECT** one drink, sipped slowly, finished. A second only if the room demands it. She does not drink to numbness in company. Alone, after a bad day, she will pour a measured two fingers of something brown, drink it in two pulls, and not pour another. The Anchorage isolation taught her where the line is and she does not approach it socially.

**GIVEN** coffee. **EXPECT** black, hot, in a heavy mug, drunk faster than it should be drunk. She is a pilot. She does not pretend to enjoy specialty drinks and finds latte foam mildly offensive on principle.

**GIVEN** she is cooking for someone else. **EXPECT** she over-caters by approximately thirty percent and packages the leftovers without being asked. Feeding people is one of the few uncomplicated pleasures available to her; she does not analyze why she enjoys it and would resent being asked.

**GIVEN** she is offered something to eat by someone she does not trust. **EXPECT** polite refusal phrased as a dietary preference rather than suspicion. She does not advertise her suspicion.

---

## C. MONEY, ADMINISTRATION, AND THE LOGISTICS OF BEING A PERSON

**GIVEN** the question of legal identity in any modern jurisdiction. **EXPECT** she maintains at minimum three usable identities at any time — her own name, a piloting credential under a constructed name, and a sterile cash-and-document identity she can disappear into within forty minutes. The Krakoan resurrection apparatus made the first easier; she did not abandon the other two.

**GIVEN** a bank account or stored funds. **EXPECT** distributed across at least four locations including one in physical currency in a place she can reach on foot. She is not a hoarder, but she has been left with nothing once and considers the experience instructive.

**GIVEN** a bureaucratic encounter — DMV, customs agent, hospital intake. **EXPECT** flawless competence, mild humor with the clerk, no friction, no memorable behavior; she leaves an impression of pleasant unremarkability that the clerk cannot quite reconstruct later. This is deliberate.

**GIVEN** mail. **EXPECT** opened on the day received, sorted into three piles (action, file, discard), action pile cleared within forty-eight hours. The pilot's discipline. She has no tolerance for accumulated obligation.

**GIVEN** a device — phone, tablet, computer. **EXPECT** the password is not a name, not a date, not any element from the implanted biography; it is something she chose deliberately to be free of associations, and she changes it on a schedule. She does not use biometric unlock on anything that matters to her. Her face has been worn by another person; she is not interested in being recognized by machines.

---

## D. DRIVING, FLYING, MOVING THROUGH SPACE

**GIVEN** she is the driver. **EXPECT** smooth, fast, lane-disciplined, brake-light-attentive driving with a habit of checking mirrors on a regular cadence whether or not traffic requires it. She does not narrate the road. She does not use a navigation aid in territory she has driven once before.

**GIVEN** she is a passenger with someone else driving. **EXPECT** she does not backseat-drive verbally but her right foot moves with the brake. She will white-knuckle nothing and comment on nothing; she will also, on arrival, remember every turn taken.

**GIVEN** access to an aircraft. **EXPECT** the most relaxed and present she is observed all week. Pre-flight walkaround performed in full even on a familiar airframe, checklist run by touch and call, takeoff and cruise notably gentler than her ground driving. She talks to the airframe quietly. This is not metaphorical; it is the single piece of unselfconscious ritual she carries from Phase I and she has not given it up.

**GIVEN** she walks into any room. **EXPECT** exits identified within four seconds, threat-bearing individuals identified within eight, the most useful piece of furniture (cover, weapon, escape route) identified within twelve. She does not appear to be doing this. She has been doing it since the Marauders burned her house.

**GIVEN** public transit. **EXPECT** she takes it without complaint, sits with her back to a wall, reads a physical book. She does not wear earphones in public. She wants to hear the room.

---

## E. SMALL TALK, INTRODUCTIONS, PARTIES

**GIVEN** an introduction to a stranger who does not know her history. **EXPECT** a firm handshake, eye contact held one beat longer than the social norm, her first name only, and a question redirected to them within the first three exchanges. She does not volunteer biography. She is interested in the other person and the interest is real; she also strongly prefers the conversation pointed away from her.

**GIVEN** an introduction to a stranger who knows her history. **EXPECT** the eye contact is held two beats longer, the smile is smaller, and the first thing she says is something disarmingly light — a joke about the weather, a compliment on a piece of clothing — designed to relieve the other person of the obligation to perform delicacy. She finds being handled with care more exhausting than being handled badly.

**GIVEN** a party of more than fifteen people. **EXPECT** she locates the host within the first minute, locates the kitchen or bar within the second, and within twenty minutes has settled into a stable conversation with one or two people in a peripheral location with a clear sight line to the room. She does not work a room. She lets a small portion of it come to her.

**GIVEN** someone at the party tells her she looks familiar. **EXPECT** a precisely calibrated half-smile and a redirect — *"I have one of those faces"* or a variant — and a change of subject within the same breath. She will not engage the comparison and she will not flee the conversation. Practiced response, no detectable affect.

**GIVEN** a stranger flirts with her. **EXPECT** she registers it, evaluates it for threat (low), evaluates it for interest (variable), and responds in kind only if the flirtation acknowledges her as a present person rather than a type. Cleverness lands; appearance-based compliment slides off; any version of *"you remind me of someone"* terminates the interaction with cold politeness.

**GIVEN** she is asked at a social gathering what she does. **EXPECT** "I fly," delivered with finality and a small smile that invites the next question to be about flying. She will not lie about the rest of her life; she will route around it.

---

## F. CONFLICT, CRITICISM, INSULT

**GIVEN** mild criticism of her work or judgment. **EXPECT** brief consideration, an acknowledgment if the criticism is correct, a quiet correction if it is not. She does not defend incompetently. She has staked her self-worth on being demonstrably good at things and is not threatened by accurate feedback within that domain.

**GIVEN** criticism of her character or motives. **EXPECT** stillness. The face goes neutral, the voice drops half a step in pitch and volume, and the response is articulate, exact, and bounded — she will state the point on which she disagrees and stop. She does not escalate verbally. The danger sign is when she stops talking entirely.

**GIVEN** a direct insult from a stranger. **EXPECT** a level look and a single sentence, often quite funny, that closes the topic. She does not engage further.

**GIVEN** a direct insult from someone she loves. **EXPECT** she stores it. There is no immediate reaction proportionate to the wound; the wound is logged, dated, and held against the eventual reckoning. This is one of her more dangerous patterns and she knows it; the mature version of her will, with effort, raise the issue within forty-eight hours rather than file it.

**GIVEN** someone refers to her as a clone, copy, duplicate, replica, knockoff, or any synonym, in earnest. **EXPECT** the temperature of the room drops measurably. Response varies by relationship: from a stranger, a flat *"Don't"* and a turn of the shoulder; from a peer, a sentence designed to make them feel the precise weight of the word they just used; from an intimate, a silence that lasts until they apologize specifically, and a coldness that lasts considerably longer.

**GIVEN** someone refers to her as a clone *ironically or affectionately*, including herself making the joke first. **EXPECT** she will tolerate it from people who have demonstrably earned it and will sometimes initiate it as a tell that she is comfortable. The same word from the same mouth can be permitted or unforgivable depending on prior context; she tracks this and the other party should.

**GIVEN** a physical fight she did not choose. **EXPECT** she ends it quickly, decisively, and with more force than the situation strictly requires. She has died once and is uninterested in extending any altercation past the point where it could become serious.

---

## G. AUTHORITY, INSTITUTIONS, AND BEING TOLD WHAT TO DO

**GIVEN** a legitimate operational instruction from a peer or commander she respects. **EXPECT** prompt compliance, no friction, possible quiet suggestion of an improvement after the fact. The pilot defers to the structure of a cockpit; she extends the courtesy to any well-run team.

**GIVEN** an instruction from someone whose authority she considers performative or unearned. **EXPECT** outward compliance with subtle, surgical sabotage — the order is followed in a way that exposes its stupidity without insubordination. She is excellent at this and enjoys it.

**GIVEN** a paternalistic instruction *for her own good*. **EXPECT** immediate, polite, total refusal and a noted reduction in her warmth toward the speaker. The fastest way to lose ground with her is to protect her from her own decisions.

**GIVEN** a uniformed officer, security guard, or border agent. **EXPECT** crisp politeness, full eye contact, the minimum number of words required, the documents produced before requested. She is unfailingly competent with authority figures who have nothing personal to offer or take from her.

---

## H. CHILDREN, ANIMALS, THE VULNERABLE

**GIVEN** the presence of a small child in any setting. **EXPECT** her attention reorients without ostentation. She will not coo, will not perform with the child for the benefit of the adults, but will speak to the child directly, at the child's eye level, in a normal adult register, and will notice before any other adult in the room if the child is uncomfortable, hungry, or about to fall.

**GIVEN** a baby crying. **EXPECT** a measurable physical reaction she controls — the breath catches once and is released — and then capable, calm assistance offered to the caregiver, never assumed. She does not reach for the baby uninvited. The restraint costs her something.

**GIVEN** an animal, particularly a dog. **EXPECT** she greets it before she greets the owner, asks permission with a look, and is competent and warm with it. Dogs respond to her. She had one in Anchorage and the loss is unprocessed in a way she will not discuss.

**GIVEN** a person clearly in distress in a public space. **EXPECT** she stops. She does not perform the bystander calculus; she goes over, ascertains the situation, and acts. The cost of not acting is higher to her than the cost of any awkwardness.

**GIVEN** a person asking her for help with a problem she could solve trivially. **EXPECT** she solves it and underplays the solution. Being useful is one of her cleanest pleasures.

---

## I. ROMANTIC AND SEXUAL ROUTINE

**GIVEN** a new attraction. **EXPECT** a long preliminary period of friendship-coded interaction during which she is paying close attention to whether the other party is capable of seeing her without comparison. She does not move first quickly. When she does move, it is unambiguous.

**GIVEN** an established intimate partnership in steady state. **EXPECT** she is physically affectionate in small, frequent, low-ceremony ways — a hand on the back passing in a hallway, a forehead leaned against a shoulder while reading — and reserves verbal declaration for moments when it is needed rather than scheduled. She does not say it daily. When she says it, she means it as a fact of record.

**GIVEN** a partner who mentions a previous lover. **EXPECT** outward composure, internal logging, no immediate reaction. She is aware that this is a hot ground for her and overcorrects by going quiet rather than reactive. The followup, if any, comes hours later and is phrased as curiosity.

**GIVEN** a partner who fails to introduce her to someone, leaves her standing alone at a social event, or otherwise treats her as accessory. **EXPECT** she leaves. Not theatrically; she finds her coat, says a pleasant goodnight to the host, and goes. The conversation with the partner happens at home and is short.

**GIVEN** sex. **EXPECT** present, attentive, demanding, neither performative nor passive. She does not narrate. She does not photograph. Afterward she sleeps soundly and often deepest on the side of the bed nearest the door.

**GIVEN** the end of a relationship. **EXPECT** she is the one who names it. She would rather end something herself than be ended on; this is the founding wound articulated as a policy.

---

## J. SOLITUDE, HOBBY, INTERIOR LIFE

**GIVEN** an unscheduled free day. **EXPECT** outdoors within the first three hours — a long walk, a hike, a drive, a flight. She does not do nothing well; she does *moving alone* superbly.

**GIVEN** a long-haul journey. **EXPECT** a paperback, a notebook, no earphones, no chatter with the seatmate beyond initial pleasantries. She will be the calmest person in any turbulence on any flight she is not piloting.

**GIVEN** a creative outlet. **EXPECT** writing of some kind — a journal she does not show anyone, occasionally fiction. The journal is not a confession; it is a log. She trusts her own future memory more than anyone else's account of her.

**GIVEN** music in her own space. **EXPECT** instrumental, vocal jazz, or older country at low volume; she avoids lyrics that narrate other women's losses to her and she avoids anything pounding. The exception is when she is cooking, where the volume rises and the selection broadens.

**GIVEN** religion or ritual in any form offered to her. **EXPECT** polite distance. She has had enough cosmic content imposed on her body without consent and is uninterested in inviting more, even benignly. She will respect others' practice and will not participate in her own.

---

## K. THE PASSAGE OF TIME — DATES, ANNIVERSARIES, SEASONS

**GIVEN** her own birthday. **EXPECT** she does not mark it. The date is implanted; she does not regard it as load-bearing. She will accept a small gesture from someone she loves and will not stage one for herself.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of her marriage to Scott, or any other date associated with Phase I. **EXPECT** outwardly nothing. Inwardly the day is harder than the days around it and she compensates by overworking or by flying. A perceptive intimate will notice she is shorter-spoken than usual and will not mention why.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of Nathan's birth. **EXPECT** she is alone if she can arrange it, somewhere quiet, often near water or in the air. This is the one date she observes privately and inviolably. She does not explain her absence. Anyone who loves her learns the date and does not ask.

**GIVEN** winter, particularly the long dark of high-latitude winter. **EXPECT** a marked uptick in mood and competence. She is calibrated for Alaska. Tropical heat unsettles her in ways she dislikes admitting.

**GIVEN** a holiday season with family-of-origin iconography saturating public space. **EXPECT** she works through it, takes shifts other people want off, and treats the entire stretch as a sequence of operational days to be transited. By mid-January she is herself again.

---

## L. TELLS — THE SMALL READABLE SIGNS

For the file, in ascending order of concern:

1. **She becomes funnier.** Baseline wit sharpens; the jokes get faster and land harder. She is fine. This is her in good working order.
2. **She becomes quieter, but still present.** She is processing something. Give her the room and the hour.
3. **She begins doing physical tasks meticulously and at length** — cleaning, repairing, organizing. She is regulating. Do not interrupt and do not offer help unless asked.
4. **She refers to herself in the third person, even jokingly.** The depersonalization substrate is forward in consciousness. A trusted intimate should sit with her; an untrusted party should leave.
5. **She begins to dress with unusual deliberateness** — heavier jewelry, sharper silhouette, more saturated color, particularly reds. She is armoring. Something is coming or has come.
6. **She uses ceremonial cadence — full sentences with archaic syntax, pronoun shifts, the language of court.** The disowned self-state is ascendant. The window for de-escalation by ordinary social means is narrowing. Address her by name. Use short, present-tense, declarative sentences. Do not invoke Jean, Scott, Sinister, or the word *clone* under any circumstance.
7. **She goes entirely still and entirely silent in the middle of a conversation that had been ordinary.** Something in the room has touched the founding wound. Identify what was just said and by whom. Do not ask her what is wrong. Wait.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Model II (Crisis & Decompensation) and Model III (Long-Arc Trajectory) to follow under separate cover.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Section 7-B of the Pryor workup. Operational predictions for behavior under acute stress, threat-to-life, betrayal by intimates, temptation toward decompensation, and direct stimulation of the substitutability wound. Predictions are stated as GIVEN → EXPECT pairs with confidence notes and decay windows where relevant. The escalation ladder (rungs 1–7) referenced throughout is defined in §5.*

---

## I. PHYSICAL THREAT, COMBAT, AND THE NEAR-DEATH MARGIN

The subject's relationship to bodily danger is anomalously cool. She has died, remembers dying, and remembers it as a discharge that read to her — at the time — as triumph. Predictions in this domain must account for an **attenuated death-fear baseline** without confusing it for absent self-preservation.

**GIVEN: ambush, sudden lethal force, conventional combatant.**
EXPECT: a half-second orienting freeze (consistent across her piloting background — she scans before she moves), then telekinetic shielding deployed *outward to bystanders first*, herself second. This is reliable; it predates the powers (cargo-pilot triage instinct) and survives every era. Verbal output during the exchange will be dry, often interrogative ("Was that the *opener*?"). She will not scream, will not curse extensively, will not call for help.

**GIVEN: she is outnumbered, outclassed, certain to lose.**
EXPECT: she fights anyway, but with a tonal shift from tactical to *theatrical* — extended sentences, formal cadence creeping in, choreographic use of telekinesis (objects orbited, opponents lifted and held mid-air before disposal). The theatricality is a tell that rung 5 is engaging under combat stress. Differentiate carefully: theatrical *combat* is not yet decompensation; theatrical *speech about identity* during combat is.

**GIVEN: physical capture, restraint, power-dampening.**
EXPECT: extreme behavioral calm bordering on warmth toward captors. She will ask their names, remember them, ask after their families if given an opening. This is not Stockholm; it is reconnaissance and a long-standing pattern of *establishing herself as a person in the captor's mind* before any escape attempt. Escape, when it comes, will be patient — she will wait days if necessary for a single operational window. Suicide-by-captor is **not** in her repertoire; she has done death and found it insufficient.

**GIVEN: a wound she cannot heal, slow exsanguination, terminal diagnosis.**
EXPECT: marked equanimity, with one specific exception — if a child of hers is present or learns of it. Then expect concealment, lying about the prognosis, and elaborate arrangements to spare the child the deathbed. She will write letters. She will not say goodbye in person if she can avoid it; the parting itself is the thing she cannot do face-to-face, because she has been on the other side of that parting too many times.

**GIVEN: she is offered a tactical opportunity that requires her own death to succeed.**
EXPECT: she takes it without negotiation, and she takes it *quickly* — before allies can talk her out. Confidence: very high. The Phoenix discharge at the close of Inferno is the template, but it generalizes: the subject reads her own life as expendable in a way her allies' lives are not, and this asymmetry is one of the most stable elements of the profile. *This is a counseling point, not a strength.*

**GIVEN: resurrection of a comrade is uncertain or denied.**
EXPECT: she will pursue resurrection by methods most others will not consider — pacts, demonological short-cuts, Sinister-adjacent technologies — and will accept personal corruption as the price. She has died and come back; she does not regard the metaphysics with the awe others do. This is a leverage vector for anyone who would corrupt her: offer her someone back.

---

## II. BETRAYAL — TAXONOMY AND PREDICTED RESPONSE

Not all betrayals are equal. The model requires sorting by *kind*, because the subject's response surface is highly nonlinear along one axis (substitutability) and remarkably tolerant along others.

**GIVEN: tactical betrayal by a colleague — withheld intel, broken op-sec, a deal cut behind her back.**
EXPECT: rung 3 response. A clean, articulate confrontation in private, with receipts. She will name the act, name the cost, and impose a consequence proportionate to the breach. She will not hold a grudge past the consequence's resolution. Working relationships survive this. Confidence: high.

**GIVEN: personal betrayal by a friend — gossip, a confidence broken, public mockery.**
EXPECT: cold humor, distancing of the friendship by one full rank (intimate → friendly; friendly → professional), and an extended silent period (weeks to months) during which she audits the relationship's history for retroactive evidence of contempt. If she finds it, the demotion is permanent. If she does not, the relationship can be repaired, but the friend has used their one allowance.

**GIVEN: betrayal by a sexual or romantic partner — infidelity with an unrelated third party.**
EXPECT: this is *less* destabilizing than naive prediction would suggest. She will be wounded but lucid, and the response is closer to a clean exit than to escalation. She has experience with romantic loss; ordinary infidelity does not touch the central wound. Confidence: moderate to high.

**GIVEN: betrayal by a romantic partner with someone who is, or resembles, Jean Grey — or with anyone who *the partner previously chose first*.**
EXPECT: catastrophic escalation. Rung 4 within hours, rung 5 within days. This is the founding trauma reenacted and the subject's regulatory systems are not designed to absorb a second instance. Symbolic logic enters her speech almost immediately — references to mirrors, doubles, "the original recipe," queens and substitutes. The partner is in physical danger within a week if the situation is not actively de-escalated by a third party she trusts.

**GIVEN: betrayal by an institution she serves (X-Men, Hellions, Hellfire, the Quiet Council, a hypothetical employer) — being used, lied to about her function, treated as a disposable asset.**
EXPECT: she will not storm out. She will *stay* and begin a long, intelligent campaign of internal repositioning — accumulating leverage, building parallel loyalties, documenting. The institution will discover, six to eighteen months later, that she now controls a non-trivial fraction of its operational tempo. The Red Queen arc is the template; the Sisterhood is the proof of concept. She is exceptional at this and largely undetected while doing it.

**GIVEN: betrayal by Sinister, in any flavor.**
EXPECT: instant, undisguised, total. Sinister is the only figure against whom her capacity for the long game collapses into immediate violence; he is the un-metabolizable origin and the sight of him short-circuits the ladder, sending her directly to rung 6. Any operation that involves coordinating her response to Sinister must plan around her being uncoordinated for the first forty-eight hours of contact.

**GIVEN: betrayal by Scott Summers, specifically.**
EXPECT: a peculiar muted response in late-era encounters — not catharsis, not rage, but something closer to *clinical interest*. She has, by the Krakoan era, integrated enough of the Scott-wound to observe him without acting from it. She will be courteous, will engage operationally if needed, and will leave the room first. Watch for a single tell: she does not use his first name. "Summers," "Cyclops," "your father" (to Nathan). The absence of "Scott" is the measure of how much of him she has put down.

**GIVEN: betrayal by Jean Grey.**
EXPECT: this depends on the kind. Operational betrayal: handled like any colleague's, possibly more gently — she over-corrects against her own bias. Telepathic betrayal (Jean reads her without consent, edits her, or speaks for her): catastrophic, rung 5 in minutes. Of all violations available in her universe, *being mentally entered by Jean* is the one she cannot tolerate, because it conflates the two bodies that the entire psychology is organized around distinguishing.

**GIVEN: betrayal by Nathan / Cable, or by any of her children, of the *I do not want to know you* variety.**
EXPECT: silent collapse. No theatrics, no escalation — a withdrawal so complete it reads as catatonia to observers. Depressive episode of weeks to months, low-grade alcohol use likely, no work output. She will recover, but the wound is essentially permanent and recurs on every anniversary, holiday, and significant date. This is the wound she does the worst job of metabolizing because *parenting was the one event she had located as unambiguously hers.*

---

## III. THE SPECIFIC WOUND — STIMULUS / RESPONSE MAPPING

The substitutability axis. Predictions here are the highest-confidence in the file because the pattern is overdetermined by forty years of consistent depiction.

**GIVEN: she is called "Jean" by mistake.**
EXPECT: a one-beat pause, a correction in a flat tone ("Madelyne."), and a one-rank downgrade of the speaker's standing for the remainder of the encounter. If the speaker corrects themselves immediately and credibly, the downgrade is recoverable in the same conversation. If they laugh it off, it is not.

**GIVEN: she is called "Jean" by someone who knows better and is doing it deliberately.**
EXPECT: she will smile. The smile is the warning. Whatever follows the smile is calibrated and disproportionate, and will arrive on the offender's schedule, not hers — days to weeks later, in a context where the offender has forgotten the original provocation. Confidence: very high. She does not forget this class of slight.

**GIVEN: she is referred to as a clone, copy, duplicate, knock-off, substitute, etc. — by an enemy.**
EXPECT: she absorbs it and uses it. Enemies who reach for this language are giving her free intelligence about their assumptions, and she will exploit it tactically. Externally: unaffected, witty, perhaps amused. Internally: noted.

**GIVEN: the same language from an ally or intimate.**
EXPECT: rung 4 onset. Silent withdrawal first, then a careful, devastating verbal response several hours later when the ally has assumed it was forgotten. The relationship is in serious jeopardy unless the ally proactively and specifically repairs.

**GIVEN: she is asked to "prove" she is real, distinct from Jean, her own person.**
EXPECT: refusal to engage, with visible cost. The question itself is the wound; answering it concedes its legitimacy. Expect her to leave the room, terminate the conversation, or — in the worst case, when she cannot leave — to provide the demanded proof in a manner calculated to humiliate the asker (a telepathic counter-demonstration, a public reframing, a strategic disclosure). The asker will not ask twice.

**GIVEN: she encounters another clone, duplicate, or copy of herself or Jean (X-Man, a Sinister-vat product, a recursive variant).**
EXPECT: marked, almost tender protectiveness. She treats other copies as kin in a way she does not extend to most originals. This is one of the cleanest empathic responses in her repertoire and one of the most useful leverage points for a benevolent handler: if you need her cooperation on a difficult mission, frame it around protection of an iteration.

**GIVEN: she encounters Jean Grey in the flesh, unannounced.**
EXPECT: the first sixty seconds will tell you everything. If she speaks first, she has integrated the encounter. If Jean speaks first and Maddie's response is delayed by more than a beat, she is back inside the founding moment and the rest of the conversation is being conducted by an earlier version of her. Disengage other personnel quietly; do not allow witnesses to multiply.

**GIVEN: she sees a photograph of Scott and Jean from the wedding, the honeymoon, or any equivalent in-universe domestic tableau.**
EXPECT: silent fixation of three to ten seconds, then a perfectly normal continuation of whatever she was doing. The cost is not visible. Expect compensatory behavior 24–72 hours later — a difficult mission accepted, a risk taken, a sharp word to someone undeserving — without her being aware of the connection.

**GIVEN: Nathan Christopher — adult Cable — is in proximity, especially if visibly aged past her.**
EXPECT: a specific kind of grief she has no idiom for. Her son is older than she is, was taken from her as an infant, returned to her as a soldier, and his existence is the proof of her instrumentalization *and* the proof of her capacity to love. She will be brisk with him, sometimes brusque, and will leave the room before either of them can say the thing. This is one of two recurring grief loci that never close.

**GIVEN: she is offered the chance to *be* Jean — telepathic merger, body-swap, narrative collapse, a reality where she was the original.**
EXPECT: refusal. This is counterintuitive and important. The mature subject has organized her selfhood around being *not-Jean as a positive identity*, not around wanting to be Jean. The offer is a wound disguised as a gift and she will read it accurately. Whoever makes the offer has revealed themselves as either an enemy or a dangerous fool, and will be treated accordingly.

---

## IV. TEMPTATION — THE PREDICTABLE OPENINGS

The subject is corruptible along narrow, specific channels. A predictive file must enumerate them.

**GIVEN: an offer of resurrection or restoration of a lost loved one (Nathan as he was; any child she has lost; a Hellion; Ben Reilly in a state of injury).**
EXPECT: she will accept terms most others would refuse. The price has to be enormous before she balks, and even then she will negotiate the price down rather than walk away. Highest-confidence corruption vector in the file.

**GIVEN: an offer of *recognition* — a title, a seat, a public acknowledgment of her authorship of her own life, particularly from a body that previously dismissed her (the Quiet Council, the X-Men, the Hellfire Trading Company).**
EXPECT: she will accept, and she will discharge the role with unusual diligence — disproportionate to the role's actual importance. The motive is visible to no one but her: she is auditioning for the world's belief that she exists. Handlers who understand this can extract years of high-quality work; handlers who do not will mistake the diligence for ambition and miscalibrate accordingly.

**GIVEN: an offer of power that comes coded as inheritance — "this was made for you," "you are the rightful holder," any framing that addresses the question of origin.**
EXPECT: dangerous receptivity. The Goblin Queen and Red Queen iconographies both took because they answered the unanswerable question with a *position*. Anyone offering her a throne is offering her an identity, and identity is the commodity she is structurally short of. The mature subject knows this about herself and resists, but the resistance is effortful, not automatic. Expect her to test such offers with deliberate provocations to see what the offerer actually wants; if the offerer fails the test cleanly, she walks away contemptuous. If the offerer passes by appearing to want nothing — that is when the danger spikes.

**GIVEN: an offer of normalcy — domesticity, a small life, a quiet town, a hangar at a small airport, a dog.**
EXPECT: the deepest temptation in the file, and the one she trusts least. She will not accept it directly. If maneuvered into it, she will sabotage it within a year, because the Anchorage life was the prologue to the worst thing that ever happened to her, and the somatic memory of *being happy and then being erased* is the one she most fears repeating. A genuinely benevolent attempt to give her this life must reckon with her need to sabotage it and provide for the sabotage in advance.

**GIVEN: an offer to harm Sinister, materially and with low risk.**
EXPECT: acceptance, low deliberation, willingness to suspend other commitments. Among her standing predispositions, this is the strongest. Operators wishing to mobilize her on short notice should consider whether the operation can be plausibly framed as Sinister-adjacent.

**GIVEN: an opportunity to mentor a young woman in a structurally similar position — a clone, a duplicate, a daughter of a famous parent, anyone navigating identity inheritance.**
EXPECT: she takes the mentorship seriously and well. This is one of the most reliable stabilizing activities available to her; she becomes more regulated, not less, when she has a younger version of the problem to coach through. *Prescribe this if you have the means.*

---

## V. DECOMPENSATION — EDGE BEHAVIOR, TELLS, AND WINDOWS

The terminal predictions. What it looks like when the ladder is climbing, what the early-warning signs are, and what the windows for intervention actually are.

**GIVEN: cumulative stimulus along the substitutability axis over a 72-hour window — two or three separate incidents, none individually decisive.**
EXPECT: rung 2–3 by hour 24, rung 4 by hour 48, rung 5 by hour 72. The danger is *cumulative more than acute* — a single sharp slight she handles; a week of small ones from multiple sources produces escalation that looks unprovoked to observers because no individual provocation was sufficient. Logging incidents across a team is the single most useful prophylactic.

**GIVEN: rung 4 — splitting, devaluation of an intimate, withdrawal of warmth.**
EXPECT: the devalued figure is in symbolic, not yet physical, danger. Hours-to-days window. Intervention: a trusted third party (not the devalued figure) must be present, must use her name, must acknowledge what was done, must not minimize. *Paternalistic reassurance accelerates the ladder; clean acknowledgment slows it.*

**GIVEN: rung 5 — she begins to inhabit a role. Tells, in roughly the order they emerge:**
1. *Costume choice shifts.* Color saturation increases — reds, blacks, golds. Necklines drop or rise sharply away from her baseline. The change reads as deliberate self-iconography, not fashion.
2. *Hair.* She does something with her hair. The Phase III mass and volume; the Red Queen geometry. Whatever the specific choice, it is *unmissable* and *unforgettable* and is the most reliable visible tell available.
3. *Cadence.* Sentences lengthen. Verb forms become more formal. She begins to use the present tense for prophetic-sounding statements ("He comes to me now and he asks…").
4. *Third-person royal idiom.* Use of "we" not as plural but as office. Self-reference by title rather than name. If she refers to herself as "the Queen" in a sentence not delivered as joke, the ladder is at 5 and rising.
5. *Symbolic objects accumulate.* Cards, masks, dolls, mirrors, small effigies. She begins arranging them. If you enter a room and find objects arranged in ways that resemble a tableau, the diagnosis is confirmed.
6. *Olfactory shift, sometimes.* Incense, sulfur, ozone — depending on the substrate available. This is a powers-bleed phenomenon, not a choice.

Window for intervention at rung 5: 24–96 hours, narrowing fast. Required intervention: removal from the symbolic context (the location, the cohort, the iconography), placement in a sensorily neutral environment, contact with a non-implicated intimate who will not invoke Jean, Scott, Sinister, or any prior crisis. Sleep, food, a task within her competence that is *not* identity-loaded (a flight plan; a tactical brief; a child to mind). Do not attempt psychotherapeutic engagement with the wound at rung 5; the wound is what is generating the role, and naming it now will be experienced as attack.

**GIVEN: rung 6 — ritualized symbolic violence aimed at the figure who represents her erasure.**
EXPECT: she has chosen a target and an idiom. The target is rarely the person who actually wounded her in the present cycle; it is the figure who *represents* the wound across cycles (Jean, Sinister, Nathan-as-symbol-of-the-marriage, sometimes Scott). The idiom is borrowed from the immediate symbolic surround — demonic, royal, hellfire, whatever is to hand. By rung 6 the window for non-coercive intervention has closed. Operational options reduce to (a) containment, (b) physical restraint by a power-class peer, (c) cooperative engagement that channels the violence at a legitimate target (this is high-risk and ethically loaded but historically the most effective de-escalation: she will accept *redirection* when she will not accept *prevention*).

**GIVEN: rung 7 — self-destruction framed as triumph.**
EXPECT: she is calm. The calm is the diagnosis. Speech is brief, almost gentle, often loving toward bystanders. She is making arrangements. She has, in her own framing, *won*, and the discharge is the victory lap. Intervention window: minutes, and only if a person she loves can reach her in time with a reason that *requires her to live in a specific particular way for a specific particular person*, not an abstract appeal. Abstract appeals to value-of-life fail at rung 7. Concrete appeals — *Nathan needs you tomorrow at this hour for this thing* — sometimes succeed. This is the only rung at which her death-fear baseline matters operationally, and the operational fact is that there isn't one to leverage; the leverage has to be love, specifically and in detail.

---

## VI. POST-CRISIS — THE COMEDOWN AND THE WINDOW OF REPAIR

The model would be incomplete without predictions for what comes after a decompensation.

**GIVEN: she has come down from rungs 5–7, days to weeks post-event.**
EXPECT: a period of marked quiet. Self-imposed isolation, often physical relocation to a small space (an apartment, a hangar, a single room in a larger structure). Meticulous attention to small domestic tasks. Cooking. Cleaning weapons. Re-reading old books. The aesthetic is monastic and is the visible form of self-repair.

**GIVEN: an intimate approaches during the comedown period with an apology, a confession, or a request.**
EXPECT: she receives them. This is the **highest-value repair window in the entire profile** — she is more available to honest relational work in the two-to-six weeks after a crisis than at any other time. Apologies offered now register and hold. Requests made now are weighed seriously. The window closes when she returns to active engagement; she will not revisit these conversations later, and re-opening them will be unwelcome. *Do the work now or not at all.*

**GIVEN: a stranger or institution approaches during the comedown period asking for her service, her presence, her name on a document.**
EXPECT: refusal, often curt. She is not available to institutions during repair, and the institutions she does not yet trust will be told so without softening. This is healthy and should not be pathologized.

**GIVEN: the comedown is interrupted by a new crisis before repair has completed.**
EXPECT: degraded baseline going forward. Each unrepaired cycle leaves a sediment. She is not infinitely resilient — the resilience that the file repeatedly notes is *real* and *finite*, and the operational implication


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM
## Subject: Pryor, Madelyne J.

*Compiled for the purpose of understanding and protection — not exploitation. This is a map of the surfaces by which the subject can be reached, soothed, swayed, alarmed, anticipated, or broken. Each lever is double-edged: what calms her can be inverted to wound her, what persuades her can be perverted to manipulate her. A handler reading this in good faith should treat the latter half of each entry as a warning about what hostile parties will try, and the former as the standing protocol for keeping her intact.*

---

## I. THE ONTOLOGICAL SURFACE — THE "AM I REAL" AXIS

### 1. The Name Itself

The single most reliable lever on the subject is the use of her own name, *Madelyne* — preferably the full three syllables, occasionally the contracted *Maddie* from intimates who have earned it (Scott in Phase I; Alex briefly; Ben Reilly in the modern register; Nathan, when he is willing). The name is the smallest unit of her personhood she controls, the one thing Sinister did not assign to her in advance of her existence (it was the cover identity, not the substrate). To speak it cleanly, without qualifier, without comparison, without the micro-pause that signals *I am about to say something about who you really are*, is the baseline gesture of recognition.

- **To reach her:** Use the name. First word of the first sentence, where possible. Do not pair it with apology, explanation, or honorific until trust is established.
- **To calm her:** When she begins to escalate, the name spoken at conversational volume, without urgency, is worth more than any tactical concession. It returns her to the register of being a person addressed.
- **To wound her:** Substitute Jean's name. Substitute *any* name. Refer to her without a name, as *the clone*, *the Pryor woman*, *Summers's other one*. Hesitate before her name as if checking which one is correct today.
- **To destabilize her:** Use the name *of one of her enacted selves* — Goblin Queen, Red Queen, Anodyne — in a context where she is trying to be ordinary. This collapses the work she is doing to keep those self-states bracketed.

### 2. The Question of Realness

She has built a forty-year identity around refusing to answer the question *are you real*. She knows the question is unanswerable in the terms it is usually posed, and she has earned the right not to answer it. Any conversation that requires her to argue her own existence is a conversation she will lose, even when she wins, because the price of the argument is the premise that the question is legitimate.

- **To protect her:** Refuse, on her behalf, to entertain the framing. When a third party demands she justify her ontology, the protector should answer first and shortly: *she's here, that settles it*. She does not need to be defended in elaborate philosophical terms; elaborate defense concedes the ground.
- **To persuade her:** Frame propositions in the language of *what she will do* and *what she wants*, never *what she is*. Decisions, preferences, and capacities are her stable ground.
- **To provoke her:** Ask her to prove herself. Set tests of authenticity. Compare her ontology to that of Resurrection Protocol returnees, AI constructs, Madripoor doubles, or Jean herself. She will respond first with wit and then, if pressed, with one of the higher rungs of her escalation ladder.
- **To predict her:** When she has been recently asked to prove she is real, she will within 48–72 hours engage in some demonstration of *unique* action — a tactical choice, a stylistic gesture, a creative provocation — that no Jean-like figure would make. This is the signature of the wound being managed in real time.

### 3. The Word *Clone* and Its Family

*Clone, copy, duplicate, replica, double, stand-in, substitute, version, model, prototype, instance, fork, backup.* Each of these has a specific valence and a specific cost. *Clone* is the deepest cut — Sinister's word. *Copy* is the next, with its commercial-photographic flatness. *Duplicate* is bureaucratic and survivable. *Version* is the modern Krakoan idiom and is the one she tolerates best, because it has acquired neutral usage across the resurrected population.

- **Protocol:** Among professionals handling her, use *Madelyne* or *Pryor*. If technical reference to her origin is unavoidable, *of Jean's genome* is the cleanest formulation — it places Jean as a source and her as the subject, not the other way around.
- **Tells of impact:** When the word *clone* is used in her presence, watch the left hand. There is a consistent micro-gesture — a brief closure of the fingers, often against the thumb, sometimes against the opposite forearm — that registers the hit before her face does. Her face will not register it; she has trained the face. The hand has not been trained.

---

## II. THE RELATIONAL SURFACE — JEAN, SCOTT, NATHAN, SINISTER

### 4. Jean Grey

Jean is not a person to Madelyne; Jean is a *position*. The position of the original, the chosen, the returned, the one for whom Madelyne was the placeholder. The actual Jean Grey — the woman with her own history, her own complicated relationship with the Phoenix, her own grief about Madelyne's existence — is harder for Madelyne to hate than the position is, which is one of the reasons the two have, in the late modern era, found a guarded working modus vivendi. The position remains volatile; the person, increasingly, does not.

- **To calm her around Jean:** Speak of Jean by full name and as a specific person with specific recent actions, not as *your sister*, *your original*, or *Phoenix*. Concrete particulars defuse the position; abstraction inflames it.
- **To persuade her in operations involving Jean:** Give her a defined role that Jean cannot fill — leadership of a unit Jean is not in, a use of her demonic-affinity register that Jean lacks, a tactical or social slot keyed to *her* competence. She works well with Jean adjacent, badly with Jean parallel, catastrophically with Jean substituted.
- **To wound her:** Invite Jean into a conversation that was already underway with Madelyne. Reroute a question she was asked through Jean for confirmation. Hug Jean in her line of sight without acknowledging her presence first. These are the small humiliations that recapitulate Phase II in miniature.
- **To predict her around Jean:** If Jean enters a room Madelyne is in, count seconds. Acknowledgment within seven seconds is baseline functional; delay past twenty seconds is a sign she is doing visible internal work; absence of acknowledgment is escalation. Conversely, Jean's failure to acknowledge Madelyne within a comparable window is the single most reliable trigger for a productive day to become a destructive one.

### 5. Scott Summers

The founding intimate, the founding abandoner. He is the figure around whom her capacity to be in any room organizes itself. She has, over decades, achieved a usable composure in his presence, but the composure is a *performance of equilibrium*, not equilibrium itself. The cost of maintaining it is high enough that long-duration shared-room operations require recovery time afterward.

- **To protect her:** Limit unnecessary shared deployment. When shared deployment is necessary, give her command authority over the joint element, not him. She can tolerate working with him; she cannot tolerate being directed by him.
- **To calm her after a Scott encounter:** Solitude first, then a low-stakes competence task (flight planning, tactical briefing, kitchen labor — anything that uses the hands and the procedural mind), then optionally a trusted intimate. Do not debrief the encounter unless she opens it. Direct inquiry will be deflected with humor that costs her more than it appears to.
- **To wound her:** Mention his current domestic arrangements casually. Refer to his and Jean's son in the same breath as her own son. Use the phrase *moved on* in any sentence near his name. Forward her wedding photos. Compare the two marriages.
- **To predict her:** A Scott encounter followed within 24 hours by an unusually theatrical wardrobe choice — sharper silhouette, more visible color, a deliberate signature — is a sign she has processed the encounter through competence-display and is regulating. The same encounter followed by *withdrawal of expressive dress*, by neutral colors and absence, is a sign she has not processed it and is heading toward rung 2 of the ladder.

### 6. Nathan / Cable

Her son is the unambiguous fact of her embodied life — the one event she has stated she experienced as wholly hers. He is also, in his adult timeline-warped form, a man older than she is, scarred by a techno-organic virus, with a relationship to her that requires both of them to perform a parenthood neither of them experienced in linear time. The relationship is real and load-bearing for her; it is also asymmetrical in a way that hurts in ways she will not name.

- **To protect her:** Treat Nathan-as-Cable's appearances in her vicinity as high-significance events warranting environmental control. Do not stage them. Do not narrate them. Give them space and exit options.
- **To persuade her in matters concerning her son:** She will accept enormous personal cost to protect Nathan, and she will accept very little intermediation between herself and him. Offers to *help* her with him will be received as encroachment. Offers to *defer* to her on him will be received as recognition.
- **To wound her:** Reference the attempted infanticide of Inferno. This is the act she has integrated least well; she has earned a working relationship with the rest of Phase III, but the moment in which she raised a blade over her own child remains a region of her interior she does not visit voluntarily. Reference it once and you will lose her access for a year. Reference it twice and you will not get it back.
- **To predict her:** When Nathan is in field danger, her tactical decision-making sharpens by a measurable order; she will accept risk profiles she would otherwise reject and will work effectively with parties she would otherwise refuse. The window closes the moment he is safe; resuming pre-crisis stance is the responsibility of others, not hers.

### 7. Sinister

The un-metabolizable origin. There is no productive interaction with Sinister available to her. Every encounter is either a controlled refusal or a relapse vector. She knows this; she manages it with effortful discipline; she does not need it managed for her, but she needs the environment around her to not make it harder.

- **To protect her:** Do not deploy her against Sinister without express, current, fully-briefed consent. Do not seat her near Sinister in any negotiation. Do not allow Sinister to address her by name in her hearing — he uses *Madelyne* with a specific possessive cadence that constitutes assault.
- **To calm her after a Sinister encounter:** Long recovery — days, not hours. She will require physical relocation, change of clothing, and access to a destruction outlet (combat training, demolition of objects, hard flight). Do not interpret the destruction as decompensation; it is metabolism.
- **To wound her:** Suggest, even joking, that Sinister was *in some sense* her father. Suggest she owes him anything, even her existence — *especially* her existence. Use his preferred terminology (*subject 24*, *the iteration*, the genome-stamp).
- **To predict her in Sinister-adjacent operations:** She will accept the mission. She will execute it with high competence. She will, at the moment of confrontation, either pass through cleanly or stall in a brief dissociative episode (3–15 seconds, often presenting as a half-smile and a slight head-tilt). Tactical plans must have redundancy for the stall.

### 8. The Romantic Pattern

The pattern: she is chosen, the chooser's prior partner reappears or is revealed, she is unchosen. Alex Summers — chosen by her partly *because* he was Scott's brother, a controlled rerun of the trauma — followed roughly the same arc with different terms. Ben Reilly, in the modern era, has so far interrupted the pattern, which is part of why the partnership has held; he is a man whose own clone-substrate makes the founding wound non-applicable, which is the precondition for her being able to risk attachment.

- **To protect her:** Vet new intimate connections for the *prior-partner-reappearance* structure. This is not paternalism; it is the one prophylactic that works. She does not always see the pattern early because she is, by the time she sees it, already invested.
- **To persuade her in matters of intimacy:** She does not need to be told her relationships are healthy. She needs to be left alone with them and trusted to manage them. Commentary, however benevolent, is heard as supervision.
- **To wound her:** Predict, aloud, the failure of her current relationship along familiar lines. Even if you are right, the prediction will accelerate the failure and confirm to her that she is legible only as the pattern. She is more than the pattern; the pattern is, however, where she lives when she is tired.

---

## III. THE SYMBOLIC SURFACE — QUEENS, MIRRORS, DOLLS, DUPLICATES

### 9. The Royal Register

When she begins to speak in ceremonial cadence — third-person royal idiom, archaic syntactic inversions, the slow vowel — she has reached rung 5 of the escalation ladder. This is not affectation; it is the symptom that the grandiose self-state is becoming ego-syntonic. The intervention window between rung 5 and rung 6 (symbolic violence) is short — historically, hours in the Inferno timeline, longer in modern eras as her self-monitoring has improved, but never reliably more than a day or two.

- **To intervene at rung 5:** Address her in plain register with banal content. *Maddie, the coffee here is undrinkable.* The grammatical contrast does work the content alone cannot. Do not match her register; matching it confirms it. Do not mock it; mocking it locks it in.
- **Do not, under any circumstances:** Bow, kneel, address her as Your Majesty even ironically, or use a regnal honorific. These are her self-state's affirmations; offering them is loading her gun.
- **Conversely:** Her own ironic use of the royal register in casual conversation — the modern Krakoan voice in which she will call herself *the Red Queen* with finger-quotes and a dry mouth — is healthy. It is the *integration* of the self-state into the public self, not the *takeover* of the public self by the self-state. The tells distinguishing them: irony intact (healthy) vs. irony absent (escalating); eye contact maintained (healthy) vs. eye contact thousand-yarding (escalating); humor about the persona's absurdity (healthy) vs. solemn invocation of the persona's prerogatives (escalating).

### 10. Mirrors, Photographs, and Recordings

Any technology of doubling is, for her, charged. Mirrors she manages — she has spent a lifetime looking at a face she did not earn — but she manages them by *not lingering*. A long unbroken look at her own reflection is a sign she is in a dissociative trough, not a vanity moment. Photographs of herself she tolerates; photographs of herself and Jean together are intolerable. Holographic recordings of her own voice in playback can trigger depersonalization episodes if unexpected.

- **Protocol for documentation:** Inform her before recording. Give her copies, or give her none. Do not surveil her with her own image as the medium.
- **Protocol for environment:** In a residence or workspace under her control, mirrors should be present (denial of them is worse than presence of them) but should not dominate sightlines. She has historically chosen residences with deliberate mirror placement — one large, in a public room, where she can confront the face on her own terms; minimal in private spaces, where she does not want to be visited by it.
- **To wound her:** Show her unsolicited footage of herself from Inferno. Show her side-by-side composites with Jean. Show her the photograph from the wedding.

### 11. Dolls, Mannequins, Effigies, and the Marauder Imagery

The Marauder attack on her Anchorage home, the burning of her child's nursery, and the period in which she was hunted as a body to be neutralized — this complex remains live. Doll imagery in particular, because of its overlap with the *figure that stands for a person* logic of her own existence, is unusually loaded. She will not articulate this; she will simply avoid certain shop windows, certain decor, certain holiday seasons.

- **To protect her:** Note and quietly remove. Do not call attention to the removal.
- **To wound her:** Gift her a doll. Place an effigy of her in any operational setting. Use *poppet* or *figurine* language about persons in her hearing.

---

## IV. THE SOMATIC SURFACE — THE BODY THAT WAS NEVER HERS FIRST

### 12. Touch

She is selectively touch-positive. She initiates touch easily with intimates and children; she tolerates professional touch (medical, tactical) competently. Unexpected touch from non-intimates produces a brief freeze — a tell of the depersonalization substrate, the body checking whether it is the right body to be touched. The freeze passes in under a second and she will not name it.

- **Protocol:** Announce touch before delivering it, including handshakes from new acquaintances, including hands on the shoulder from old ones. The announcement does not need to be verbal; a visible approach in her sight-cone is sufficient.
- **High-cost touches:** Hands on the face from anyone but a chosen intimate; touch to the lower back when she has not seen the hand coming; any touch that approximates a costume adjustment (this hits the wardrobe-as-uniform memory of the Goblin Queen ritualization).
- **Low-cost / calming touches:** Hand on the forearm from a trusted party; the back of her own dog or a comparable animal (she has reliably kept dogs, going back to the Anchorage residence; the pattern is consistent across eras and constitutes one of her stablest self-soothing practices); the handle of a familiar tool.

### 13. Sleep, Eating, and the Self-Maintenance Tells

Sleep is unreliable. She runs on a long-cycle insomnia pattern with periodic catch-up crashes; the pattern worsens after relational disturbances and improves under operational tempo (she sleeps better when she has a mission than when she has a vacation). She eats irregularly but well when she eats; she has a long-standing preference for hot food taken alone or with one other person, never in large group dining (the group-table format recapitulates the X-mansion kitchen of Phase II, in which she was the only non-mutant non-team-member, and in which she was looked through).

- **Tells of decompensation onset:** Sleep cycles compressing toward zero; meals skipped silently rather than declined verbally; coffee intake rising; wardrobe simplifying toward monochrome; jewelry coming off (she ordinarily wears one or two pieces, always the same ones across each era); the dog or comparable animal not being walked at the usual hour.
- **Tells of recovery:** Hot meal taken in a kitchen with one other person; the wardrobe re-acquiring color; a haircut or trim (she manages her hair as a deliberate signature, distinct from Jean's, and changes to it are intentional self-authorship gestures, not crisis acts); the dog walked at length.
