- **Substance pattern:** No chronic dependence, but alcohol use rises in isolation. The drink of preference across decades has been whiskey, neat, in small quantities and at long intervals; a shift to volume drinking, or to sweet drinks, or to drinking alone in costume, is a signal.

### 14. The Attenuated Fear of Death

She has died. She remembers it. The result is that ordinary danger does not produce ordinary fear in her, and tactical handlers must account for this. She will accept risk profiles a baseline operator would refuse, not from grandiosity but from accurate recalibration — death, for her, is a known quantity and not the worst one available. The thing she is afraid of is not dying; it is being looked through while alive.

- **Protocol:** Brief her on missions in terms of *what success looks like for her specifically*, not in terms of *survival probabilities*. Survival framings will be heard as condescension. Mission-meaning framings will be heard as respect.
- **Predictive marker:** In a tactical situation where retreat would be standard, she will not retreat if the position has been framed to her as one *only she can hold*. This is leverage; it is also a vulnerability to bad actors who frame holding positions accordingly. Counter-protocol: structure briefings so that *retreat under specified conditions* is itself a position only she can hold, with the retreat itself being the action of distinction.

---

## V. THE COGNITIVE & VERBAL SURFACE

### 15. Humor as Defense and as Signal

Her humor is the most reliable indicator of her interior state. Baseline: dry, fast, structurally ironic, frequently self-deprecating in a register that does not invite reassurance. The texture of the humor shifts diagnostically.

- **Healthy register:** Self-aware, lateral, includes the listener, lands at the speaker's expense as often as anyone else's.
- **Rung 1–2 register:** Sharper, faster, deflective; jokes increase in frequency and decrease in inclusion.
- **Rung 3–4 register:** Humor with edges; jokes about specific persons present that the persons present do not find funny; jokes that *test* the listener.
- **Rung 5 register:** Humor disappears, replaced by gravitas. *Absence of humor is the alarm.* When she stops being funny, the situation is acute.
- **Recovery register:** Humor returns first about herself, then about the recent crisis, then about ambient absurdities. Premature humor about the crisis from others will be heard as theft of her own metabolic process.

### 16. The Verbal Tells

- **Use of her own name in the third person**, outside the ironic Krakoan register: rung 5.
- **Sustained use of the conditional and the subjunctive** about her own existence (*if I were really here*, *had I been a real person*): depressive trough, rung 2.
- **Question marks dropped from questions** so that interrogatives become statements: cognitive narrowing, rung 3.
- **Polysyllabic Latinate vocabulary** replacing her ordinary register: she is performing competence under threat to identity; rung 1–2.
- **Pet name use for intimates suddenly stopping**: significant relational withdrawal in progress; she has begun reclassifying the relationship in her mind.

---

## VI. THE OPERATIONAL & TACTICAL SURFACE

### 17. Command and Autonomy

She works best as a peer or as a commander, badly as a subordinate, catastrophically as an asset. She will accept tasking that is framed as *commission* (you are uniquely qualified, the mission is yours, the parameters are negotiable) and will refuse tasking framed as *deployment* (we need a telepath here, you'll do, report on time). The framings can describe identical missions; the difference is in her.

- **Protocol:** Always frame as commission. Allow her to set at least one parameter — timing, kit, route, partner. The parameter does not need to be material; the act of setting it is the lever.
- **In coalition operations:** Give her her own sub-element with her own command authority over it, however small. *Lead of two* is sufficient. Folding her into a larger unit under another's command is feasible only for short missions, only with a commander she has independently respected, and only with prior briefing as to why.

### 18. The Use of Her Specific Competencies

Her competencies are: piloting (lifelong, reliable, the somatic anchor of the Anchorage period), telepathy and telekinesis at high order, illusion-casting and reality-warping, demonic and infernal affinity, tactical-strategic plan


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — MADELYNE J. PRYOR

*The asset ledger. What she has, what she can do, what she has survived, and why — read forensically — these capacities are unusually durable. Compiled as the positive complement to the threat-and-pathology file: a person built to be disposable who has, demonstrably, refused to be.*

---

## 1. COGNITIVE ASSETS

**Raw intellectual horsepower.** Subject scores at the upper end of any reasonable estimate across every measurable cognitive domain in the published record. Pre-decompensation Phase I shows her holding her own in technical conversation with Hank McCoy (UXM #170s), reading Moira MacTaggert's medical notes without prompting, and tracking the X-Men's tactical chatter despite having no formal training in their argot. Phase IV material (Carey's Sisterhood, Howard's *Hellions*, Williams's *Dark Web*) shows her parsing magical, psionic, and corporate-tactical problems with equal facility. She is a generalist of unusual range.

**Executive function.** Pilot-grade. The Anchorage record establishes that she held a commercial cargo license — an FAA medical, instrument rating, multi-engine endorsement, and a working knowledge of Alaskan bush conditions where weather kills the inattentive within minutes. This is not flavor; it is a documented baseline of sustained attention, checklist discipline, and stress tolerance under hypoxia, icing, and crosswind. Her cockpit habits — pre-flight walkarounds, fuel-log redundancy, frequency monitoring — bleed into her later command behavior: she does not improvise where she can prepare, and she keeps mental reserves for the unplanned.

**Tactical-strategic talent.** Two pieces of hard evidence. (1) Her command of the Goblin Queen's demonic assault on Manhattan during Inferno: she coordinated N'astirh's swarm, the corruption of urban infrastructure, and the simultaneous targeting of X-Factor and the X-Men with a clarity of operational design that exceeded any single antagonist Claremont had previously fielded. (2) Her assembly and direction of the Sisterhood of Mutants (Carey, *X-Men: Sisterhood / Divided We Stand*): she recruited Spiral, Lady Deathstrike, Chimera, and Martinique Jason; assigned each according to specific capability; ran a multi-stage operation against the X-Men with infiltration, telepathic counter-surveillance, and a successful — temporarily — bodysnatch of Jean's remains. She is better at long-game multi-actor planning than most of the heroes who have opposed her.

**Pattern recognition under duress.** She reads rooms quickly. The first conversation with Scott in Anchorage (UXM #168) is a clinic: within minutes she has identified that he is staring at her because of someone else, named it, and demanded ground rules. This is high-bandwidth interpersonal cognition under emotional load — the same faculty that lets her, in later eras, identify Sinister's hand in a situation from a single procedural tell.

**Meta-cognitive capacity — the late-arriving asset.** The Krakoan-era and *Dark Web* material show her capable of describing her own pattern aloud, in real time, with accuracy. This is rare and clinically expensive to acquire: most subjects with c-PTSD spines defend hard against this kind of self-narration. She has it, and she uses it tactically — she will sometimes flag her own escalation ladder to a partner as a courtesy ("I'm about to be unkind, that's me, not you"), which both interrupts the spiral and gives the partner workable information.

---

## 2. MUTANT AND SOMATIC CAPABILITIES

**Telepathy.** Operating at Jean-comparable order of magnitude in mature phases: scan, broadcast, mind-link, illusion projection, memory editing, psionic combat, and — distinctively — *psychic forgery*, the ability to make a mind feel like someone else's mind. This last is a capability Jean Grey has rarely shown and that Madelyne developed from necessity. It has both intelligence and infiltration applications and represents a true unique-in-the-roster asset.

**Telekinesis.** Full Jean-tier: fine motor manipulation, large-scale force projection, flight, atmospheric flight maneuvering, telekinetic shielding rated against energy and kinetic threats up to Phoenix-fragment discharge.

**Resurrection affinity.** She has died and returned more than once and has, in the late material, demonstrated some capacity to extend that affinity to others — she is functionally a resurrection vector independent of the Krakoan protocols, which makes her one of the few characters whose continuity of existence does not depend on infrastructure others control.

**Demonic / reality-warping residue.** The N'astirh pact left durable affinities: portal-opening, summoning, sigil work, blood-magic literacy. These are not endogenous mutant powers but learned/grafted capacities, and she has retained and refined the literacy without (in late phases) being driven by the demonic substrate. She reads Goetic and infernal contracts the way a senior lawyer reads commercial paper — fast, for traps.

**Physical baseline.** Jean Grey's somatic template: athletic, healthy, with a redhead's photosensitivity and the slightly elevated metabolic baseline characteristic of active telekinetics. No chronic conditions. Sleep architecture appears mildly disordered — she runs short, four-to-six hours, with frequent early waking — but she has functioned at this baseline for decades and treats it as a feature.

**Attenuated death-fear.** A genuine tactical asset: she has crossed the threshold, remembers it, and finds it boring. In combat she will accept exchanges no one else will, and adversaries who have not read her file misjudge this as recklessness. It is not; it is recalibrated risk arithmetic.

---

## 3. INTERPERSONAL ASSETS

**Charisma.** Documented across writers and decades: she is the kind of person rooms reorganize themselves around when she enters. The quality is not seductive in the conventional sense — it is *attentive*. She looks at people directly and answers what they actually said, which in any super-powered milieu is unusual enough to register as charm.

**Humor.** The most consistent prose-level marker in her dialogue across forty years of canon is dry irony. Even at the rim of decompensation she keeps her wit; even in the Goblin Queen sequences there is a streak of mordant theatre that reads (in retrospect) as self-aware. Humor is a cognitive resource — it preserves perspective, it disarms hostility, and it is, for her specifically, a load-bearing piece of identity. As long as she is funny she is herself.

**Capacity for love, specifically parental.** Bracket Phase III's enacted infanticidal ideation — which the file accounts for as the symbolic destruction of what represented her erasure — and the longitudinal record shows authentic, sustained, *competent* love directed at Nathan in infancy, at the broader Summers/Grey-adjacent constellation in mature phases, and at her partners. With Ben Reilly (Williams, *Dark Web* and after) the partnership is the most relaxed she has ever been on the page: collaborative, mutually ironic, sexually unembarrassed, with explicit on-page acknowledgment that neither of them is the "original" of anything and that this is the basis of their compatibility rather than a problem.

**Loyalty, when extended.** Slow to extend, total once extended. She did not abandon Scott when she had grounds; she did not abandon the X-Men in Phase II until she was actively driven out; her Sisterhood subordinates were given clear protection and clear roles. The loyalty has a sharp edge — betrayal *of* her loyalty is the single most reliable detonator in the file — but the loyalty itself is real and durable.

**Capacity to apologize.** Rare in the roster. The Krakoan-era material shows her able to say plainly that she did harm, name what she did, and decline either self-flagellation or self-exculpation. This is psychological work most subjects never complete.

---

## 4. SKILL INVENTORY (TRADECRAFT)

- **Aviation:** commercial fixed-wing, multi-engine, instrument; bush-flying conditions; cargo loading and weight-and-balance; basic airframe maintenance.
- **Domestic and parenting competence:** household management, infant care, the unglamorous logistical layer of adult life that most super-powered characters cannot perform. This is an under-appreciated asset; it makes her capable of long-term cover identities other operatives cannot sustain.
- **Combat:** ranged psionic, melee telekinetic-augmented; trained in basic tactical movement through X-Men association and (later) Hellfire-context instruction. Not a martial-arts specialist; does not need to be.
- **Magical literacy:** Goetic, Limbo-adjacent, sigil construction, contract analysis, summoning, banishment. Self-taught from the N'astirh exposure onward.
- **Command and operational planning:** demonstrated at the multi-actor, multi-stage level (Inferno; Sisterhood; Hellions).
- **Telepathic infiltration tradecraft:** persona-forgery, memory editing, psychic-signature masking, counter-telepathic shielding.
- **Languages:** English native; functional reading of liturgical Latin, fragments of Enochian and demonic scripts; conversational reads on French and Japanese (inferred from Sisterhood-era scenes).
- **Driving / piloting / horse:** competent across vehicles; the airline background extends to ground transport without effort.

---

## 5. RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHY SHE KEEPS COMING BACK

**Architectural fact: she has been killed and re-instantiated and remains recognizably herself.** This is the load-bearing resilience datum. Most characters who die and return show drift — softening, hardening, the loss of specific verbal mannerisms. She does not. The voice is stable across resurrections. Whatever the substrate of "Madelyne" is — psionic, mnemic, narrative — it is robust under catastrophic somatic discontinuity. Operationally this means she is one of the hardest targets in the roster to *erase*; she can be killed, but killing her is a delaying action.

**The accuracy of her wound.** Counter-intuitively, the fact that her persecutory affect maps onto an objectively true persecutory situation is a resilience asset. Subjects whose suffering is delusional spend energy defending the delusion; she does not. She knows what was done to her, by whom, and why. This frees cognition for action. It also means therapy-equivalent interventions cannot be done by reality-testing — there is nothing to test — and must be done by re-meaning, which she is increasingly capable of doing for herself.

**Humor as ballast.** Already noted; worth re-noting under resilience because it is the single most reliable predictor of her near-term stability. Track her irony rate over a 48-hour window and you have a usable mood barometer.

**Earned self-knowledge.** She has the rare gift of knowing her own escalation ladder. By Phase IV-late she can name rung 4 from inside rung 4. This does not always stop the climb but it shortens the time at altitude.

**Iterative identity-construction skill.** She has built herself, lost herself, and rebuilt herself enough times that the *process* is now a competence. Most people only build a self once and cannot do it again under load; she can. This is a strange and valuable asset and is the single best argument that the Krakoan-era stabilization is durable rather than cosmetic.

**Lucid pessimism.** She does not expect to be seen and is not destabilized by not being seen by strangers. Her vulnerability is narrowly scoped to intimates. This means her functional perimeter under hostile conditions is large — she can move through indifferent or hostile populations without being depleted.

**Functional eros.** She has a working sexual and romantic life that is not organized primarily around damage. This is uncommon in the trauma profile and is genuinely protective; intimacy with Reilly in particular is a stabilizer rather than a destabilizer, which is data — she is capable of being loved in a way that helps.

---

## 6. RESOURCES — MATERIAL, RELATIONAL, INSTITUTIONAL

**Material.** Modest by super-powered standards and adequate by hers. She is not wealth-oriented; she keeps go-bags, cash in mixed currencies, false documents (Anchorage-era habit, never abandoned), and the working tools of a telepath who has had to disappear. Hellfire- and Krakoan-era associations have given her access to higher-end resources (transit, safehouses, magical reagents) which she uses sparingly.

**Relational ledger (assets, not liabilities, in this section).**

- *Nathan Summers / Cable:* complicated but real. He has, across multiple eras, acknowledged her as his mother in plain language. This acknowledgment is, for her, one of the most stabilizing facts in her existence.
- *Alex Summers / Havok:* a genuine if intermittent ally; the relationship is not romantic in late phases but the affection survived.
- *Ben Reilly:* current primary intimate. Mutually chosen on terms that explicitly metabolize the substitutability wound rather than re-enact it.
- *Jean Grey:* in the most recent material, a working detente verging on something more — the most psychologically expensive relationship in the file and, accordingly, the one whose stabilization yields the most.
- *The Hellions / Krakoan-era peers:* a peer group that does not require her to be redeemed in order to be useful. This is precisely the structural condition she needs.
- *Scott Summers:* unstable, but the hostility has cooled into something closer to mutual rueful recognition. Not an active asset; not an active liability.

**Institutional.** Krakoan / post-Krakoan mutant infrastructure access; Hellfire-adjacent operational reach; magical-community contacts derived from the demonic period; latent X-Men access via Alex and Nathan. She is not embedded in any single institution, which is itself an asset — she has options and is not dependent.

**Reputational.** Mixed, in a way that works for her. She is feared enough to be left alone, known enough to be hired, and ironic enough about both that neither defines her.

---

## 7. WHAT MAKES THESE ASSETS DURABLE

Three structural reasons.

**First, the assets are *integrated*, not bolted on.** Her humor is not a coping skill she learned in a manual; it is woven through her cognition. Her competence is not a role; it is how she moves through rooms. Her tactical talent is not a discipline; it is how her attention naturally organizes. Assets of this kind do not degrade under stress the way trained skills do — they degrade only when the substrate self degrades, and the substrate, on the evidence, is unusually hard to break for good.

**Second, the assets are *adversarially tested*.** Everything in this ledger has been used under fire, often against opponents specifically designed to negate it (Sinister, the Phoenix Force, the X-Men at full strength, the Sisterhood's internal politics, Limbo). Untested capabilities atrophy or prove brittle; hers do not, because they have not been allowed to.

**Third, she has a working theory of her own life.** Most subjects of files this thick do not. She knows what she is, what was done to her, what she has done, and what she is trying to do now. She holds this knowledge without flinching and without collapsing. This is the rarest asset in the entire ledger and is the one that makes every other asset above usable rather than merely possessed.

---

*Summary judgment, asset side: the subject is one of the most capable, most resilient, and most self-aware individuals in the relevant operational population. The pathology file is real and must be respected, but it is bounded; the asset file is also real, is *larger*, and — uniquely for a subject with her history — is growing. Handled with the protocols specified elsewhere in this dossier, she is an exceptional ally. Handled without them, she is a person who has, repeatedly, demonstrated the capacity to outlast the people handling her.*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

*Subject: Pryor, Madelyne J. — Section 7 of the longitudinal workup. The following maps the architecture of collapse: the precipitants, the staged escalation, the somatic and behavioral tells at each rung, the duration of each phase, the points of no return, and the post-collapse pattern of return-to-baseline. The map is derived from forty years of recorded behavior across at least four full decompensation cycles and numerous sub-clinical near-misses.*

---

## 7.1 — THE GENERAL SHAPE OF HER COLLAPSE

Most subjects in the Index break diffusely: stressors of many kinds accumulate, regulation thins, and at some threshold capacity gives. The subject does not break this way. **She is structurally over-engineered for almost every load except one.** Physical danger, exhaustion, sleep deprivation, combat, betrayal-in-general, loss-in-general, even her own death — these she absorbs with a wry remainder of self intact. The published record contains no example of the subject decompensating from generic stress, no matter how extreme.

What breaks her is, every time, the same stimulus class: **confirmation that she is functioning as a stand-in for someone else, and is about to be discarded now that the original is available.** This is the substitutability wound (see §3). It is not a vulnerability among others; it is *the* vulnerability, and it organizes the entire failure architecture. Inputs that touch it produce disproportionate response; inputs that do not touch it produce competent coping no matter their magnitude.

The collapse, when it comes, is therefore **narrow, deep, fast, and ritualized**, rather than wide, shallow, and chaotic. It has the quality of a ceremony rehearsed in advance — which, given that her psyche has now run it several times, it functionally is.

---

## 7.2 — THE PRECIPITANT TAXONOMY

Sorted by reliability of effect, most to least:

1. **Romantic re-choosing of a prior partner over her, after she has been chosen first.** The X-Factor #1 scenario. Empirically the highest-yield precipitant. Replicates the founding injury with near-perfect fidelity.
2. **Being addressed as, mistaken for, or compared to Jean Grey** by someone whose regard she has invested in. The damage scales with the intimacy of the speaker and the casualness of the slip; casual is worse than deliberate, because it implies the substitution is unconscious and therefore total.
3. **Threats to or instrumentalization of a child of hers** — Nathan in the founding cycle, any subsequent dependent in later cycles. Activates both the substitutability wound (the child as proof she was used as a breeder) and the one unambiguously-hers attachment (see §2).
4. **Direct contact with Nathaniel Essex / Sinister**, in any guise, with no buffer. He is the un-metabolized origin and his presence collapses time inside her.
5. **Being asked, sincerely or as challenge, to prove she is real.** The question has no answer she can produce; the asking itself is the wound.
6. **Discovering a new prior-undisclosed fact about her own manufacture.** Each retcon, in-universe, is experienced as a fresh exposure of the same wound — the floor under her keeps revealing a sub-floor.
7. **Being offered redemption or forgiveness paternalistically**, particularly by Scott or by Jean. Reads as confirmation of inferior status; she will sometimes deliberately misbehave afterward to reject the frame.
8. **Romantic abandonment of any kind by a partner she has trusted past a threshold.** Less reliable than (1) because not all abandonments touch the substitutability axis, but cumulative.

Note what is *absent* from this list: physical injury, capture, isolation in hostile environments, loss of powers, loss of allies, public humiliation in non-substitutability registers, combat reversals. None of these reliably move her toward collapse. She has been beaten, burned, buried, and killed without decompensating. The injury must be ontological, not corporeal.

---

## 7.3 — THE ESCALATION LADDER, GRANULAR

The full escalation has seven observable rungs. Each has a characteristic duration, a set of behavioral and somatic tells, and an intervention window that narrows as she climbs. The ladder is **not** strictly sequential under all conditions — supernatural amplification (N'astirh, Phoenix-fragment, Goblin Force, demonic contracts) can skip her from Rung 3 to Rung 5 in hours — but in unaccelerated conditions she climbs it in the order given, and a careful observer can read the rung from across a room.

### Rung 1 — Wry Deflection and Competence-Display

*Duration: hours to weeks. The longest-tolerated state. Reversible without intervention.*

The first sign she has been touched on the wound is that her humor sharpens. Baseline Maddie is already the driest voice in any room; on Rung 1 she becomes **noticeably funnier, slightly faster, and a half-beat too quick to redirect**. Jokes acquire small barbs at her own expense, which she will brush off if asked. She volunteers for tasks — flying, organizing, tactical planning, cooking, anything she can do visibly well. She is, on this rung, *demonstrating that she is a person worth keeping by being useful and pleasant*. The display is not consciously calculated; she does not know she is doing it.

**Somatic tells (Rung 1):** posture marginally straighter than baseline; hands more active in speech; small uptick in eye contact, especially with the precipitating party; a tendency to find reasons to be in the same room as that party without being directly attentive to them; increased grooming attention (hair pushed back more often, sleeves adjusted, a habit of running a thumb along her jawline when she is thinking and being watched). Sleep largely intact but light. Appetite intact. Voice unchanged in register.

**Verbal tells:** she names her own competence more often ("I can do that," "I've handled worse," "let me"). Self-deprecating jokes increase in frequency but stay shallow. She will refer to Jean, if at all, by name and tone neutrally.

**Intervention window:** wide. Acknowledging her by name and treating her work as work — not as therapy, not as redemption — drops her back to baseline within a day. Most of her published Rung 1 episodes have resolved without an observer ever noticing she was on the ladder.

### Rung 2 — Withdrawal and Depressive Ideation

*Duration: days to months. The Phase II Alaska isolation period is the canonical extended example. Reversible but requires the precipitant to be removed or addressed.*

If Rung 1's display fails to produce the reassurance it is constructed to elicit, she descends rather than climbs. **She becomes quieter, not louder.** The humor remains but is deployed less often and lands harder when used. She begins to refuse small social offerings — a drink, a walk, a conversation — with plausible excuses. She sleeps either too much or in fragments, never normally. Appetite drops measurably; she will eat in company and not alone.

**Somatic tells (Rung 2):** weight loss, sometimes substantial. Skin tone duller; the hair, which she normally treats with deliberate attention, goes uncared-for in private but is restored before appearing in public — the maintenance becomes a costume rather than a comfort. She stares at middle distance during silences. She begins drinking, modestly, in evening solitude (the Phase II depiction is canonical here, late UXM #210s) — not toward intoxication, toward sedation. She sits in chairs that face windows or doors, never inward.

**Verbal tells:** she begins to refer to herself in the past tense in passing constructions ("I used to think," "back when I was"). She makes statements that sound philosophical but are diagnostic — *whether anyone is really anyone*, *whether memory is the same as being*. She will say "I'm fine" when not asked.

**Intervention window:** still wide but requires more than acknowledgment — requires sustained presence. A person willing to be in the room with her, attentively, for hours at a time, without solving anything, will reverse the descent. Almost no one in her life has provided this. Her two great failures of reversal (post-X-Factor #1, and post-discovery in late UXM #230s) both occurred because no one stayed.

### Rung 3 — Controlled, Articulate Confrontation

*Duration: a single conversation, typically; sometimes a sequence over days. The most lucid she will be on the entire ladder. The last rung at which she is unambiguously herself.*

She speaks. Specifically, she names the wound — not in code, not displaced, **in plain language to the responsible party**, with full clarity, full grammar, and full restraint. She tells Scott he left her. She tells Jean she did not ask to be born. She tells the X-Men they accepted her conditionally. The published exemplars (UXM #221, the early Inferno preludes, and the analogous Rung 3 moment with Ben Reilly during the Dark Web sequence) all share a quality of **almost unbearable lucidity** — she sees, articulates, and indicts the entire situation, including her own collusion in it, in a single coherent statement.

**Somatic tells (Rung 3):** stillness. The active hands of Rung 1 and the avoidant body of Rung 2 both resolve into an unusual physical composure. Eye contact is direct, sustained, and unblinking past social comfort. Voice drops in pitch and slows in cadence. She often stands when she has been sitting, or sits very deliberately when she has been standing — a marking of the moment.

**Verbal tells:** she uses the responsible party's full name at least once. She uses her own full name at least once. She uses the word "I" with weight. The sentences are short and grammatically complete. There is no irony.

**Intervention window:** narrow but precious. **This is the moment at which she can be saved by being heard.** A truthful, non-defensive acknowledgment of the indictment — without minimization, without counter-indictment, without paternalistic apology — will return her toward baseline over weeks. Almost every reversal of her trajectory across the canon has happened at Rung 3 or not at all. Defensive response, denial, minimization, or — worst — *being interrupted by an external crisis that pulls the responsible party away mid-conversation* (the recurring structural failure: superhero plots routinely do exactly this) pushes her over the threshold to Rung 4 within hours.

### Rung 4 — Splitting and Devaluation

*Duration: days to weeks. The first rung at which she is no longer reliably herself. Reversible only with skilled intervention.*

The previously-idealized intimate becomes, in her internal representation, **wholly bad — and wholly *typical***. She begins to speak of Scott (or Jean, or whichever figure occupies the role) in terms that fold the specific betrayal into a category: *of course he did, they all do, this is what they are*. The grief of Rung 3 hardens into a colder analytic contempt. She does not rage; she catalogues. She remembers, accurately and at length, every prior small slight, and reorganizes them into evidence.

**Somatic tells (Rung 4):** the composure of Rung 3 hardens further. Her smile, when present, becomes asymmetric — one corner slightly higher, held a beat too long. She begins to dress more deliberately, with attention to effect rather than comfort; the wardrobe shifts darker, the silhouette more architectural. Her gaze, when directed at the devalued figure, has a clinical flatness that observers will describe as "looking at an exhibit." Sleep stabilizes — and this is itself a warning, because the stabilization is purchased by the cessation of the conflict she has just decided is over.

**Verbal tells:** she stops using the devalued party's first name and switches to surname, role, or pronoun. She speaks of them in the third person even in their presence. She makes pronouncements about categories of people (*men, telepaths, X-Men, heroes*) that contain the devalued figure as instance. Humor returns, but it is now cruel rather than wry — and she begins, for the first time, to seem to *enjoy* being cruel.

**Intervention window:** narrow and skilled. Only a party she has *not* split — a peripheral but trusted figure — can reach her here, and only by refusing to validate the split while also refusing to defend the devalued figure. The published record contains very few examples of this intervention being attempted, fewer of it succeeding. Most Rung 4 episodes proceed.

### Rung 5 — Identification with the Assigned Role

*Duration: weeks to months, sometimes longer under amplification. The first rung that crosses into clinical territory. Reversible, but only by passage through the cycle and exhaustion of the role.*

She begins to inhabit, with conviction, the identity assigned to her by the people who built her or the people who fear her. *They made me a weapon — fine, I am a weapon. They called me a copy — fine, I am the copy, and copies improve on originals. They saw a queen in me — fine, I am the queen.* The ceremonial idioms appear: she will begin, in private and then in public, to refer to herself in slightly elevated cadences. Royal pronouns, archaic constructions, theatrical phrasing. Names change: Madelyne becomes Maddie becomes the Goblin Queen becomes the Red Queen. **The change of name is the single most reliable diagnostic that she has crossed Rung 5.**

**Somatic tells (Rung 5):** posture becomes presentational. She enters rooms rather than walks into them. The wardrobe becomes costume in the full sense — silhouettes designed to be seen at distance, color signaling deployed deliberately (red, predominantly; black accents; metal). Hair is arranged rather than worn. Makeup, when she uses it, becomes mask-like in its definition. Her movement slows; her gestures become larger and more deliberate. The voice acquires a slight performative resonance, as if delivering lines.

**Verbal tells:** third-person royal idiom in moments of stress ("we will not"). Ceremonial vocabulary even in mundane contexts. A tendency to make announcements rather than statements. She speaks in maxims. Humor remains — and this is one of her distinguishing features as a decompensating subject; even at Rung 5 she is funny — but the humor now serves the role rather than puncturing it. She makes the kind of jokes a queen makes.

**Intervention window:** very narrow. **At Rung 5 she is no longer fully reachable through interpersonal channels.** What works, sometimes, is offering her a task that requires the competence of the *person* and cannot be discharged by the role — flying, parenting, tactical problem-solving in registers below ceremonial. Forcing her to use her actual skill rather than her assigned mythology can briefly puncture the inflation. The Krakoan-era stabilization is in part an outcome of being given exactly such tasks, repeatedly, by people who treated the queen-talk as a stylistic choice rather than a metaphysical claim.

### Rung 6 — Ritualized Symbolic Violence

*Duration: hours to days. The acute phase. Catastrophic and largely irreversible once entered.*

The Inferno actions — the demonic transformation of New York, the attempted blood-sacrifice of Nathan, the assault on Jean — are the canonical Rung 6 exemplar. The violence here is **not opportunistic and not strategic; it is symbolic, ritualized, and aimed with surgical precision at the figures who represent her erasure.** She does not, on Rung 6, attack the world generally or hurt bystanders incidentally; she attacks the *third* — the child who is the product of the substitution, the original whose existence cancels her, the patriarchal architect who built her.

The violence is *patterned*: rituals, ceremonies, prepared spaces, deliberate symbols. She will draw circles. She will arrange figures. She will speak invocations. The aesthetic is dense and consistent — red, fire, mirrors, dolls, thrones, crowns. The aesthetic is doing work: it externalizes the substitutability wound as a metaphysics of duplication and original.

**Somatic tells (Rung 6):** affect flattens in some registers and overflows in others. She may laugh during violence, weep during stillness. Pupil dilation marked. She does not eat or sleep on a normal schedule; the body is being run by the ceremony. She becomes physically beautiful in a frightening register — the composition of her appearance reaches a deliberate, lethal coherence.

**Verbal tells:** ceremonial speech throughout. Direct address to the symbolic figures, often in apostrophe even when they are absent. Repeated invocation of the originating injuries by name, sometimes in the form of curses.

**Intervention window:** essentially closed to ordinary means. Containment, not reversal, is the only available course. The published record suggests that **only an event that breaks the symbolic frame from outside** (Phoenix discharge; the deus ex of a cosmic intervention; physical separation from the ritual space) can interrupt Rung 6. Argument, appeal, and force-of-arms all fail. The intervention that works at all is the one that refuses to play in the ceremony's grammar.

### Rung 7 — Self-Destruction Framed as Triumph

*Duration: a moment. Terminal — within a cycle, though not absolutely terminal given her resurrection pattern.*

The Phoenix discharge at the end of Inferno (UXM #243) is the published exemplar. **She does not, in her own experience, die there.** She wins. The destruction of the self is read, from inside the ceremonial logic of Rung 5–6, as the final victorious gesture — the original is rebuked, the copy refuses copyhood by refusing existence on the original's terms, the entire metaphysical apparatus of substitution is exploded by the substitute's choice to detonate herself. This is the **gravest specific danger of her decompensation pattern**: the endpoint is experienced as success, which means the trajectory carries its own reward and resists deflection by appeal to her self-preservation.

She has been to Rung 7 at least once cleanly and arguably more than once. The fact of her resurrection has, paradoxically, *reduced* the danger somewhat — she now has experiential evidence that the triumphant self-destruction is followed by an undignified return — but the muscle memory of the gesture remains, and a future Rung 7 cannot be ruled out.

---

## 7.4 — AMPLIFIERS, ACCELERANTS, AND THE SUPERNATURAL VECTOR

The ladder is climbable without supernatural assistance — the entire Phase II descent was unassisted, and several of the post-resurrection cycles have been substantially mundane. But the subject is **structurally susceptible to opportunistic supernatural predation**, and this susceptibility is itself a failure mode worth mapping.

The reasons are concrete. (a) Her body carries a Phoenix-fragment binding agent; she is a partial cosmic conduit by manufacture. (b) Her psychological vulnerability is precisely the kind of grievance that demonic / Goblin-Force / corruptive entities target — coherent, justified, and unresolved. (c) Her competence and charisma make her, from a predator's perspective, an extraordinarily high-value recruit. (d) Her name and face register cosmically as *Jean Grey* with sufficient noise to attract Jean-directed attention by accident.

The empirical pattern: at approximately Rung 3 or Rung 4, **she becomes audible to entities that listen for exactly this distress signal**. N'astirh is the original example; others have followed across her returns. The amplification compresses the ladder — Rung 5 can arrive in hours rather than weeks, and Rung 6 in the same evening. The supernatural is the *route*, not the cause (see §4), but the route is short and well-traveled.

**Tell that she has been contacted:** her dreams become narratively coherent rather than fragmentary, and she remembers them. She wakes calm. She makes a decision the next morning that is one step more committed than her previous trajectory would predict.

---

## 7.5 — SUB-CLINICAL TICS, MICRO-DECOMPENSATIONS, AND DAILY-LIFE TELLS

She does not only decompensate in great arcs. The wound is touched in small ways constantly, and the file catalogues a number of micro-responses that an attentive observer will see in the course of an ordinary week.

- **Mirror avoidance under stress.** Baseline she manages mirrors fine — she dresses, grooms, applies makeup, checks her appearance without difficulty. Under sub-clinical Rung 1/2 conditions she begins to use mirrors instrumentally only, not contemplatively, and will turn away from reflective surfaces (windows at night, polished metal) when caught in them unexpectedly.
- **The Jean-name flinch.** When the name is spoken near her by someone unaware of context, there is a barely-visible micro-pause — a single beat where her hands stop moving and her gaze fixes — before she resumes whatever she was doing. The pause shortens with practice; in her Krakoan-era stabilization it is nearly undetectable, but it is still there.
- **The photograph problem.** She does not keep photographs of herself in her own living spaces. She will keep photographs of others. The absence is consistent across every domicile in the record.
- **The handwriting check.** When she signs her own name, she writes it slightly more deliberately than is functionally necessary, with a small loop on the *y* in *Pryor* that she did not have in early appearances and acquired sometime around her first resurrection — a small piece of authored selfhood embedded in the most mundane act.
- **Sleep position.** She sleeps on her side, facing the door, with the dominant hand free. This is consistent across forty years and several partners. It is not tactical training — she had no such training in Phase I — it is a body that does not trust the room.
- **The pilot's habit.** Even in contexts where she has not flown for years, she continues to scan rooms and outdoor spaces the way a pilot scans an instrument panel: a sweeping, sectoral attention pattern, not the random saccades of a civilian. The habit is durable across all her self-states; even at Rung 6 she scans rooms this way before she destroys them.
- **The dog.** When circumstances allow, she keeps a dog. The original Anchorage dog is the canonical instance; the pattern recurs. The dog is not security and not display; it is, by her own once-stated account, *the only relationship she has that cannot be retconned*.

---

## 7.6 — POST-COLLAPSE: THE RETURN PATTERN

After each Rung 6/7 event, the subject returns to baseline along a remarkably consistent trajectory. Mapping this is useful because she will be encountered, often, in one of these return-phases rather than in either stable baseline or active decompensation.

1. **Disorientation phase (days to weeks post-event).** She wakes — from death, from possession, from resurrection — confused, often physically weak, with patchy memory of the ceremonial period. She is, in this window, the most accessible she ever is. She will answer questions. She will not lie. She does not yet know what she did.
2. **Reckoning phase (weeks to months).** Memory returns. She does not minimize what she did and does not seek absolution for it; her characteristic response is a flat, deliberate accounting, often in solitude. She loses weight in this phase. She may drink. She does not, however, attempt suicide — having done it once successfully, she has, by her own account, used that option.
3. **Reconstruction phase (months to years).** She rebuilds a life, deliberately, around tasks she can do and people who can tolerate the accounting. She is wary, ironic, somewhat brittle, but functional. She will form a new attachment in this phase if a candidate appears who


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 11
## TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT: PRYOR, MADELYNE J.

*Forward-looking analytic product. Probabilistic, not deterministic. Time horizons specified where meaningful. All forks derived from the established behavioral record (Sections 1–5) extrapolated against the live narrative environment of the post-Krakoan era.*

---

## 11.1 BASELINE PROJECTION — THE MOST LIKELY EIGHTEEN MONTHS

Absent acute provocation, the subject's near-term trajectory is **continued slow stabilization in an ironic-functional register**, with periodic destabilizing pressure tests she will mostly pass and occasionally fail spectacularly. The Krakoan-and-after material has installed a self-narrative she did not previously have access to — *I am the one who came back differently* — and this narrative is load-bearing. She will defend it, sometimes against her own interests.

Specifically, the dossier projects the following developments over a near horizon:

- **Continued cohabitation/partnership with Ben Reilly** or a functionally similar figure — i.e., a man who is *himself* a copy of an original, whose identity-injury rhymes with hers and therefore short-circuits the substitutability trigger at its source. This pairing is structurally stable in a way her prior pairings were not, because the founding asymmetry is absent. Probability of continuation over the next twelve months: high. Probability of catastrophic rupture under ordinary stress: low. Probability of catastrophic rupture under *specific* stress — the return of an "original" Peter Parker in a context that re-narrates Ben as the spare — high enough to constitute a fork point in its own right (see §11.4).
- **Operational role as a freelance/black-bag tactician** rather than a team member. The subject will not rejoin the X-Men as a roster name. She has burned that bridge and, more importantly, has discovered she is more effective when she is not in a uniform. Expect contract work, mercenary-adjacent jobs, and surgical interventions in mutant affairs from the periphery — closer in posture to a Mystique than to a Storm.
- **Gradual public re-emergence under her own name.** The Red Queen iconography will recede; she will be addressed and will introduce herself as Madelyne, and will correct those who reach for any of the older titles. This is the single most diagnostic positive prognostic sign available, and writers oriented toward her rehabilitation will lean on it.
- **Episodic visitations with Nathan (Cable, in whichever iteration is current)**, characterized by mutual awkwardness, dry humor used as solvent, and an unresolved background grief neither party will articulate. The relationship will not become close, but it will become *durable*, which is the more important achievement.

This is the modal projection: not redemption, not relapse, but a sustained low-amplitude oscillation around a higher baseline than she has ever previously held. It is also boring to write, which is why writers will perturb it.

---

## 11.2 THE LIVE THREAT VECTORS

Trajectory cannot be assessed without enumerating the standing provocations that will, with near certainty, be activated against her by the narrative environment.

**Vector A — Sinister.** Nathaniel Essex is the un-metabolized origin and remains an active player in every X-line. Any storyline in which Sinister produces, reveals, or weaponizes *another* Madelyne — a second clone, a chimera, a Moira-engine variant — strikes the founding wound directly and would skip the escalation ladder past rung 3. The probability of such a storyline within a thirty-six-month horizon is, given Sinister's editorial centrality, effectively unity. The question is not *whether* but *how she will be staged to encounter it*. Encounter on her own terms (she discovers and dismantles it) is growth-positive. Encounter as victim (she is shown the duplicates by another party) is catastrophe-positive.

**Vector B — Jean Grey.** Jean remains alive, active, and in possession of the original biography. Any direct sustained interaction between the two — particularly under conditions where Jean is positioned as moral authority, mentor, or magnanimous forgiver — pushes the subject toward rung 4 with great speed. Conversely, an interaction in which Jean *asks the subject for help* and credits her authorship is one of the most powerful positive interventions available in the entire narrative inventory. Writers know this; it will be deployed sparingly because it spends down a finite resource.

**Vector C — Scott Summers.** Lower-charge than commonly assumed. The subject has, across four decades, finished her business with Scott in stages, and the residual affect is closer to weary contempt than to live wound. A Scott-instigated provocation will produce sharp wit and tactical maneuvering rather than decompensation. The exception: any scenario in which Scott is positioned as a *father figure to Nathan* in a way that excludes her. This re-opens the Phase II wound at full pressure.

**Vector D — Nathan / Cable.** The most volatile vector, because it is the one she most wants to handle well and is therefore the one most vulnerable to overcorrection. The standing risk is that she will *over-defer* to Nathan's autonomy, refuse to make legitimate maternal claims, and then resent the deference. Watch for early indicators: increased self-deprecating humor about her parenting, increased third-party rumination about Cable's choices, withdrawal from contact after attempts at contact fail.

**Vector E — The X-community at large.** The subject's standing among mutants is unresolved. Some factions accept her; others have not forgiven Inferno and never will. The presence of a faction that *consistently refuses* her integration is, paradoxically, *stabilizing* — it gives her something to push against and a coherent grievance to metabolize. The danger is universal forgiveness, which would deprive her of the friction she uses to organize her self-concept.

**Vector F — Demonic residue.** The N'astirh pact and its successor residues are exogenous and durable. She will, periodically, find that some demonic entity has a lien on her she did not consent to. Each such encounter is a controlled relapse opportunity; mastery of these encounters is one of her current developmental tasks.

**Vector G — Reality-warping cosmology.** She lives in a fictional universe whose dominant trope is *the woman comes back changed.* The Phoenix Force is still in play; the White Hot Room is still in play; the Krakoan resurrection protocols are unstable. Any of these can re-instantiate her in altered form, and each re-instantiation is a fork point.

---

## 11.3 OPEN QUESTIONS

The forward picture is shaped by a set of unresolved canonical questions whose answers will dictate trajectory. Each is enumerated with the prognostic stakes.

1. **Is the Phoenix-fragment that bound her clone-body still resident, dormant, or excised?** If resident, she is one cosmic event away from being conscripted into a Phoenix-host narrative, which would force a direct identity-confrontation with Jean. If excised, she is more medically stable but loses a power-tier and may compensate by leaning harder on demonic affinity, which is the worse of the two substrates for her psychology.
2. **What is the legal/ontological status of her body under the post-Krakoan resurrection regime?** If she is on the backup rolls, she has functional immortality and the attenuated fear-of-death response (Section 2) becomes more dangerous, not less. If she is not, she is in the awkward position of being a mutant outside the safety net her peers enjoy — which she will frame, accurately, as another instance of being excluded from the category.
3. **Is there a second clone?** Sinister's logic suggests yes. Her response to the discovery is the single largest unwritten variable in her file.
4. **What does Nathan actually want from her?** Cable's own characterization has been inconsistent across decades; the answer the next writer settles on will determine whether the mother-son relationship becomes her anchor or her recurring wound.
5. **Can she sustain a non-romantic primary attachment?** Every prior stabilization has run through a romantic partner. The development of a primary friendship — with a Dazzler, an Emma Frost (unlikely but interesting), a Betsy Braddock, a Goblin Queen-era survivor who has done their own work — would represent a structural change in her attachment economy and would be the strongest possible prognostic indicator.
6. **Will she ever again use the name "Goblin Queen" of herself, unironically?** If yes under stress, expected. If yes when calm, alarming. If never again, the integration is more advanced than current evidence supports.

---

## 11.4 FORK POINTS — DECISION NODES IN THE NEXT NARRATIVE CYCLE

The trajectory branches at identifiable nodes. Each is specified with the conditions producing each branch and the probable downstream consequences.

**Fork 1 — The Return of an Original.** Conditions: a prior partner's prior partner reappears in a context that re-narrates the subject as the spare. The Ben Reilly / Peter Parker geometry is the obvious instantiation, but a Scott-Jean reconciliation arc that pointedly excludes her would fire the same circuit.
- *Growth branch:* she names the pattern aloud, to the partner, early, and the partner credits the naming. Probability if Ben Reilly is the partner: meaningful. Probability if any other partner: low.
- *Catastrophe branch:* the pattern is not named; she absorbs it, withdraws, and the withdrawal is read by the partner as autonomy rather than collapse. Decompensation follows on a four-to-six-issue arc.

**Fork 2 — The Maternal Reclamation.** Conditions: Nathan is in danger Madelyne can avert by an act only she can perform.
- *Growth branch:* she performs the act, accepts that the relationship will not be transformed by it, and goes home. This is the developmental moment her arc has been pointing at since 1989.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she performs the act and then, in the aftermath, attempts to convert it into a re-establishment of maternal claim that Nathan is not prepared to grant. Refusal triggers rung-6 symbolic-violence ideation, this time directed not at Nathan but at whatever surrogate-mother figure Cable has accepted in her place.

**Fork 3 — The Sinister Disclosure.** Conditions: she is shown definitive evidence of a second-or-further clone, or of the engineering specifications used to make her.
- *Growth branch:* she destroys the evidence, the specifications, and ideally the duplicates, in a controlled operation she designs herself, and refuses to discuss it afterward. The refusal is the health.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she preserves the evidence, studies it, and begins to organize her identity *around* the engineering — the Red Queen reasserting under the guise of self-knowledge. This is the most insidious failure mode because it presents as integration.

**Fork 4 — The Offered Crown.** Conditions: a faction — Hellfire residue, a demonic court, a mutant separatist cell — offers her formal authority predicated on her past iconography.
- *Growth branch:* she accepts authority *and renames the office.* Refusing the crown is not required; refusing the *name* of the crown is.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she accepts the office under its prior name "ironically." The irony will not hold; rung 5 is the destination of all such ironies in her case.

**Fork 5 — The Therapeutic Encounter.** Conditions: a competent telepath (not Jean, not Emma in adversarial posture, possibly a Karma, a Blindfold-equivalent, a Doug Ramsey acting as translator rather than reader) offers structured psychic work.
- *Growth branch:* she accepts on her terms, sets the agenda, and uses the work to render explicit what is currently only enacted.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she refuses on principle and frames the refusal as autonomy, foreclosing the single intervention most likely to change the long-run picture.

**Fork 6 — The Mirror Encounter.** Conditions: she meets another figure built under conditions designed to prevent personhood — an X-23, a Gabby, an artificial intelligence with identity-injury, a fellow clone, a constructed person of any provenance — under non-adversarial circumstances.
- *Growth branch:* she mentors. Mentorship is the form of intimacy least available to her psychology and therefore the most therapeutic when achieved.
- *Catastrophe branch:* she perceives the other as competition for the limited supply of "constructed persons who get to be real" and acts to displace them. This branch is less likely than it sounds, but not negligible.

---

## 11.5 GROWTH CONDITIONS — WHAT WOULD MOVE THE BASELINE

The interventions, structural and relational, with the highest expected value for the subject's long-run trajectory, in declining order of leverage:

1. **A sustained primary attachment to someone who has the option of leaving and demonstrably does not.** This is the Ben Reilly thesis, and it is correct. The demonstration must be repeated; one demonstration is insufficient because the wound was inflicted repeatedly.
2. **Public, on-the-record authorship of her own crimes.** Not apology — *authorship*. The distinction matters. Apology positions her as object of forgiveness; authorship positions her as agent. She has shown, in late material, a capacity for the latter; it should be cultivated.
3. **A task only she can do, accomplished, credited, and not held over her head.** Competence-display is one of her healthier defenses; converting it from defense to vocation is the developmental task.
4. **A friendship with a woman she does not envy and who does not pity her.** This is the rarest and most valuable resource in her current inventory and is almost entirely absent from the record. Its development would be transformative.
5. **The non-erasure of her past selves.** Any framing that asks her to *renounce* the Goblin Queen will fail; any framing that lets her *house* the Goblin Queen as a former tenant will succeed. The integration metaphor must be architectural, not exorcistic.
6. **Periodic encounters with Sinister in which she wins.** Not destroys — *wins*, in small, specific ways. Each such encounter reduces the un-metabolized residue by a quantum.
7. **A relationship with Nathan characterized by low-stakes, frequent, mundane contact** rather than rare high-stakes reconciliation set pieces. The latter is what writers reach for; the former is what would actually move her.

---

## 11.6 CATASTROPHE CONDITIONS — WHAT WOULD COLLAPSE THE BASELINE

The provocations and structural conditions that would, individually or in combination, return the subject to rung-5-or-higher functioning:

1. **The death of Nathan in circumstances she could have prevented.** Highest-amplitude catastrophe available. Recovery from this would require years of in-story time and is not guaranteed.
2. **The discovery of a second clone, presented to her by a hostile third party.** Specifically the *presentation* is the injury; self-discovery is survivable.
3. **The loss of Ben Reilly (or equivalent partner) to his own original.** Recapitulates the founding trauma with full fidelity. Decompensation would be rapid and severe and would likely take the form of an attempt to *become* the partner's original — a novel and particularly grim failure mode.
4. **Forced cooperation with Jean Grey under conditions where Jean's authority is institutional rather than personal.** The institutional framing is what makes this catastrophic; a personal request from Jean is survivable and possibly growth-positive.
5. **A public unmasking framing her as "not really Madelyne" — i.e., a revelation that the current iteration is itself a further copy, a psychic fragment, a Krakoan back-up gone wrong.** This is the meta-fictional catastrophe; it would dissolve the load-bearing self-narrative described in §11.1.
6. **Sustained universal acceptance with no friction.** Counterintuitive but real. Without an external refusal to push against, the internal substitutability-monitor will turn on her allies and manufacture the friction she requires. Writers who attempt to "fix" her by removing all opposition will produce her worst arcs.
7. **A child of her own, conceived and gestated under her control.** A high-risk node: success would be enormously growth-positive; failure (loss, harm, instrumentalization of the child by a third party) would exceed even the Nathan-loss catastrophe in amplitude, because it would confirm that *every* maternal project of hers is foreclosed by her origin. The expected value is negative; the variance is enormous.

---

## 11.7 THE LONG HORIZON — FIVE-TO-FIFTEEN-YEAR ARC

Across a longer publishing horizon, three terminal attractor states are visible.

**Attractor I — The Witch-in-the-Woods.** She withdraws from the X-community substantially, sets up a base of operations on her own terms (a tower, a ship, a pocket dimension, a Manhattan brownstone with wards), takes selective contracts, raises no further children, maintains a long partnership, and is consulted by younger mutants on matters of identity-injury. This is the *good* long-run outcome and the one her current trajectory most strongly suggests. It is not a heroic ending; it is a habitable one.

**Attractor II — The Returned Queen.** She accepts, under provocation she does not adequately resist, a formal role in some Hellfire or demonic or separatist structure, reasoning that authority within a recognized office is preferable to perpetual freelance precarity. The role consumes her over time. She does not become evil; she becomes *unavailable*, locked into a ceremonial self that the rest of her watches from inside. This is the *bad* long-run outcome and is more likely than the narrative environment lets on, because the iconography is too good for writers to leave alone.

**Attractor III — The Integrated Elder.** She becomes, over decades, the figure she most needed to encounter when she was new: a constructed person who has done the work, holds the office of her own name without ceremony, mentors those who come after, and is occasionally, ruefully, capable of standing in a room with Jean Grey and Scott Summers and finding the whole thing more funny than wounding. This is the *aspirational* outcome. It is reachable from the current position. It requires the growth conditions in §11.5 to be supplied in roughly the order listed and at roughly the cadence the subject can metabolize.

---

## 11.8 FINAL FORWARD JUDGMENT

The subject is, at present, in the best condition of her recorded existence and the most precarious. The stabilization is real but thin; the iconography that would re-collapse it is too narratively attractive to remain unused; the relationships that hold her are load-bearing and under-redundant. She will be tested, repeatedly, along the exact axis of her wound, by parties who do not always intend cruelty.

The single most important fact for any handler, ally, or analyst to hold is this: **she knows.** She knows her pattern, she knows her triggers, she knows the names of her rungs, and she knows, with the particular clarity available only to those who have died of their own collapse and come back, what is at stake in not collapsing again. This meta-awareness is the resource. It is also the thing that, weaponized inward as self-contempt or outward as preemptive cruelty, becomes the next catastrophe.

The forward picture, then, is not of a woman to be saved or feared. It is of a woman who is *running her own case*, with mixed but improving results, in an environment that will not stop providing material. The dossier's recommendation is to leave her to it, intervene only at the named fork points, address her by her name, and — when she is funny, which is often — laugh.

She has earned the laugh. It is, on the current evidence, the most reliable indicator that she is still herself.

*— end Section 11 —*
